  `family.Out', and `family.ValidOut' are exactly the package's own
  `param', `inst', `out', and `validOut'. The maximum in `MSDOpt' is over
  distinct pairs only; the diagonal is not part of the search space.

  If the implementation packages these names into a `ConcreteProblemFamily',
  that family must be a projection of the data package audited at this label and
  the listed equations must unfold from the package. Merely providing abstract
  declarations named `MSDParam', `MSDInst', `MSDOut' and `MSDValidOut', then
  storing them in a family record without the score/opt equations above, is
  rejected. The distinct-pair output type and the maximum-cosine validity
  relation are the content of the node. A Lean declaration whose body or main
  proof term is `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', a wrapper around it, an
  opaque family tag, `Unit', or a proposition ending in `True' does not satisfy
  this definition.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[$\gamma$-MSD, Definition 2.11]
  \label{def:gamma-msd}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:problem-family, def:msd}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and approximation factor $\gamma\ge 1$, an
  instance of $\gamma\text{-}\MSD_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple of nonzero vectors
  $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a pair
  $i^{*}, j^{*}$ with $i^{*}\ne j^{*}$ such that
  \[
    \frac{1}{\gamma}\cdot
    \max_{\substack{1 \le i,j \le n\\i\ne j}} \cossim{v_i}{v_j}
    \le \cossim{v_{i^{*}}}{v_{j^{*}}}
    \le
    \max_{\substack{1 \le i,j \le n\\i\ne j}} \cossim{v_i}{v_j}.
  \]
  The premise $\gamma\ge1$ and the two displayed inequalities are part of the
  formal output relation. A formalization must encode the approximation factor,
  the maximum over distinct pairs, and the returned pair; it cannot replace the
  problem by an uninterpreted family tag.

  The audited declaration is a self-contained data package `def_gamma_msd', not
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder' and not a wrapper around the exact MSD
  family. It must expose a concrete family with parameter $(n,\ell,\gamma)$ and
  the following equations:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{GammaMSDParam}
      &= \{(n,\ell,\gamma): n,\ell\in\N,\ \gamma\in\R,\
          n\ge2,\ \ell\ge1\},\\
    \operatorname{GammaMSDInst}(n,\ell,\gamma)
      &= \operatorname{MSDInst}(n,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{GammaMSDOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V)
      &= \{(i,j): i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\},\\
    \operatorname{GammaMSDScore}(V,i,j)
      &= \cossim{v_i}{v_j},\\
    \operatorname{GammaMSDOpt}(V)
      &= M_V=\max_{i\ne j}\cossim{v_i}{v_j},\\
    \operatorname{GammaMSDValidOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V,(i,j))
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      \gamma\ge1\ \wedge\ i\ne j\ \wedge\
      \gamma^{-1}M_V\le\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\ \wedge\
      \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le M_V .
  \end{array}
  \]
  In field form, `def_gamma_msd' contains at least
  `param', `inst', `out', `score', `opt', `validOut', and
  `family : ConcreteProblemFamily', plus transparent equations identifying all
  of these projections with the displayed `GammaMSD...' objects and with the
  search fields of `family'. The `validOut' field must mention the parameter
  $\gamma$ directly and must include both inequalities
  $\gamma^{-1}M_V\le\cossim{v_i}{v_j}$ and
  $\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le M_V$. The theorem/projection
  `GammaMSDValidOut_iff' must be available from the audited declaration itself;
  it may not be supplied only by an unrelated external identifier.

  The factor $\gamma$ is a parameter of the family, not metadata outside the
  problem. A declaration that uses abstract components or proves only exact
  maximality does not satisfy this node; the two approximation inequalities
  above must be the visible `ValidOut' relation. A declaration whose audited
  body is `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', a delegated placeholder-style
  family wrapper, an exact-MSD relation with $\gamma$ ignored, `Unit', or a
  proof ending in `True' is rejected.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[MSD decision version, $\MSD_{n,\ell,t}$, Definition 2.12]
  \label{def:msd-dec}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:problem-family, def:msd}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and threshold $t\in[0,1]$, an instance of
  $\MSD_{n,\ell,t}$ is an $n$-tuple of nonzero vectors
  $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. It is a yes instance iff there exist
  $1\le i,j\le n$ with $i\ne j$ and $\cossim{v_i}{v_j} \ge t$. Thus the
  yes-predicate is exactly
  \[
    \exists\, i\ne j,\quad \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\ge t.
  \]
  The threshold $t$ and the nonzero-binary input promise are part of the
  definition. This node is a concrete Boolean relation, not a placeholder tag.

  The declaration audited here is a self-contained data package `def_msd_dec',
  not `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', not an opaque `MSDThreshold' tag,
  and not a family wrapper whose threshold predicates live only in external
  identifiers. It must expose the concrete decision family
  $\operatorname{MSDThreshold}$ with parameter $(n,\ell,t)$:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{MSDDecParam}
      &= \{(n,\ell,t): n,\ell\in\N,\ t\in\R,\ n\ge2,\ \ell\ge1\},\\
    \operatorname{MSDDecInst}(n,\ell,t)
      &= \operatorname{MSDInst}(n,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{MSDDecYes}(n,\ell,t,V)
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \exists i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\ \wedge\
        \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\ge t,\\
    \operatorname{MSDDecNo}(n,\ell,t,V)
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \forall i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\Rightarrow
        \cossim{v_i}{v_j}<t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  In field form, `def_msd_dec' contains at least
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{param} &: \mathrm{Type},\\
    \operatorname{inst} &: \operatorname{param}\to\mathrm{Type},\\
    \operatorname{yes} &: \prod_p \operatorname{inst}(p)\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    \operatorname{no} &: \prod_p \operatorname{inst}(p)\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    \operatorname{family} &: \operatorname{ConcreteProblemFamily},
  \end{array}
  \]
  plus transparent projection equations identifying `param', `inst', `yes' and
  `no' with the displayed `MSDDecParam', `MSDDecInst', `MSDDecYes' and
  `MSDDecNo', and identifying `family.Param', `family.Inst', `family.Yes' and
  `family.No' with those same fields. The yes and no predicates themselves must
  contain the threshold range condition $0\le t\le1$. In particular,
  `MSDDecYes_iff' and `MSDDecNo_iff' must be recoverable by projecting from the
  declaration audited at this label.

  `MSDDecYes' and `MSDDecNo' may be helper names only if their definitions are
  transparent at this label and reduce to the displayed predicates. A family
  record containing opaque predicates with those names, or a trivial output
  relation, does not formalize Definition~2.12. A Lean declaration whose body is
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', a placeholder-style family wrapper,
  `Unit', or a proposition ending in `True' is rejected even if external helper
  declarations elsewhere state the right cosine-threshold predicates.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Least Similar Document, $\LSD_{n,\ell}$, Definition A.14]
  \label{def:lsd}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:problem-family, def:msd}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$, an instance of $\LSD_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple
  of nonzero vectors $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a pair
  $(i,j)$ with $i\ne j$ minimizing $\cossim{v_i}{v_j}$ over all distinct pairs:
  \[
    \cossim{v_i}{v_j}
    =
    \min_{\substack{1\le p,q\le n\\p\ne q}}\cossim{v_p}{v_q}.
  \]
  Formally this is a search relation over nonzero binary vectors and distinct
  output indices, not a tag.

  The declaration audited at this label is a self-contained data package
  `def_lsd' (for example a structure value `LSDProblemData'), not
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', not a call to that placeholder, and not
  a bare `ConcreteProblemFamily' value whose concrete score and optimum are only
  hidden in external helpers. In particular, the `family' field consumed by
  downstream algorithmic and hardness nodes must be a concrete
  `ConcreteProblemFamily' built as a projection of the package's own concrete
  score/optimum fields, exactly as `def_msd' exposes the concrete `MSDFamily'.
  A `family' field of the form
  `(LSDFamily : def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder)', or any value whose type
  is `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', is rejected: it replaces the
  concrete least-similarity relation by an abstract parameter-sensitive tag.
  The package may contain a field `family : ConcreteProblemFamily' for use by
  later nodes, but the audited declaration itself must also expose the concrete
  fields and projection equations below, under these names or transparent
  equivalents (the least-similarity analogue of the MSD fields):
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{LSDParam} &= \operatorname{MSDParam}
      = \{(n,\ell): n,\ell\in\N,\ n\ge2,\ \ell\ge1\},\\
    \operatorname{LSDInst}(n,\ell) &= \operatorname{MSDInst}(n,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{LSDOut}(n,\ell,V) &=
      \{(i,j): i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\},\\
    \operatorname{LSDScore}(V,i,j) &= \cossim{v_i}{v_j},\\
    \operatorname{LSDOpt}(V) &=
      \min_{i\ne j}\operatorname{LSDScore}(V,i,j),\\
    \operatorname{LSDValidOut}(n,\ell,V,(i,j))
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      i\ne j\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{LSDScore}(V,i,j)=\operatorname{LSDOpt}(V).
  \end{array}
  \]
  In field form, the package must contain at least
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{param} &: \mathrm{Type},\\
    \operatorname{inst} &: \operatorname{param}\to\mathrm{Type},\\
    \operatorname{out} &: \prod_p \operatorname{inst}(p)\to\mathrm{Type},\\
    \operatorname{score} &: \prod_{p,V}
      \operatorname{out}(p,V)\to\R,\\
    \operatorname{opt} &: \prod_{p,V}\R,\\
    \operatorname{validOut} &: \prod_{p,V}
      \operatorname{out}(p,V)\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    \operatorname{family} &: \operatorname{ConcreteProblemFamily},
  \end{array}
  \]
  together with equations identifying these fields with `LSDParam',
  `LSDInst', `LSDOut', `LSDScore', `LSDOpt', and `LSDValidOut' as displayed
  above, and equations saying that `family.Param', `family.Inst', `family.Out',
  and `family.ValidOut' are exactly the package's own `param', `inst', `out',
  and `validOut'. The minimum in `LSDOpt' is over distinct pairs only; the
  diagonal is not part of the search space.

  Abstract components named `LSDParam', `LSDInst', `LSDOut' and `LSDValidOut'
  are acceptable only when these equations unfold from the declaration audited
  at this label and `family' is the concrete projection just described. A Lean
  declaration whose body or main proof term is
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', a wrapper around it, an opaque family
  tag, `Unit', or a proposition ending in `True', or whose `family' field has
  type `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', does not satisfy this definition;
  the concrete minimizing relation has been erased.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[$\gamma$-LSD, Definition A.15]
  \label{def:gamma-lsd}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:problem-family, def:lsd}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and approximation factor $\gamma\ge 1$, an
  instance of $\gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple of nonzero vectors
  $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a pair
  $i^{*} \ne j^{*}$ such that
  \[
    \min_{\substack{1 \le i,j \le n\\i\ne j}} \cossim{v_i}{v_j}
    \le \cossim{v_{i^{*}}}{v_{j^{*}}}
    \le \gamma \cdot
    \min_{\substack{1 \le i,j \le n\\i\ne j}} \cossim{v_i}{v_j}.
  \]
  The formal output relation must include the premise $\gamma\ge1$, the minimum
  over distinct pairs, and the two approximation inequalities. It cannot be
  represented by a bare family tag.

  The audited declaration is a self-contained data package `def_gamma_lsd', not
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder' and not a wrapper around the exact LSD
  family. As in `def_gamma_msd', the `family' field consumed by downstream
  nodes must be a concrete `ConcreteProblemFamily' built as a projection of this
  package's own approximation-validity field; a `family' field of the form
  `(GammaLSDFamily : def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder)', or of type
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', is rejected. It must expose a concrete
  family with parameter $(n,\ell,\gamma)$ and the following equations:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{GammaLSDParam}
      &= \{(n,\ell,\gamma): n,\ell\in\N,\ \gamma\in\R,\
          n\ge2,\ \ell\ge1\},\\
    \operatorname{GammaLSDInst}(n,\ell,\gamma)
      &= \operatorname{LSDInst}(n,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{GammaLSDOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V)
      &= \{(i,j): i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\},\\
    \operatorname{GammaLSDScore}(V,i,j)
      &= \cossim{v_i}{v_j},\\
    m_V &= \min_{i\ne j}\cossim{v_i}{v_j},\\
    \operatorname{GammaLSDValidOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,V,(i,j))
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      \gamma\ge1\ \wedge\ i\ne j\ \wedge\
      m_V\le\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\ \wedge\
      \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le\gamma m_V .
  \end{array}
  \]
  In field form, `def_gamma_lsd' contains at least
  `param', `inst', `out', `score', `opt', `validOut', and
  `family : ConcreteProblemFamily', plus transparent equations identifying all
  of these projections with the displayed `GammaLSD...' objects and with the
  search fields of `family'. The `validOut' field must mention the parameter
  $\gamma$ directly and must include both inequalities
  $m_V\le\cossim{v_i}{v_j}$ and $\cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le\gamma m_V$; the
  minimum $m_V$ and both inequalities are part of the validity relation.

  The factor $\gamma$ is a parameter of the family, not metadata outside the
  problem. A declaration that imports opaque components, stores only the tag
  `GammaLSD', proves only exact minimality, or whose `family' field has type
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder' is not this node. A declaration whose
  audited body is `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', a delegated
  placeholder-style family wrapper, an exact-LSD relation with $\gamma$ ignored,
  `Unit', or a proof ending in `True' is rejected.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[LSD decision version, $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$, Definition A.16]
  \label{def:lsd-dec}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and threshold $t\in[0,1]$, an instance of
  $\LSD_{n,\ell,t}$ is an $n$-tuple of nonzero vectors
  $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. It is a yes instance iff there exist
  $1\le i,j\le n$ with $i\ne j$ and $\cossim{v_i}{v_j} \le t$. Thus the
  yes-predicate is exactly
  \[
    \exists\, i\ne j,\quad \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le t,
  \]
  with the nonzero-binary input promise and threshold $t$ included in the
  relation.

  The declaration audited here must expose the concrete decision family
  $\operatorname{LSDThreshold}$ with parameter $(n,\ell,t)$:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{LSDDecInst}(n,\ell,t)
      &= \operatorname{LSDInst}(n,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{LSDDecYes}(n,\ell,t,V)
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \exists i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\ \wedge\
        \cossim{v_i}{v_j}\le t,\\
    \operatorname{LSDDecNo}(n,\ell,t,V)
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      0\le t\le1\ \wedge\
      \forall i,j:\operatorname{Fin} n,\ i\ne j\Rightarrow
        t<\cossim{v_i}{v_j}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are the decision predicates used by the algorithm and transformer
  nodes. Opaque helpers named `LSDDecYes' and `LSDDecNo' are insufficient unless
  this exact existential/nonexistential cosine-threshold content unfolds from
  the declaration at this label.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Bichromatic $\gamma$-LSD]
  \label{def:bichromatic-gamma-lsd}
  \uses{def:cosine, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and $\gamma\ge1$, an instance of bichromatic
  $\gamma\text{-}\LSD_{n,\ell}$ is a pair of $n$-tuples
  $A=(a_1,\ldots,a_n)$ and $B=(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$ of nonzero vectors in
  $\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a cross-color pair $(i,j)$ with
  $1\le i,j\le n$ such that, writing
  \[
    c_I(p,q)=\cossim{a_p}{b_q},
    \qquad
    m_I=\min_{1\le p,q\le n} c_I(p,q),
  \]
  one has
  \[
    m_I \le c_I(i,j) \le \gamma m_I .
  \]
  The output indices range over different color classes, so no $i\ne j$
  condition is present. The nonzero-binary promises on both lists, the
  approximation factor $\gamma$, the cross-color minimum $m_I$, and the two
  approximation inequalities are the concrete search relation. A formalization
  that treats this as the monochromatic $\gamma$-LSD family with a tag, or that
  omits the $A\times B$ indexing, is not this problem.
\end{definition}

\chapter{Fine-grained complexity: hypotheses and intermediate problems}

% --- The hardness hypotheses, stated as assumptions/conjectures. ------------

\begin{definition}[$k$-SAT]
  \label{def:ksat}
  \uses{def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For a parameter $k\in\N$, $k\SAT$ is the satisfiability problem for Boolean
  formulas in conjunctive normal form in which every clause has at most
  $k$ literals; $n$ denotes the number of variables. An instance is such a CNF
  formula, and it is a yes instance iff there exists a Boolean assignment of its
  $n$ variables satisfying every clause. Recalled to state SETH. This is a
  concrete decision problem, not merely the symbol $k\SAT$.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Strong Exponential Time Hypothesis (SETH), Definition 2.4 / A.1]
  \label{assumption:seth}
  \uses{def:ksat, def:truly-subquadratic}
  A $k\SAT$ algorithm is concrete data: a run function on $k$-CNF formulas, a
  proof that the returned Boolean is true exactly on satisfiable formulas, and a
  worst-case runtime function $T_{\mathcal A}(n)$ over formulas with $n$
  variables. SETH is the proposition
  \[
    \forall\,\eps>0,\ \exists\,k\ge1,\ \neg\exists\,\mathcal A,\ C>0,\ n_0,\
      \forall n\ge n_0,\quad
        T_{\mathcal A}(n) \le C\cdot 2^{(1-\eps)n}.
  \]
  Equivalently, for every exponent saving $\eps>0$ there is a clause width
  $k$ for which no correct algorithm decides concrete $k\SAT$ in time
  $O(2^{(1-\eps)n})$. The quantified lower-bound content, the algorithm
  correctness relation for satisfiability, the runtime function, and the
  exponential bound are all part of this assumption. A statement that merely
  quantifies $\eps,k,n$ and concludes `True' for large $n$ is not SETH.
\end{assumption}

\begin{definition}[Orthogonal Vectors, $\OV_{n,\ell}$, Definition 2.5 / A.2]
  \label{def:ov}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$, an instance of $\OV_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple
  $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$. It is a yes instance iff there exists a
  pair $1\le i,j\le n$ with $i\ne j$ and $\inner{v_i}{v_j} = 0$. Thus the
  formal yes-predicate is
  \[
    \exists\, i\ne j,\quad \sum_{r=1}^{\ell} v_i[r]v_j[r]=0.
  \]
  The input type, binary promise, distinctness condition and orthogonality
  equation must all be encoded.
  The formal parameter record for this family contains not only the numeric
  fields $n$ and $\ell$, but also the positivity proofs
  \[
    \operatorname{hn}:2\le n,\qquad
    \operatorname{hell}:1\le\ell .
  \]
  Every construction producing an $\OV$ parameter must fill these fields. In
  particular, a generated record literal of the form
  `{ n := ..., ell := ... }' is incomplete; it must also provide
  `hn := ...' and `hell := ...' proving the displayed bounds.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Bichromatic Orthogonal Vectors]
  \label{def:bichromatic-ov}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$, an instance of bichromatic $\OV_{n,\ell}$ is a
  pair of $n$-tuples $A = \{a_1, \ldots, a_n\}$ and
  $B = \{b_1, \ldots, b_n\}$ of vectors in $\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. It is a yes
  instance iff there exist $i,j$ with $\inner{a_i}{b_j} = 0$. Unlike the
  monochromatic version, $i$ and $j$ range over different color classes and need
  not be distinct. This concrete two-input yes-predicate is the content of the
  node.
  The formal parameter record for this family contains the fields
  \[
    n:\N,\qquad \ell:\N,\qquad
    \operatorname{hn}:1\le n,\qquad
    \operatorname{hell}:1\le\ell .
  \]
  Therefore any parameter map into the bichromatic family must explicitly
  construct the two proof fields. For example, the monochromatic-to-bichromatic
  map from an $\OV$ parameter $p$ is
  \[
    \operatorname{OVToBichromaticParam}(p)=
    \{\,n:=p.n,\ \ell:=p.\ell,\ 
       \operatorname{hn}:=(1\le2\le p.n)\text{ using }p.\operatorname{hn},\
       \operatorname{hell}:=p.\operatorname{hell}\,\}.
  \]
  A record literal that copies only `n' and `ell' omits part of the concrete
  problem parameter and is rejected.
\end{definition}

\begin{conjecture}[Orthogonal Vectors Conjecture (OVC), Conjecture 2.6 / A.3]
  \label{conjecture:ovc}
  \uses{def:ov, def:no-tsq-alg, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  For any $\eps > 0$ there exists a constant $c > 0$ such that
  $\NoTSQAlg{\OV_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}$; equivalently, the dimension is
  $c\log n$ up to the fixed rounding convention.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{assumption}[SETH implies OVC, Williams (2005)]
  \label{thm:seth-implies-ovc}
  \uses{assumption:seth, conjecture:ovc}
  This is a cited external dependency from Williams (2005), not a proof
  reproduced in the paper. Its mathematical content is the implication
  \[
    \text{SETH}\Longrightarrow \text{OVC}.
  \]
  Consequently all hardness results below can be stated under SETH \emph{or}
  OVC. A formalization of this blueprint may register this node as an axiom or
  imported cited theorem. It should not generate a local proof obligation unless
  it also formalizes the standard split-and-list reduction from $k$-SAT to
  Orthogonal Vectors and the corresponding runtime calculation.
\end{assumption}

% --- Minimum Inner Product problems. ---------------------------------------

\begin{definition}[Minimum Inner Product, $\MinIP_{n,\ell}$, Definition 2.7 / A.5]
  \label{def:minip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$, an instance of $\MinIP_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple
  $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a distinct pair
  $(i,j)$ minimizing $\inner{v_i}{v_j}$ over all distinct pairs:
  \[
    \inner{v_i}{v_j} =
    \min_{\substack{1\le p,q\le n\\p\ne q}}\inner{v_p}{v_q}.
  \]
  This is a search relation over binary vectors and distinct indices.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[$\gamma$-Min-IP, Definition 2.8 / A.6]
  \label{def:gamma-minip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and $\gamma\ge 1$, an instance of
  $\gamma\text{-}\MinIP_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple
  $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a distinct pair
  $(i,j)$ satisfying the following relation. Define the score and optimum
  \[
    s_I(p,q)=\inner{v_p}{v_q},
    \qquad
    m_I=\min_{\substack{p,q\\p\ne q}}s_I(p,q).
  \]
  Then
  \[
    \operatorname{GammaMinIPValidOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,I,(i,j))
    \Longleftrightarrow
    i\ne j\ \wedge\ \gamma\ge1\ \wedge\
    m_I\le s_I(i,j)\ \wedge\ s_I(i,j)\le\gamma m_I .
  \]
  The premise $\gamma\ge1$ and this multiplicative approximation relation are
  part of the definition. The output score is allowed to be larger than the
  minimum by a factor of at most $\gamma$; it is not required to dominate all
  scores. A declaration that states
  $\forall p,q,\ s_I(p,q)\le s_I(i,j)$, or
  $s_I(i,j)\le\gamma s_I(p,q)$ for every pair $(p,q)$, is a Max-IP-style
  relation and does not satisfy this node. The audited declaration must expose
  the named score $s_I$, optimum $m_I$, and the displayed iff for
  $\operatorname{GammaMinIPValidOut}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Min-IP decision version, $\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}$, Definition 2.9 / A.7]
  \label{def:minip-dec}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and $0\le t\le \ell$, an instance of
  $\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}$ is an $n$-tuple $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. It is a
  yes instance iff there exists a distinct pair $(i,j)$ with
  $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\le t$. The threshold $t$ and this existential inequality are
  part of the yes-predicate.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Bichromatic Min-IP]
  \label{def:bichromatic-minip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  This node defines the whole bichromatic Min-IP family bundle at this label.
  The declaration audited at \ref{def:bichromatic-minip} must expose all four
  named components below, either as fields of a structure
  $\operatorname{BichromaticMinIPBundle}$ or as an equivalent dependent Sigma
  package. A declaration for only the exact search family is not this node.

  First, the shared instance type is
  \[
    \operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n,\ell)
    =
    \{(A,B): A=(a_1,\ldots,a_n),\ B=(b_1,\ldots,b_n),\
      a_i,b_j\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}\}.
  \]
  For $I=(A,B)$ define
  \[
    s_I(i,j)=\inner{a_i}{b_j},\qquad
    m_I=\min_{1\le p,q\le n}s_I(p,q).
  \]
  The bundle then contains three separate concrete problem-family declarations:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{BMinIPExact}:&
      \operatorname{Param}=\N\times\N,\quad
      \operatorname{Inst}(n,\ell)=\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    &
      \operatorname{Out}(n,\ell,I)=
        \{(i,j):1\le i,j\le n\},\\
    &
      \operatorname{ValidOut}(n,\ell,I,(i,j))
        \Longleftrightarrow s_I(i,j)=m_I;\\[2mm]
    \operatorname{BMinIPApprox}:&
      \operatorname{Param}=\N\times\N\times\R,\quad
      \operatorname{Inst}(n,\ell,\gamma)=\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    &
      \operatorname{Out}(n,\ell,\gamma,I)=
        \{(i,j):1\le i,j\le n\},\\
    &
      \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma}(n,\ell,\gamma,I,(i,j))
        \Longleftrightarrow
        \gamma\ge1\ \wedge\ m_I\le s_I(i,j)\le \gamma m_I;\\[2mm]
    \operatorname{BMinIPThreshold}:&
      \operatorname{Param}=\N\times\N\times\R,\quad
      \operatorname{Inst}(n,\ell,t)=\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    &
      \operatorname{Yes}_{t}(n,\ell,t,I)
        \Longleftrightarrow
        \exists\, i,j,\ 1\le i,j\le n\ \wedge\ s_I(i,j)\le t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here $\operatorname{BMinIPExact}$ is a search family with parameter
  $(n,\ell)$, $\operatorname{BMinIPApprox}$ is a different search family with
  parameter $(n,\ell,\gamma)$, and $\operatorname{BMinIPThreshold}$ is a
  decision family with parameter $(n,\ell,t)$. The approximation factor
  $\gamma$ and threshold $t$ are not optional metadata and cannot share a single
  overloaded parameter. The exact and approximate output relations must not be
  merged by a disjunction. In particular,
  $\operatorname{BMinIPApprox}$ must be definitionally tied to the minimum
  $m_I$: it is rejected if it requires
  $\forall p,q,\ s_I(p,q)\le s_I(i,j)$, if it requires
  $s_I(i,j)\le\gamma s_I(p,q)$ for every pair, or if it otherwise makes the
  returned pair maximal rather than within a factor $\gamma$ of the minimum.
  The statement at this label must include the projections or unfolding
  theorems for
  $\operatorname{BMinIPInst}$, $\operatorname{BMinIPExact}$,
  $\operatorname{BMinIPApprox}$, and $\operatorname{BMinIPThreshold}$; otherwise
  later uses of the approximate and threshold bichromatic problems have no
  concrete semantics.
\end{definition}

% --- Maximum Inner Product problems. ---------------------------------------

\begin{definition}[Maximum Inner Product, $\MaxIP_{n,\ell}$, Definition A.9]
  \label{def:maxip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$, an instance of $\MaxIP_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple
  $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a distinct pair
  $(i,j)$ maximizing $\inner{v_i}{v_j}$ over all distinct pairs:
  \[
    \inner{v_i}{v_j} =
    \max_{\substack{1\le p,q\le n\\p\ne q}}\inner{v_p}{v_q}.
  \]
  This is a concrete search relation over binary vectors and distinct indices.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[$\gamma$-Max-IP, Definition A.10]
  \label{def:gamma-maxip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and $\gamma\ge 1$, an instance of
  $\gamma\text{-}\MaxIP_{n,\ell}$ is an $n$-tuple
  $v_1, \ldots, v_n \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$. A valid output is a distinct pair whose
  inner product is a $\gamma$-approximation of the maximal inner product.
  Define
  \[
    s_I(p,q)=\inner{v_p}{v_q},
    \qquad
    M_I=\max_{\substack{p,q\\p\ne q}}s_I(p,q).
  \]
  Then
  \[
    \operatorname{GammaMaxIPValidOut}(n,\ell,\gamma,I,(i,j))
    \Longleftrightarrow
    i\ne j\ \wedge\ \gamma\ge1\ \wedge\
    \gamma^{-1}M_I\le s_I(i,j)\ \wedge\ s_I(i,j)\le M_I .
  \]
  The factor $\gamma$ and the premise $\gamma\ge1$ are part of the output
  relation. For $\gamma>1$ this is intentionally weaker than exact
  maximization: any pair whose score lies in the displayed interval is valid.
  A declaration that requires $\forall p,q,\ s_I(p,q)\le s_I(i,j)$ is the exact
  $\MaxIP$ relation, not this approximate relation, even though exact
  maximizers are valid examples. The audited declaration must expose the named
  score $s_I$, optimum $M_I$, and the displayed iff for
  $\operatorname{GammaMaxIPValidOut}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Max-IP decision version, $\MaxIP_{n,\ell,t}$, Definition A.11]
  \label{def:maxip-dec}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  For parameters $n,\ell\in\N$ and $0\le t\le \ell$, an instance of
  $\MaxIP_{n,\ell,t}$ is an $n$-tuple $v_1,\ldots,v_n\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$. It is a
  yes instance iff there exists a distinct pair $(i,j)$ with
  $\inner{v_i}{v_j}\ge t$. The threshold and this existential inequality are the
  concrete yes-predicate.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Bichromatic Max-IP]
  \label{def:bichromatic-maxip}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:parameter-sensitive-placeholder}
  This node defines the whole bichromatic Max-IP family bundle at this label.
  The declaration audited at \ref{def:bichromatic-maxip} must expose all four
  named components below, either as fields of a structure
  $\operatorname{BichromaticMaxIPBundle}$ or as an equivalent dependent Sigma
  package. A declaration for only the exact search family is not this node.

  First, the shared instance type is
  \[
    \operatorname{BMaxIPInst}(n,\ell)
    =
    \{(A,B): A=(a_1,\ldots,a_n),\ B=(b_1,\ldots,b_n),\
      a_i,b_j\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}\}.
  \]
  For $I=(A,B)$ define
  \[
    s_I(i,j)=\inner{a_i}{b_j},\qquad
    M_I=\max_{1\le p,q\le n}s_I(p,q).
  \]
  The bundle then contains three separate concrete problem-family declarations:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{BMaxIPExact}:&
      \operatorname{Param}=\N\times\N,\quad
      \operatorname{Inst}(n,\ell)=\operatorname{BMaxIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    &
      \operatorname{Out}(n,\ell,I)=
        \{(i,j):1\le i,j\le n\},\\
    &
      \operatorname{ValidOut}(n,\ell,I,(i,j))
        \Longleftrightarrow s_I(i,j)=M_I;\\[2mm]
    \operatorname{BMaxIPApprox}:&
      \operatorname{Param}=\N\times\N\times\R,\quad
      \operatorname{Inst}(n,\ell,\gamma)=\operatorname{BMaxIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    &
      \operatorname{Out}(n,\ell,\gamma,I)=
        \{(i,j):1\le i,j\le n\},\\
    &
      \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma}(n,\ell,\gamma,I,(i,j))
        \Longleftrightarrow
        \gamma\ge1\ \wedge\ \gamma^{-1}M_I\le s_I(i,j)\le M_I;\\[2mm]
    \operatorname{BMaxIPThreshold}:&
      \operatorname{Param}=\N\times\N\times\R,\quad
      \operatorname{Inst}(n,\ell,t)=\operatorname{BMaxIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    &
      \operatorname{Yes}_{t}(n,\ell,t,I)
        \Longleftrightarrow
        \exists\, i,j,\ 1\le i,j\le n\ \wedge\ s_I(i,j)\ge t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here $\operatorname{BMaxIPExact}$ is a search family with parameter
  $(n,\ell)$, $\operatorname{BMaxIPApprox}$ is a different search family with
  parameter $(n,\ell,\gamma)$, and $\operatorname{BMaxIPThreshold}$ is a
  decision family with parameter $(n,\ell,t)$. The approximation factor
  $\gamma$ and threshold $t$ are not optional metadata and cannot share a single
  overloaded parameter. The exact and approximate output relations must not be
  merged by a disjunction. In particular,
  $\operatorname{BMaxIPApprox}$ must be definitionally tied to the interval
  $\gamma^{-1}M_I\le s_I(i,j)\le M_I$: it is rejected if it requires the exact
  maximizer condition $\forall p,q,\ s_I(p,q)\le s_I(i,j)$ as its validity
  relation. Exact maximizers satisfy the approximate relation, but the
  approximate component's $\operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma}$ must be exactly the
  displayed approximation relation, not the stronger exact one. The statement at
  this label must include the projections or unfolding theorems for
  $\operatorname{BMaxIPInst}$, $\operatorname{BMaxIPExact}$,
  $\operatorname{BMaxIPApprox}$, and $\operatorname{BMaxIPThreshold}$; otherwise
  later uses of the approximate and threshold bichromatic problems have no
  concrete semantics.
\end{definition}

\chapter{Fine-grained reductions between intermediate problems}

\begin{lemma}[Elementary arithmetic for recursive split indices]
  \label{lem:split-tree-index-arithmetic}
  \lean{Nat.succ_pos, Nat.succ_le_of_lt, Nat.lt_of_lt_of_le, Nat.le_sub_of_add_le}
  \mathlibok
  This leaf records the elementary natural-number inequalities used when a
  recursive split node or concrete call record carries an index
  $k:\operatorname{Fin} n$ with a right child proof $h:k+1<n$. No proof in this
  blueprint may require importing `Mathlib.Tactic.Omega' or using the `omega'
  tactic; the local Mathlib build used by the disposable Lean checker does not
  provide that tactic module.

  The required arithmetic facts are:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{zeroLtFromTwoLe}:&
      2\le n \Rightarrow 0<n,\\
    \operatorname{splitIndexLt}:&
      k:\operatorname{Fin} n \Rightarrow k<n,\\
    \operatorname{splitIndexLtSucc}:&
      k:\operatorname{Fin} n \Rightarrow k<n+1,\\
    \operatorname{rightChildIndexLtSucc}:&
      h:k+1<n \Rightarrow k+1<n+1,\\
    \operatorname{suffixCardinalityGeTwo}:&
      h:k+1<n \Rightarrow 2\le n-k,\\
    \operatorname{rightOrigIndexLt}:&
      j<n-(k+1) \Rightarrow k+1+j<n,\\
    \operatorname{canonicalOffsetLt}:&
      k<q<n \Rightarrow q-(k+1)<n-(k+1),\\
    \operatorname{canonicalOffsetOrig}:&
      k<q \Rightarrow k+1+(q-(k+1))=q .
  \end{array}
  \]
  In Lean these should be proved with core `Nat' lemmas and the proof fields
  already stored in the parameter and call records. For example,
  `zeroLtFromTwoLe' is obtained by `lt_of_lt_of_le zero_lt_two hn';
  `suffixCardinalityGeTwo' is obtained from
  `Nat.succ_le_of_lt h : k+2 \le n' followed by `Nat.le_sub_of_add_le`;
  `rightOrigIndexLt' is obtained from the defining inequality
  `j.isLt : j < n-(k+1)' by the standard add/sub cancellation lemmas for
  naturals. These facts must be projected as theorem fields from the split-tree
  arithmetic package whenever the generated construction uses names such as
  `splitIndex', `hasRightChild', `canonicalLower', or `canonicalUpper'.
  A generated proof term `by omega' at any of these obligations is rejected;
  an implementation must instead expose and use the named arithmetic fields
  above.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Append-coordinate construction for bichromatic OV]
  \label{lem:ov-bichromatic-append-construction}
  \uses{def:bichromatic-ov, def:ov, def:inner-prod}
  Given a bichromatic $\OV_{n,\ell}$ instance
  $A=(a_1,\ldots,a_n)$ and $B=(b_1,\ldots,b_n)$, define
  \[
    a_i'=(a_i,1,0)\in\{0,1\}^{\ell+2},
    \qquad
    b_j'=(b_j,0,1)\in\{0,1\}^{\ell+2},
  \]
  and let $W=(a_1',\ldots,a_n',b_1',\ldots,b_n')$ be the corresponding
  monochromatic $\OV_{2n,\ell+2}$ instance. The construction has the following
  concrete behavior:
  \[
    \inner{a_i'}{a_{i'}'}=\inner{a_i}{a_{i'}}+1\ge1,\qquad
    \inner{b_j'}{b_{j'}'}=\inner{b_j}{b_{j'}}+1\ge1,
  \]
  and
  \[
    \inner{a_i'}{b_j'}=\inner{a_i}{b_j}.
  \]
  Consequently,
  \[
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\mathrm{BOV}}(A,B)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(W).
  \]
  The formal witness at this label must include the actual transformed
  monochromatic instance as data, together with proof-valued theorem fields for
  every displayed equation and equivalence. Here ``proof-valued'' is meant
  literally: a field named, for example, `appendLeftRow' has type
  \[
    \forall i,\ \operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)_{\operatorname{inl}(i)}
      =(a_i,1,0),
  \]
  and the field value is a proof of that statement. It is not a data field
  `appendLeftRow : Prop' whose value is the proposition above, nor a field
  returning a proposition to be proved elsewhere. A generated package whose
  row equations, inner-product equations, binary promise, auxiliary-predicate
  bridge, or yes-equivalence are stored only as `Prop'-valued fields has not
  asserted the construction correctness of this node.

  In Lean terms, the package must contain a field such as
  \[
    \operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B):
      \operatorname{OVInst}(2n,\ell+2),
  \]
  where the transformed $\OV$ parameter is the full parameter record
  \[
    \operatorname{BOVAppendOVParam}(p)=
    \{\,n:=p.n+p.n,\ \ell:=p.\ell+2,\
       \operatorname{hn}:=2\le p.n+p.n,\
       \operatorname{hell}:=1\le p.\ell+2\,\}.
  \]
  The proof field $\operatorname{hn}$ is obtained from the bichromatic source
  proof $p.\operatorname{hn}:1\le p.n$ twice, giving
  $1+1\le p.n+p.n$. The proof field $\operatorname{hell}$ is obtained from
  $p.\operatorname{hell}:1\le p.\ell$ and monotonicity of addition on the
  right, giving $1\le p.\ell\le p.\ell+2$. Thus a Lean definition
  \[
    \operatorname{BOVAppendOVParam}(p):\operatorname{OVParam}
  \]
  must use a record literal with all four fields `n', `ell', `hn', and
  `hell'. The literal `{ n := p.n + p.n, ell := p.ell + 2 }' is missing the
  proof fields and is not this construction. This is the corresponding
  instance type exposed by Definition~\ref{def:ov}. Its
  row equations must be proof fields of this same package:
  \[
    W_{\operatorname{inl}(i)}=(a_i,1,0),\qquad
    W_{\operatorname{inr}(j)}=(b_j,0,1),
  \]
  equivalently the first $n$ rows are the $a_i'$ and the last $n$ rows are the
  $b_j'$. The package must also include proof fields that $W$ satisfies the
  concrete $\OV$ input promise at parameter $(2n,\ell+2)$, namely that every
  row is a binary vector of length $\ell+2$. The inner-product identities and
  the final correctness field are likewise theorem fields, with types exactly
  the displayed propositions:
  \[
    \operatorname{BichromaticOVYes}_{n,\ell}(A,B)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}
      (\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)).
  \]
  More explicitly, the audited package has fields, or transparent equivalents,
  with the following \emph{types}:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{appendLeftRow}:&
      \forall i,\ W_{\operatorname{inl}(i)}=(a_i,1,0),\\
    \operatorname{appendRightRow}:&
      \forall j,\ W_{\operatorname{inr}(j)}=(b_j,0,1),\\
    \operatorname{appendBinaryPromise}:&
      \forall r,h,\ W_r[h]\in\{0,1\},\\
    \operatorname{appendLeftInner}:&
      \forall i,i',\
      \inner{a_i'}{a_{i'}'}=\inner{a_i}{a_{i'}}+1,\\
    \operatorname{appendRightInner}:&
      \forall j,j',\
      \inner{b_j'}{b_{j'}'}=\inner{b_j}{b_{j'}}+1,\\
    \operatorname{appendCrossInner}:&
      \forall i,j,\
      \inner{a_i'}{b_j'}=\inner{a_i}{b_j},\\
    \operatorname{appendPredicate\_iff\_OVYes}:&
      \operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}(A,B)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}(W),\\
    \operatorname{appendYesIff}:&
      \operatorname{BichromaticOVYes}_{n,\ell}(A,B)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}(W).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Each line is a proof field: after projection it is directly usable as a
  theorem of the indicated equality, promise, or iff. The field type may not be
  `Prop', `True', `Unit', a Sigma containing only the proposition as data, or an
  uninterpreted predicate whose definition is not the displayed formula.
  A custom predicate such as
  $\operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}(A,B)$ may be used only as a local
  abbreviation if the same audited package also proves the definitional
  equality or iff
  \[
    \operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}(A,B)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}
      (\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)).
  \]
  Without this bridge to the concrete $\OV$ family, the node is rejected.
  Merely asserting that some transformed instance exists, proving only a
  Sum-indexed auxiliary yes predicate, or stating that the construction is a
  reduction omits the behavior needed by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:ov-bichromatic-equiv}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:bichromatic-ov, def:ov, def:inner-prod}
  Expanding the inner product in the last two coordinates gives
  \[
    \inner{(a_i,1,0)}{(a_{i'},1,0)}
      =\inner{a_i}{a_{i'}}+1,
    \qquad
    \inner{(b_j,0,1)}{(b_{j'},0,1)}
      =\inner{b_j}{b_{j'}}+1,
  \]
  so two vectors from the same color class in the transformed monochromatic
  instance can never be orthogonal. Similarly,
  \[
    \inner{(a_i,1,0)}{(b_j,0,1)}
      =\inner{a_i}{b_j}+1\cdot0+0\cdot1
      =\inner{a_i}{b_j}.
  \]
  Therefore the only orthogonal pairs in $W$ are exactly transformed
  cross-color pairs, and the bichromatic and monochromatic yes predicates are
  equivalent.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[OV/bichromatic OV reduction regimes]
  \label{def:ov-bichromatic-regimes}
  \uses{def:ov, def:bichromatic-ov}
  This node owns the four regime predicates used by
  Lemma~\ref{lem:ov-bichromatic-equiv}. They are top-level mathematical
  definitions with fixed names and fixed bodies, not optional fields of the
  reduction witness and not proof-only summaries.
  The declaration audited at this label is a concrete package
  $\operatorname{OVBichromaticRegimePackage}$, or an equivalent dependent Sigma
  package, whose own projections include the four predicate-valued fields
  listed below and the four iff theorem fields stating their bodies. It is not
  a registry of external names, not a proof-only structure about already
  declared predicates, and not a package whose only theorem fields are
  reflexive equalities such as
  \[
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}
      =\operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}.
  \]
  After unfolding the declaration audited at
  \ref{def:ov-bichromatic-regimes}, the types of the package fields themselves
  must expose the parameter records and concrete bodies below:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    R.\operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime}
      &: \operatorname{OVParam}\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    R.\operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime\_iff}
      &: \forall p,\
        R.\operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime}(p)
        \Longleftrightarrow 2\le p.n\wedge1\le p.\ell,\\
    R.\operatorname{monoToBiTgtRegime}
      &: \operatorname{BichromaticOVParam}\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    R.\operatorname{monoToBiTgtRegime\_iff}
      &: \forall q,\
        R.\operatorname{monoToBiTgtRegime}(q)
        \Longleftrightarrow
        1\le q.n\wedge1\le q.\ell\wedge
        \exists p:\operatorname{OVParam},\
          R.\operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime}(p)\wedge
          q.n=p.n\wedge q.\ell=p.\ell,\\
    R.\operatorname{biToMonoSrcRegime}
      &: \operatorname{BichromaticOVParam}\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    R.\operatorname{biToMonoSrcRegime\_iff}
      &: \forall p,\
        R.\operatorname{biToMonoSrcRegime}(p)
        \Longleftrightarrow 1\le p.n\wedge1\le p.\ell,\\
    R.\operatorname{biToMonoTgtRegime}
      &: \operatorname{OVParam}\to\mathrm{Prop},\\
    R.\operatorname{biToMonoTgtRegime\_iff}
      &: \forall q,\
        R.\operatorname{biToMonoTgtRegime}(q)
        \Longleftrightarrow
        2\le q.n\wedge3\le q.\ell\wedge
        \exists p:\operatorname{BichromaticOVParam},\
          R.\operatorname{biToMonoSrcRegime}(p)\wedge
          q.n=p.n+p.n\wedge q.\ell=p.\ell+2 .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The public reserved names
  $\operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}$,
  $\operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}$,
  $\operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}$ and
  $\operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}$ must be transparent projections from
  this package, or transparent aliases to those projections with equations
  showing, for example,
  \[
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)
    =
    R.\operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime}(p).
  \]
  The accompanying public iff theorems must be obtained by projecting the
  concrete package fields above. A formalization that defines the public names
  elsewhere and then audits only a package of identifiers plus `rfl' theorems
  has not exposed the predicate bodies at this label.

  Let $\operatorname{OVParam}$ be the full parameter record from
  Definition~\ref{def:ov}, with fields
  $p.n$, $p.\ell$, $p.\operatorname{hn}:2\le p.n$ and
  $p.\operatorname{hell}:1\le p.\ell$. Let
  $\operatorname{BichromaticOVParam}$ be the full parameter record from
  Definition~\ref{def:bichromatic-ov}, with fields
  $q.n$, $q.\ell$, $q.\operatorname{hn}:1\le q.n$ and
  $q.\operatorname{hell}:1\le q.\ell$. The four reserved Lean declarations are
  predicates with the following exact meanings:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)
      &:\Longleftrightarrow
      2\le p.n\ \wedge\ 1\le p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}(q)
      &:\Longleftrightarrow
      1\le q.n\ \wedge\ 1\le q.\ell\ \wedge\
      \exists p:\operatorname{OVParam},\
        \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)\ \wedge\
        q.n=p.n\ \wedge\ q.\ell=p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)
      &:\Longleftrightarrow
      1\le p.n\ \wedge\ 1\le p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}(q)
      &:\Longleftrightarrow
      2\le q.n\ \wedge\ 3\le q.\ell\ \wedge\
      \exists p:\operatorname{BichromaticOVParam},\
        \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)\ \wedge\
        q.n=p.n+p.n\ \wedge\ q.\ell=p.\ell+2 .
  \end{array}
  \]
  A compliant Lean implementation may write these as transparent `def`s or as
  reducible abbreviations. In either case, unfolding the declaration with the
  reserved name must reveal the corresponding conjunction/existential above.
  The declarations may not be
  \[
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p):=\mathrm{True},
    \quad
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}(q):=\mathrm{True},
    \quad
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p):=\mathrm{True},
    \quad
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}(q):=\mathrm{True},
  \]
  and may not reduce to `Unit', `Nonempty True', an always-true marker
  proposition, or a structure whose only field is a trivial proof.

  The same audited declaration must expose the four iff theorems
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime\_iff}:&
      \forall p,\
      \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)
      \Longleftrightarrow 2\le p.n\wedge 1\le p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime\_iff}:&
      \forall q,\
      \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}(q)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      1\le q.n\wedge1\le q.\ell\wedge
      \exists p:\operatorname{OVParam},\
        \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)\wedge
        q.n=p.n\wedge q.\ell=p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime\_iff}:&
      \forall p,\
      \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)
      \Longleftrightarrow 1\le p.n\wedge1\le p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime\_iff}:&
      \forall q,\
      \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}(q)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      2\le q.n\wedge3\le q.\ell\wedge
      \exists p:\operatorname{BichromaticOVParam},\
        \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)\wedge
        q.n=p.n+p.n\wedge q.\ell=p.\ell+2 .
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are theorem fields or transparent theorems attached to this node. They
  are not propositions stored as data. In particular, a theorem whose right
  side is `True' or whose proof is `Iff.rfl' after defining the regime to be
  `True' fails this node. A theorem whose statement is only an identity
  between a predicate and itself, or an iff between a predicate and itself,
  also fails this node: the right-hand side of each iff must be the displayed
  conjunction/existential body, so that the statement itself rules out an
  abstract registry implementation.

  The image-membership facts are also part of the definition package. If
  $\operatorname{OVToBichromaticParam}(p)$ is the identity parameter map with
  the bichromatic proof fields filled from $p.\operatorname{hn}$ and
  $p.\operatorname{hell}$, then
  \[
    \operatorname{monoToBiTargetInRegime}:
      \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)\to
      \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}
        (\operatorname{OVToBichromaticParam}(p)).
  \]
  If $\operatorname{BOVAppendOVParam}(p)$ is the append-coordinate parameter
  map $(n,\ell)\mapsto(2n,\ell+2)$ with the $\OV$ proof fields filled, then
  \[
    \operatorname{biToMonoTargetInRegime}:
      \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)\to
      \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}
        (\operatorname{BOVAppendOVParam}(p)).
  \]
  These two fields must be proved from the displayed bodies by giving the
  required source parameter as the existential witness. They must not be proved
  by `trivial', because the target predicates are not definitionally true.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[OV is subquadratic equivalent to bichromatic OV, Lemma A.4]
  \label{lem:ov-bichromatic-equiv}
  \uses{def:ov, def:bichromatic-ov, def:ov-bichromatic-regimes, lem:ov-bichromatic-append-construction, def:fg-reduction-predicates, def:tsq-alg-exists}
  This node asserts a concrete pair of fine-grained reductions, not merely an
  abstract logical equivalence:
  \[
    \SubquadEquiv{\OV_{n,\ell}}{\text{bichromatic }\OV_{n,\ell}}.
  \]
  The declaration audited at this label must be the concrete witness package
  $\operatorname{OVBichromaticEquivWitness}$ itself, or an equivalent dependent
  Sigma package with the projections below. It must not be merely
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{OVBichromaticEquivWitness})$. The
  directional reduction subpackages must expose their construction data; they
  may not be only opaque fields of type $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ whose
  source regime, call list, reconstruction, correctness and runtime projections
  cannot be inspected at this label. The package contains two concrete
  subpackages
  \[
    R_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}
      \quad\text{and}\quad
    R_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}},
  \]
  with the following mandatory fields.
  In addition to the concrete subpackages below, the audited witness must
  export actual fine-grained reduction values:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{monoToBiFGReduction}:&
      \operatorname{FGReduction}(\OV,\mathrm{BOV}),\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoFGReduction}:&
      \operatorname{FGReduction}(\mathrm{BOV},\OV),\\
    \operatorname{subquadEquivProof}:&
      \SubquadEquiv{\OV}{\mathrm{BOV}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These fields are values/proofs, not types or propositions describing that such
  values could exist. Concretely, `monoToBiFGReduction' and
  `biToMonoFGReduction' must be constructed by the constructor for
  Definition~\ref{def:fg-reduction-predicates} (or by a transparent reducible
  definition whose projections reduce to that constructor) using the source
  regimes, parameter maps, call lists, reconstruction procedures, correctness
  proofs and runtime accounting specified below. A field
  `monoToBiFGReduction : Prop', a field whose value is the type
  `FGReduction OV BOV', or a field containing only
  `Nonempty (FGReduction OV BOV)' without a witness is rejected. The proof
  `subquadEquivProof' must be obtained from these two concrete reduction
  values, for example by pairing `Nonempty.intro monoToBiFGReduction' and
  `Nonempty.intro biToMonoFGReduction'; it may not be an independent axiom or a
  proposition-valued field.

  The concrete subpackages are the data from which these two reduction values
  are built. Each displayed correctness or runtime item below is again a
  proof-valued field: its type is the displayed equality, iff, implication or
  inequality, and its value is a proof. It is not a field of type `Prop' whose
  value is the displayed proposition.

  The source regimes are explicit large-parameter regimes, not arbitrary
  nonempty predicates:
  \[
    R_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}.\operatorname{SrcRegime}(n,\ell)
      \Longrightarrow n\ge2,\ \ell\ge1,
    \qquad
    R_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}.\operatorname{SrcRegime}(n,\ell)
      \Longrightarrow n\ge1,\ \ell\ge1,
  \]
  and each regime is the concrete full-domain regime from
  Definition~\ref{def:ov-bichromatic-regimes}. In particular, neither source
  regime may be empty, `False', `True', or a proposition with no parameter
  constraints.
  The mono-to-bi source-regime projection must contain exactly the two
  well-formedness bounds, not an unspecified source-slice predicate:
  \[
    \operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime\_iff}(n,\ell)
    \Longleftrightarrow n\ge2\wedge \ell\ge1 .
  \]
  The audited witness must also expose the two projections
  \[
    \operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime\_n}(h): n\ge2,
    \qquad
    \operatorname{monoToBiSrcRegime\_ell}(h): \ell\ge1
  \]
  for every
  $h:R_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}.\operatorname{SrcRegime}(n,\ell)$,
  and a converse constructor from $n\ge2$ and $\ell\ge1$. These projections
  must be recoverable from the declaration audited at this label, not merely
  from a comment or an external helper theorem. The bi-to-mono source-regime
  projection analogously unfolds to $n\ge1\wedge\ell\ge1$.
  A source regime saying only $n\ge2$, or only eventual nonemptiness, is not the
  regime used in this lemma: the reduction calls the bichromatic problem in the
  same dimension $\ell$, so the target instance is only one of the concrete
  vector problems of Definition~\ref{def:bichromatic-ov} when $\ell\ge1$.
  In particular, the Lean term
  `fun p => 2 <= p.n' is explicitly rejected as the mono-to-bi source regime:
  it drops the dimension condition and does not provide the required
  `monoToBiSrcRegime_iff' equivalence.

  The four generated Lean names used for the directional reduction regimes are
  reserved at this label and must have the concrete meanings below. They are
  predicates on the corresponding full parameter records; none of them may be
  definitionally `True', `Unit', `Nonempty True', or a proposition whose only
  field is `trivial'.
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p):&
      2\le p.n\ \wedge\ 1\le p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}(q):&
      1\le q.n\ \wedge\ 1\le q.\ell\ \wedge\
      \exists p:\operatorname{OVParam},\
        \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)
        \wedge q.n=p.n\wedge q.\ell=p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p):&
      1\le p.n\ \wedge\ 1\le p.\ell,\\
    \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}(q):&
      2\le q.n\ \wedge\ 3\le q.\ell\ \wedge\
      \exists p:\operatorname{BichromaticOVParam},\
        \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)
        \wedge q.n=p.n+p.n\wedge q.\ell=p.\ell+2 .
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are the definitions from
  Definition~\ref{def:ov-bichromatic-regimes}; the equivalence witness must
  import those exact predicates instead of redeclaring local all-true regimes.
  The audited witness must expose theorem fields
  `OVMonoToBiSrcRegime_iff', `OVMonoToBiTgtRegime_iff',
  `OVBiToMonoSrcRegime_iff', and `OVBiToMonoTgtRegime_iff' proving the four
  displayed equivalences. It must also expose image-membership fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{monoToBiTargetInRegime}:&
      \operatorname{OVMonoToBiSrcRegime}(p)\to
      \operatorname{OVMonoToBiTgtRegime}
        (\operatorname{OVToBichromaticParam}(p)),\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoTargetInRegime}:&
      \operatorname{OVBiToMonoSrcRegime}(p)\to
      \operatorname{OVBiToMonoTgtRegime}
        (\operatorname{BOVAppendOVParam}(p)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These fields are part of the reduction witness because the target oracle is
  only called on parameters lying in its target regime. The mono-to-bi target
  regime is therefore the image of the identity parameter map into the
  bichromatic family, with the required positivity proofs; the bi-to-mono target
  regime is the image of the append-coordinate parameter map
  $(n,\ell)\mapsto(2n,\ell+2)$. A generated definition such as
  `def OVMonoToBiTgtRegime := True' or
  `def OVBiToMonoSrcRegime := True' is explicitly rejected even if the
  surrounding reduction package separately constructs well-formed parameters.
  A target regime saying only `True' erases the parameter transformation and
  makes the runtime and oracle-call obligations independent of the concrete
  target family, so it is not the regime used in Lemma A.4.

  The mono-to-bi subpackage has concrete fields:
  \[
    \operatorname{hasZero}(V)
      \Longleftrightarrow \exists i,\ v_i=0^\ell,
    \qquad
    \operatorname{toBi}(V)=(V,V)
  \]
  for every monochromatic instance $V=(v_1,\ldots,v_n)$. Its transformed
  parameter map is the full bichromatic parameter record
  \[
    \operatorname{OVToBichromaticParam}(p)=
    \{\,n:=p.n,\ \ell:=p.\ell,\
       \operatorname{hn}:=1\le p.n,\
       \operatorname{hell}:=p.\operatorname{hell}\,\},
  \]
  where the proof $\operatorname{hn}:1\le p.n$ is derived from the
  monochromatic proof $p.\operatorname{hn}:2\le p.n$ by transitivity
  $1\le2\le p.n$. The map $\operatorname{toBi}(V)=(V,V)$ is an instance of this
  exact parameter. A generated definition
  \[
    \operatorname{OVToBichromaticParam}(p):\operatorname{BichromaticOVParam}
  \]
  must therefore fill `hn' and `hell' explicitly; the record
  `{ n := p.n, ell := p.ell }' is rejected.
  Its transformed
  algorithm, given a bichromatic OV algorithm $\mathcal A$, is definitionally:
  first return true if $\operatorname{hasZero}(V)$, and otherwise run
  $\mathcal A$ on $\operatorname{toBi}(V)=(V,V)$. The correctness field is the
  concrete equivalence
  \[
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{hasZero}(V)\ \vee\
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\mathrm{BOV}}(V,V),
  \]
  together with the proof that when $\operatorname{hasZero}(V)$ is false, every
  diagonal pair has nonzero inner product:
  $\inner{v_i}{v_i}\ne0$ for all $i$.

  The bi-to-mono subpackage has concrete parameter and instance maps
  \[
    (n,\ell)\mapsto(2n,\ell+2),\qquad
    a_i\mapsto a_i'=(a_i,1,0),\qquad
    b_j\mapsto b_j'=(b_j,0,1),
  \]
  where the parameter map is the same full $\operatorname{BOVAppendOVParam}$
  record from Lemma~\ref{lem:ov-bichromatic-append-construction}, including
  the proof fields
  \[
    \operatorname{hn}:2\le n+n,\qquad
    \operatorname{hell}:1\le\ell+2 .
  \]
  and maps $(A,B)$ to the monochromatic list
  $A'\cup B'=(a_1',\ldots,a_n',b_1',\ldots,b_n')$. Its correctness field is the
  pair of displayed equalities and the resulting yes-predicate equivalence for
  the concrete transformed $\OV$ instance:
  \[
    \inner{a_i'}{a_{i'}'}\ge1,\qquad
    \inner{b_j'}{b_{j'}'}\ge1,\qquad
    \inner{a_i'}{b_j'}=\inner{a_i}{b_j},
  \]
  hence
  \[
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\mathrm{BOV}}(A,B)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}
      \bigl(\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)\bigr),
  \]
  where $\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)$ is the
  $\operatorname{OVInst}(2n,\ell+2)$ from
  Lemma~\ref{lem:ov-bichromatic-append-construction}. The witness may not state
  correctness only for an auxiliary predicate
  $\operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}$. If such a predicate is introduced,
  the witness must contain a field
  \[
    \operatorname{appendPredicate\_iff\_OVYes}:
    \operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}(A,B)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}
      (\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)),
  \]
  and the exported `biToMonoCorrect' field below must target the right-hand
  concrete $\operatorname{OVYes}$ statement, not the auxiliary predicate.
  The Boolean reconstruction field for this direction is exactly the Boolean
  answer returned by the monochromatic OV algorithm on
  $\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)$.

  Both subpackages include proof-valued runtime-transform fields, not just
  correctness:
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)
      \le C\bigl(n\ell+T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)\bigr),
    \qquad
    T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell)
      \le C\,T_{\mathrm{mono}}(2n,\ell+2)+C'n\ell,
  \]
  which preserve a truly subquadratic exponent up to polynomial factors in
  $\ell$. These fields must have the displayed inequalities as their field
  types, so projecting the field gives a proof of the inequality. They may not
  be fields of type `Prop' whose values are the displayed propositions, and
  they may not have type `True', `Unit',
  `Nonempty True', or any other vacuous placeholder, and they may not omit the
  target runtime functions $T_{\mathrm{bi}}$ and $T_{\mathrm{mono}}$. The
  transformed runtimes are defined runtimes of the constructed algorithms, not
  arbitrary fields. Concretely, for constants
  $c_{\mathrm{scan}},c_{\mathrm{build}},c_{\mathrm{test}}>0$,
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{scan}}\,n\ell+
      T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)+
      c_{\mathrm{test}}\ell
  \]
  for the zero-vector scan, one bichromatic oracle call and the final Boolean
  reconstruction, while
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{build}}\,n(\ell+2)+
      T_{\mathrm{mono}}(2n,\ell+2)
  \]
  for building the appended instance and making one monochromatic oracle call.
  The runtime inequalities above are then derived from these definitions. A
  field assigning either transformed runtime to $0$, or to a value independent
  of the target runtime function, is rejected even if the displayed inequality
  is syntactically provable.
  The bi-to-mono runtime field is split into two required fields:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{biToMonoRuntimeDef}:&
      T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell,T_{\mathrm{mono}})
      =
      c_{\mathrm{build}}\,n(\ell+2)+T_{\mathrm{mono}}(2n,\ell+2),\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoRuntimeBound}:&
      T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell,T_{\mathrm{mono}})
      \le C\,T_{\mathrm{mono}}(2n,\ell+2)+C'n\ell .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The left side of the bound must be the named runtime function from
  `biToMonoRuntimeDef'. The bound is rejected if, after unfolding only the field
  declaration being audited, its conclusion has syntactically identical left and
  right sides, or if the target runtime occurs only on the right side but not in
  the definition of
  $T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell,T_{\mathrm{mono}})$.

  More explicitly, the audited witness package must contain named fields whose
  contents are at least:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{monoToBiCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V)\Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{hasZero}(V)\vee\operatorname{Yes}_{\mathrm{BOV}}(V,V),\\
    \operatorname{monoToBiRuntime}:&
      \forall T_{\mathrm{bi}},\
      T_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)
      \le C(n\ell+T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)),\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoLeftInner}:&
      \inner{a_i'}{a_{i'}'}=\inner{a_i}{a_{i'}}+1,\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoRightInner}:&
      \inner{b_j'}{b_{j'}'}=\inner{b_j}{b_{j'}}+1,\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoCrossInner}:&
      \inner{a_i'}{b_j'}=\inner{a_i}{b_j},\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\mathrm{BOV}}(A,B)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}
        (\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B)),\\
    \operatorname{appendPredicate\_iff\_OVYes}:&
      \operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}(A,B)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}
        (\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B))
      \quad\text{if an auxiliary predicate is introduced},\\
    \operatorname{biToMonoRuntime}:&
      \forall T_{\mathrm{mono}},\
      T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell)
      =c_{\mathrm{build}}n(\ell+2)+T_{\mathrm{mono}}(2n,\ell+2)
      \ \wedge\
      T_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell)
      \le C\,T_{\mathrm{mono}}(2n,\ell+2)+C'n\ell .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The three bi-to-mono inner-product fields may be imported directly from
  Lemma~\ref{lem:ov-bichromatic-append-construction}, but they must still be
  present in, or projected from, the reduction witness audited at this label. A
  proof object containing only empty-regime reductions, only abstract
  $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ fields, only runtime fields equal to `True', or
  runtime fields set to $0$ or otherwise disconnected from the oracle runtime,
  only correctness for $\operatorname{OVAppendMonochromaticYes}$ rather than
  $\operatorname{OVYes}_{2n,\ell+2}(\operatorname{appendOVInst}(A,B))$, or
  only the implication
  $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\OV}\leftrightarrow\TSQAlg{\OV}$, is too weak and
  does not satisfy this lemma.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:ov, def:bichromatic-ov, def:inner-prod, lem:ov-bichromatic-append-construction, def:fg-reduction-predicates, def:tsq-alg-exists}
  ($\Leftarrow$) Suppose $\mathcal A$ solves bichromatic $\OV_{n,\ell}$ in
  $\bigO(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))$. Given an $\OV_{n,\ell}$ instance
  $V = \{v_1, \ldots, v_n\}$, first check (in time $\bigO(n\ell)$) whether any
  $v_i$ is the all-zero vector; if so, this is a yes instance. Otherwise set
  $A = B = V$ and run $\mathcal A$ on $A,B$. Since no vector is zero,
  $\inner{v_i}{v_i} \ne 0$ for all $i$, so a pair $i \ne j$ with
  $\inner{v_i}{v_j} = 0$ exists iff $\mathcal A$ reports an orthogonal pair
  $a \in A$, $b \in B$. Total time $\bigO(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell) +
  n\ell) = \bigO(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))$.
  This gives the witness
  $R_{\mathrm{mono}\leftarrow\mathrm{bi}}$ on the nonempty source regime of all
  sufficiently large monochromatic parameters; the instance map is $V\mapsto
  (V,V)$ after the explicit zero-vector branch, the output reconstruction is
  the returned Boolean answer, and the displayed runtime bound supplies the
  algorithm-transform field of Definition~\ref{def:fg-reduction-predicates}.

  ($\Rightarrow$) Suppose $\mathcal A'$ solves $\OV_{n,\ell}$ in
  $\bigO(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))$. Given a bichromatic instance
  $A = \{a_1, \ldots, a_n\}$, $B = \{b_1, \ldots, b_n\}$ with $a_i, b_j \in
  \{0,1\}^{\ell}$, build $a_i' = (a_i, 1, 0) \in \R^{\ell+2}$ and
  $b_j' = (b_j, 0, 1) \in \R^{\ell+2}$, and let $A' = \{a_1', \ldots, a_n'\}$,
  $B' = \{b_1', \ldots, b_n'\}$. Then $\inner{a_i'}{a_j'} \ge 1$ and
  $\inner{b_i'}{b_j'} \ge 1$ for all $i,j$ (the appended coordinates contribute
  $1$), while $\inner{a_i'}{b_j'} = \inner{a_i}{b_j}$. Hence a pair of orthogonal
  vectors in $A' \cup B'$ can only be of the form $a_i', b_j'$, i.e.\ an
  orthogonal bichromatic pair $a_i, b_j$. Running $\mathcal A'$ on $A' \cup B'$
  (of size $2n$ in dimension $\ell+2$) decides the bichromatic instance in time
  $\bigO((2n)^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell+2)) =
  \bigO(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))$.
  This gives the witness
  $R_{\mathrm{bi}\leftarrow\mathrm{mono}}$ on the nonempty source regime of all
  sufficiently large bichromatic parameters; its parameter map is
  $(n,\ell)\mapsto(2n,\ell+2)$, its instance map is the append-coordinate
  construction above, its Boolean reconstruction is the monochromatic answer,
  and its correctness theorem is exactly the equivalence between an orthogonal
  pair in $A'\cup B'$ and an orthogonal bichromatic pair in $A\times B$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Min-IP is at least as hard as OV]
  \label{lem:minip-harder-ov}
  \uses{def:minip, def:gamma-minip, def:ov, def:fg-reduction-predicates, def:no-tsq-alg, conjecture:ovc, def:log-parameter-regimes}
  For any $\gamma \ge 1$,
  $\AtLeastHard{\MinIP_{n,\ell}}{\OV_{n,\ell}}$ and
  $\AtLeastHard{\gamma\text{-}\MinIP_{n,\ell}}{\OV_{n,\ell}}$. Consequently,
  assuming OVC, for any $\eps>0$ there is $c>0$ such that
  $\NoTSQAlg{\MinIP_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}$.

  The declaration audited at this label must be the concrete reduction witness
  package $\operatorname{OVToMinIPWitness}$, not only abstract
  $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ fields or the lower-bound conclusion. It contains
  two subwitnesses, one for exact Min-IP and one for $\gamma$-Min-IP. These
  subwitnesses are named
  \[
    \operatorname{exactReduction}
    \quad\text{and}\quad
    \operatorname{gammaReduction},
  \]
  but despite these names their types are not
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{FGReduction}(\OV,\MinIP))$ and not
  $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ with hidden internals. They are concrete
  structures whose projections are exactly the maps, reconstruction rule,
  zero-correctness theorems and runtime bounds listed below. A generated Lean
  declaration in which `exactReduction' or `gammaReduction' is an abstract
  reduction witness is rejected.

  Trial-3 failure-specific refinement: `exactReduction' and `gammaReduction'
  are not allowed to be assigned opaque helper values such as
  `OVToMinIPExactReduction.mk' or `OVToGammaMinIPReduction.mk' when the audited
  declaration $\operatorname{OVToMinIPWitness}$ does not itself project the
  fields of those helpers. If helper structures are used, they must be
  transparent at this label and the parent witness must re-export all of their
  mathematical fields with named projections. After unfolding only
  $\operatorname{OVToMinIPWitness}$, then the projections
  `exactReduction' and `gammaReduction', the following names, or transparent
  equivalents, must be available:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactTargetFamily}:&
      \text{the concrete }\MinIP\text{ family from Definition~\ref{def:minip}},\\
    \operatorname{gammaTargetFamily}:&
      \text{the concrete }\gamma\text{-}\MinIP\text{ family from
      Definition~\ref{def:gamma-minip}},\\
    \operatorname{exactToMinIP}:&
      \operatorname{OVInst}(n,\ell)\to
      \operatorname{MinIPInst}(n,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{gammaToMinIP}:&
      \operatorname{OVInst}(n,\ell)\to
      \operatorname{GammaMinIPInst}(n,\ell,\gamma),\\
    \operatorname{exactToMinIP\_eq}:&
      \forall V,\ \operatorname{exactToMinIP}(V)=V,\\
    \operatorname{gammaToMinIP\_eq}:&
      \forall V,\ \operatorname{gammaToMinIP}(V)=V,\\
    \operatorname{exactAnswer}:&
      V\mapsto o\mapsto
      \left(\inner{v_{o.1}}{v_{o.2}}=0\right),\\
    \operatorname{gammaAnswer}:&
      V\mapsto o\mapsto
      \left(\inner{v_{o.1}}{v_{o.2}}=0\right),\\
    \operatorname{exactMinInner}:&
      V\mapsto\min_{p\ne q}\inner{v_p}{v_q},\\
    \operatorname{gammaMinInner}:&
      V\mapsto\min_{p\ne q}\inner{v_p}{v_q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The target-family fields above must reduce to the concrete search families
  whose `Inst', `Out' and `ValidOut' relations are specified in
  Definitions~\ref{def:minip} and~\ref{def:gamma-minip}. They must not be
  `def_minip.placeholder', `def_gamma_minip.placeholder',
  `def_parameter_sensitive_placeholder', an opaque family tag, `Unit', or a
  `ConcreteProblemFamily' value whose validity relation is hidden behind an
  uninterpreted predicate. In particular, an implementation where
  `exactReduction.targetFamily = def_minip.placeholder' or
  `gammaReduction.targetFamily = def_gamma_minip.placeholder' fails this node
  even if the parent record separately contains a lower-bound proposition.

  For every
  $\OV_{n,\ell}$ instance $V=(v_1,\ldots,v_n)$ both subwitnesses use the
  identity instance map
  \[
    \operatorname{toMinIP}(V)=V
  \]
  and, given an oracle output pair $(i,j)$, reconstruct the Boolean OV answer by
  the concrete test
  \[
    \operatorname{answer}(V,(i,j)) =
    \mathrm{true}
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \inner{v_i}{v_j}=0 .
  \]
  The exact subwitness has correctness fields
  \[
    \operatorname{MinInner}(V)=0
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V),
    \qquad
    \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\MinIP}(V,(i,j))
    \wedge \inner{v_i}{v_j}=0
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\OV}(V).
  \]
  Here
  \[
    \operatorname{MinInner}(V)
      :=
      \min_{\substack{p,q\\p\ne q}}\inner{v_p}{v_q}
  \]
  is a required field or transparent local definition of the witness package,
  not an opaque symbol.
  The exact subwitness must expose the proof-valued fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactMinInner\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{exactMinInner}(V)=
        \min_{p\ne q}\inner{v_p}{v_q},\\
    \operatorname{exactMinInnerZeroIffOVYes}:&
      \operatorname{exactMinInner}(V)=0
      \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{exactReturnedZeroIffOVYes}:&
      \operatorname{MinIPValidOut}
        (\operatorname{exactToMinIP}(V),o)
      \to
      \left(
        \inner{v_{o.1}}{v_{o.2}}=0
        \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V)\right),\\
    \operatorname{exactRunCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{exactAnswer}(V,o)=\mathrm{true}
      \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V)
      \quad\text{under the same }\operatorname{MinIPValidOut}\text{ proof}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are theorem fields. They may not be fields of type `Prop' containing
  the displayed statements as data, and they may not be consequences proved
  only by an opaque $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ object.
  The approximate subwitness has the additional zero-approximation field
  \[
    \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma\text{-}\MinIP}(V,(i,j))
    \wedge \gamma\ge1
    \Longrightarrow
    \bigl(\operatorname{MinInner}(V)=0
      \Longleftrightarrow \inner{v_i}{v_j}=0\bigr),
  \]
  which is proved from
  $0\le\operatorname{MinInner}(V)\le\inner{v_i}{v_j}\le
  \gamma\operatorname{MinInner}(V)$.
  The approximate subwitness must expose the analogous proof-valued fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{gammaMinInner\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{gammaMinInner}(V)=
        \min_{p\ne q}\inner{v_p}{v_q},\\
    \operatorname{gammaApproxZero}:&
      \operatorname{GammaMinIPValidOut}
        (n,\ell,\gamma,\operatorname{gammaToMinIP}(V),o)
      \to \gamma\ge1\to
      \left(
        \operatorname{gammaMinInner}(V)=0
        \Longleftrightarrow
        \inner{v_{o.1}}{v_{o.2}}=0\right),\\
    \operatorname{gammaReturnedZeroIffOVYes}:&
      \operatorname{GammaMinIPValidOut}
        (n,\ell,\gamma,\operatorname{gammaToMinIP}(V),o)
      \to \gamma\ge1\to
      \left(
        \inner{v_{o.1}}{v_{o.2}}=0
        \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V)\right),\\
    \operatorname{gammaRunCorrect}:&
      \operatorname{gammaAnswer}(V,o)=\mathrm{true}
      \Longleftrightarrow \operatorname{OVYes}(V)
      \quad\text{under the same valid-output and }\gamma\ge1\text{ proofs}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The proof of `gammaApproxZero' must unfold the concrete
  $\gamma$-Min-IP validity relation from
  Definition~\ref{def:gamma-minip}: if
  $m=\operatorname{gammaMinInner}(V)$ and the returned score is $s^*$, then
  $0\le m\le s^*\le\gamma m$. It then proves
  $m=0\Longleftrightarrow s^*=0$. A theorem whose assumptions and conclusion
  are both `GammaMinIPValidOut ...', or a theorem that ignores the returned
  oracle pair $o$, is rejected.

  Both subwitnesses include the runtime
  field
  \[
    T_{\OV\leftarrow\MinIP}(n,\ell)
      \le C\bigl(T_{\MinIP}(n,\ell)+n\ell\bigr)
  \]
  and the analogous bound for $\gamma$-Min-IP,
  \[
    T_{\OV\leftarrow\gamma\MinIP}(n,\ell,\gamma)
      \le C\bigl(T_{\gamma\MinIP}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell\bigr).
  \]
  These runtime fields mention the target algorithm runtime function and the
  $O(n\ell)$ cost of testing the returned pair. They are not tautological
  inequalities such as
  $T_{\MinIP}(n,\ell)+n\ell\le T_{\MinIP}(n,\ell)+n\ell$; their left-hand side
  is the runtime of the constructed OV algorithm, defined by running the oracle
  once and then computing $\inner{v_i}{v_j}$ for the returned pair. A proof
  object containing only
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{FGReduction})$, an opaque algorithm
  transfer implication, or an OVC lower-bound proposition is too weak.

  To make this runtime accounting auditable, the witness must separate the
  definition of the constructed runtime from the upper-bound theorem. The exact
  subwitness contains named projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactConstructedRuntime}(T_{\MinIP},n,\ell)
      &: \R_{\ge0},\\
    \operatorname{exactRuntimeDef}:&
      \operatorname{exactConstructedRuntime}(T_{\MinIP},n,\ell)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{call}}\,
        T_{\MinIP}(n,\ell)
      +c_{\mathrm{test}}\ell
      +c_{\mathrm{copy}}n\ell
      +c_{\mathrm{bool}},\\
    \operatorname{exactRuntimeBound}:&
      \operatorname{exactConstructedRuntime}(T_{\MinIP},n,\ell)
      \le
      C\bigl(T_{\MinIP}(n,\ell)+n\ell\bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here $c_{\mathrm{call}},c_{\mathrm{test}},c_{\mathrm{copy}},c_{\mathrm{bool}}$
  are fixed positive constants belonging to the witness. The first summand is
  the runtime of the target Min-IP oracle on the concrete identity instance
  $\operatorname{toMinIP}(V)$, the second is the cost of computing the one
  returned inner product, the third covers copying or coercing the input into
  the target family, and the last covers the Boolean reconstruction. The
  analogous approximate projections are
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{gammaConstructedRuntime}(T_{\gamma\MinIP},n,\ell,\gamma)
      &: \R_{\ge0},\\
    \operatorname{gammaRuntimeDef}:&
      \operatorname{gammaConstructedRuntime}(T_{\gamma\MinIP},n,\ell,\gamma)
      =
      c'_{\mathrm{call}}\,
        T_{\gamma\MinIP}(n,\ell,\gamma)
      +c'_{\mathrm{test}}\ell
      +c'_{\mathrm{copy}}n\ell
      +c'_{\mathrm{bool}},\\
    \operatorname{gammaRuntimeBound}:&
      \operatorname{gammaConstructedRuntime}(T_{\gamma\MinIP},n,\ell,\gamma)
      \le
      C'\bigl(T_{\gamma\MinIP}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell\bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The bound fields are rejected if their left-hand side is syntactically the
  same expression as their right-hand side, if the left-hand side is
  $T_{\MinIP}(n,\ell)+n\ell$ or
  $T_{\gamma\MinIP}(n,\ell,\gamma)+n\ell$ rather than the named constructed
  runtime, or if the named constructed runtime does not mention the target
  oracle runtime. The generated Lean should expose the two defining equations
  and then prove the two inequalities from positivity of the fixed constants;
  it should not satisfy the node by choosing the constructed runtime to be
  exactly the final big-$O$ upper-bound expression.

  The lower-bound consequence is also a required projection of the audited
  witness, and its target is Min-IP, not OV. These projections are
  proof-valued theorem fields, not fields storing propositions to be proved
  elsewhere. Concretely, projecting
  `exactMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC' from
  $\operatorname{OVToMinIPWitness}$ must immediately give a term whose type is
  \[
    \forall \eps>0,\ \exists c>0,\
      \NoTSQAlg{\MinIP_{n,\logDim(c,n)}},
  \]
  and projecting `gammaMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC' must immediately give a term
  whose type is
  \[
    \forall \eps>0,\ \exists c>0,\ \forall\gamma\ge1,\
      \NoTSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\MinIP_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}.
  \]
  These field types are the transferred lower-bound statements themselves. The
  witness may not instead contain fields such as
  `exactMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC : Prop',
  `gammaMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC : Prop', or `lowerBoundStatement : Prop',
  together with equality fields saying that those propositions are intended to
  mean the displayed formulas. Such fields store statement labels as data; they
