  do not prove the lower-bound consequence required by this lemma.
  Since OVC already supplies
  \[
    \forall \eps>0,\ \exists c>0,\ 
      \NoTSQAlg{\OV_{n,\logDim(c,n)}},
  \]
  the reduction witness must export the transferred conclusions
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{exactMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC}:&
      \forall \eps>0,\ \exists c>0,\ 
        \NoTSQAlg{\MinIP_{n,\logDim(c,n)}},\\
    \operatorname{gammaMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC}:&
      \forall \eps>0,\ \exists c>0,\ \forall\gamma\ge1,\
        \NoTSQAlg{\gamma\text{-}\MinIP_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These fields are derived by contradiction: a truly subquadratic algorithm for
  the displayed Min-IP family, together with the corresponding exact or
  approximate reduction subwitness above, constructs a truly subquadratic
  algorithm for $\OV_{n,\logDim(c,n)}$, contradicting the OVC instance for the
  same logarithmic slice. The family occurring in the conclusion must be the
  concrete Min-IP family instantiated at $(n,\logDim(c,n))$, and in the
  approximate case at $(n,\logDim(c,n),\gamma)$.
  A field whose conclusion is instead
  $\NoTSQAlg{\OV_{n,\logDim(c,n)}}$, or whose Lean target is an
  `OVLogProblemFamily' or any other original-OV family, merely restates the
  hypothesis and is rejected. The transferred lower-bound field must mention
  the exact family projection of Definition~\ref{def:minip}, respectively
  Definition~\ref{def:gamma-minip}, and the proof must invoke
  `exactReduction' or `gammaReduction' to turn a hypothetical Min-IP algorithm
  into an OV algorithm before applying OVC.
  If a convenience field named `lowerBoundStatement' is present, it must also
  be a theorem field whose type is the conjunction of the two transferred
  lower bounds above, or a reducible pair of the two theorem fields
  `exactMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC' and `gammaMinIPLowerBoundFromOVC'. It is
  rejected if it is merely a proposition-valued field, a string/tag for the
  statement, a `Nonempty' wrapper around a proposition, or a field accompanied
  only by equations identifying the proposition it stores. The proof term for
  any accepted `lowerBoundStatement' must reduce to the contradiction argument
  using OVC and the exact/gamma reduction witnesses; it may not be supplied as
  independent unproved data.

  These runtime projections are mandatory fields of the subwitnesses
  themselves. In particular, unfolding
  $\operatorname{exactReduction}$ must expose fields literally named, or
  transparently equivalent to,
  `exactConstructedRuntime', `exactRuntimeDef', and `exactRuntimeBound'; and
  unfolding $\operatorname{gammaReduction}$ must expose
  `gammaConstructedRuntime', `gammaRuntimeDef', and `gammaRuntimeBound'. A
  witness that exposes only fields called `runtimeBound' or
  `gammaRuntimeBound', with no separate constructed-runtime function and no
  defining equation for that function, is not a witness for this lemma even if
  the displayed asymptotic inequality appears elsewhere in the file. The audit
  should reject any implementation in which the constructed runtime can be
  changed independently of the oracle call and returned-pair inner-product test,
  or in which the runtime definition is hidden behind an opaque
  $\operatorname{FGReduction}$ object.

  The projections must be separate fields, not a single bundled conjunction.
  In particular, an implementation where the exact side exposes only
  \[
    \operatorname{exactRuntimeBound}(T_{\MinIP})
      \ \wedge\ 
      \forall n,\ell,\ \operatorname{exactRuntimeDef}(T_{\MinIP},n,\ell)
  \]
  is not aligned with this node: the audited structure must have
  `exactConstructedRuntime' as a function field, `exactRuntimeDef' as a theorem
  whose left-hand side is that function, and `exactRuntimeBound' as a theorem
  whose left-hand side is again that same function. The same rule applies to
  the approximate side: `gammaRuntimeBound' alone is insufficient unless
  `gammaConstructedRuntime' and `gammaRuntimeDef' are also projections of
  $\operatorname{gammaReduction}$. The exact and approximate constructed
  runtimes must both contain the oracle-call cost, returned-pair inner-product
  test cost, input-copy/coercion cost, and Boolean reconstruction cost as
  displayed above.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:minip, def:gamma-minip, def:ov, conjecture:ovc}
  Given an $\OV_{n,\ell}$ instance, run the (approximate) Min-IP algorithm to
  obtain a pair achieving the minimum inner product (or a $\gamma$-approximation
  of it) and test whether that value is $0$. There is an orthogonal pair iff the
  minimum inner product is $0$; and any multiplicative $\gamma$-approximation of
  $0$ must itself be $0$, so the $\gamma$-approximate version detects it too.
  Hence a truly subquadratic algorithm for ($\gamma$-)Min-IP gives one for OV,
  which is impossible under OVC (Conjecture~\ref{conjecture:ovc}).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Canonical split-call score transport for Min-IP]
  \label{lem:minip-canonical-cross-score-transport}
  \uses{def:minip, def:bichromatic-minip, def:inner-prod, lem:split-tree-index-arithmetic}
  Let $X$ be a concrete $\MinIP_{n,\ell}$ instance and let
  $o=(i,j)$ be a distinct output pair. Write
  \[
    i_-=\min(i,j),\qquad i_+=\max(i,j),
  \]
  and let $\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)$ be the split-tree call whose left
  child contains exactly the row $i_-$ and whose right child contains the
  consecutive rows strictly after $i_-$. Let
  $\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)$ be the index of $i_+$ inside this
  right child. This node records the concrete row transport that is needed
  before comparing scores:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{canonicalLeftOrig}(o):&
      \operatorname{callLeftOrig}(\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o),0)=i_-,\\
    \operatorname{canonicalRightOrig}(o):&
      \operatorname{callRightOrig}
        (\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o),
         \operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))=i_+,\\
    \operatorname{canonicalLeftRow}(X,o):&
      \forall r,\ 
      \operatorname{leftRow}
        (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),0)[r]
      =X_{i_-}[r],\\
    \operatorname{canonicalRightRow}(X,o):&
      \forall r,\ 
      \operatorname{rightRow}
        (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
         \operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))[r]
      =X_{i_+}[r].
  \end{array}
  \]
  Consequently, for the canonical cross-pair
  $(0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))$,
  \[
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
       (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)))
    =
    \inner{X_{i_-}}{X_{i_+}}.
  \]
  Combining this with commutativity of the finite-sum inner product gives the
  orientation-independent score transport
  \[
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
       (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)))
    =
    \operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(X,o).
  \]

  The generated Lean names for these fields are reserved at this label. If the
  implementation uses the names
  `MinIPSplitCanonical_leftOrig',
  `MinIPSplitCanonical_rightOrig',
  `MinIPSplitCanonical_leftRow',
  `MinIPSplitCanonical_rightRow', and
  `MinIPSplitCanonicalScore_eq', then their normalized statements must be the
  four origin/row equations and the final score equality above. The row
  equations are proof-valued theorem fields, not propositions stored as data.
  Trial-14 failure-specific refinement: the score equality is about the score
  of the canonical split-tree call itself.  The declaration audited at this
  label must not introduce a separate one-row bichromatic instance, such as
  `canonicalBichromaticPairInst X o', and then prove a score equation for that
  separate instance at output pair $(0,0)$.  The normalized left-hand side of
  `MinIPSplitCanonicalScore_eq' must be exactly
  \[
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
       (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))),
  \]
  or the same expression with transparent aliases unfolded.  The audited
  package must also expose a theorem field
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{MinIPSplitCanonicalScore\_toPairScore}:&
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
       (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)))
    =
    \operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(X,o).
  \end{array}
  \]
  This second equality is orientation-independent: it must handle both
  $o=(i_-,i_+)$ and $o=(i_+,i_-)$, using commutativity of the finite-sum inner
  product only after the canonical split-call row equations have rewritten the
  left and right rows to $X_{i_-}$ and $X_{i_+}$.  A theorem whose conclusion is
  \[
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      (\operatorname{canonicalBichromaticPairInst}(X,o),(0,0))
    =
    \operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(X,o)
  \]
  is rejected even if `canonicalBichromaticPairInst' happens to contain the two
  same vectors, because it does not state that the pair's score occurs in the
  actual recursive oracle call
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o))$ at index
  $(0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))$.  Likewise, proving only the two
  row-origin equations for `crossInst' and a separate score theorem for the
  one-row instance fails this node; the score theorem itself must mention the
  canonical split call and canonical right index.
  Trial-15 failure-specific refinement: the audited package must expose the
  canonical split-call score theorem as one theorem with the split-call
  left-hand side and the original-pair right-hand side, not as two disconnected
  facts.  The required theorem field is
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{canonicalSplitCallPairScore}:&
    \forall X,o,\ 
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      \bigl(\operatorname{crossInst}
        (X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
        (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))\bigr)
    =
    \operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(X,o).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Its proof may use an intermediate theorem
  \[
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
      (\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
       (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)))
    =
    \inner{X_{i_-}}{X_{i_+}},
  \]
  but the exported theorem above must remain about the same
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(X,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o))$.  A theorem for
  any object whose type is
  $\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(1,1,\ell)$, a theorem at index $(0,0)$, or a
  theorem whose left-hand side contains a name other than
  `crossInst X (canonicalCall o)' is not accepted unless a separate projection
  first proves that this object is definitionally the canonical split call and
  that $(0,0)$ is definitionally
  $(0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))$.  In the ordinary case
  $\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)$ is not a constant zero index; it is
  the index of $i_+$ in the right suffix of the split call, and that index must
  occur syntactically in the score statement.
  In particular, `MinIPSplitCanonical_rightRow' must state the coordinatewise
  equality
  \[
    \forall r,\ 
    X.V\!\left(
      \operatorname{MinIPCallRightOrig}
        (\operatorname{MinIPSplitCanonicalCall}(o))
        (\operatorname{MinIPSplitCanonicalRightIndex}(o))
    \right)(r)
    =
    X.V(\operatorname{MinIPSplitPairHigh}(o))(r),
  \]
  or the equivalent vector equality obtained from
  `MinIPSplitCanonical_rightOrig' by congruence. The proof of
  `MinIPSplitCanonicalScore_eq' must use these row equations explicitly before
  simplifying the finite sum. It is rejected if it tries to prove
  \[
    \inner{X_{i_-}}{
      X_{\operatorname{callRightOrig}
        (\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o),\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))}}
    =
    \inner{X_{i_-}}{X_{i_+}}
  \]
  only by a broad `simp' call while the right argument remains under a lambda.
  The intended formal proof is: prove the origin equalities as `Fin' equalities,
  derive row equalities by applying congruence to $X.V$, rewrite the
  cross-score definition using those row equalities, and only then handle the
  possible orientation of the original pair using inner-product commutativity.
  All bounds needed to construct the canonical right index are part of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:split-tree-index-arithmetic}. In particular, from
  $\operatorname{canonicalLower}(o)<\operatorname{canonicalUpper}(o)<n$ the
  generated proof must first derive
  \[
    \operatorname{canonicalUpper}(o)
      -(\operatorname{canonicalLower}(o)+1)
      < n-(\operatorname{canonicalLower}(o)+1)
  \]
  and then
  \[
    \operatorname{canonicalLower}(o)+1+
    \bigl(\operatorname{canonicalUpper}(o)
      -(\operatorname{canonicalLower}(o)+1)\bigr)
    =
    \operatorname{canonicalUpper}(o).
  \]
  These are projected arithmetic facts, not tactic guesses. A proof of
  `MinIPSplitCanonical_rightOrig' or
  `MinIPSplitCanonicalScore_eq' that imports `Mathlib.Tactic.Omega' or closes
  the finite-index goals by `omega' does not satisfy this node.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:minip, def:bichromatic-minip, def:inner-prod, lem:split-tree-index-arithmetic}
  The left origin equation is immediate from the definition of the canonical
  call. For the right origin equation, the right child consists exactly of the
  rows whose original indices are strictly larger than $i_-$. Since $o$ is a
  distinct pair, $i_+>i_-$, and the canonical right index is defined as the
  offset $i_+-(i_-+1)$ in this suffix. Thus converting the right-child index
  back to an original index gives $i_+$.

  Applying the row map $X.V$ to the two origin equalities gives equality of the
  actual vectors, and hence coordinatewise equality for every coordinate $r$.
  Expanding the cross-score of the canonical call gives the finite-sum inner
  product of these two transported rows, so the row equalities rewrite it to
  $\inner{X_{i_-}}{X_{i_+}}$. If the original output pair was already ordered
  as $(i_-,i_+)$ this is exactly $\operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(X,o)$; otherwise
  the same score is obtained by commutativity of the finite-sum inner product.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Pair coverage in the Min-IP recursive split tree]
  \label{lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}
  \uses{def:minip, def:bichromatic-minip, lem:minip-canonical-cross-score-transport, lem:split-tree-index-arithmetic}
  Let $V=(v_1,\ldots,v_n)$ be a monochromatic $\MinIP_{n,\ell}$ instance, and
  let $\operatorname{callTree}(V)$ be the finite binary tree obtained by
  recursively splitting every node $U$ with $|U|\ge2$ into two ordered children
  $U_L,U_R$ and stopping only at leaves of size $0$ or $1$. This node records
  the missing global combinatorial invariant behind Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}.

  The declaration audited at this label must expose a package
  $\operatorname{MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage}$ with the following projections.
  First, the tree is a real finite rooted tree, not a per-node helper:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{root}:& V,\\
    \operatorname{children}(U):& (U_L,U_R)\text{ for every internal node }U,\\
    \operatorname{leaf\_iff}:&
      U\text{ is a leaf}\Longleftrightarrow |U|<2,\\
    \operatorname{internalNodes}:&
      \text{the finite set of non-leaf nodes of }\operatorname{callTree}(V),\\
    \operatorname{allCalls}:&
      \{\,\operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R):
         U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}\,\}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The field `allCalls' is a finite family of concrete bichromatic Min-IP target
  instances with their child sizes and vector lists; it is not just the set of
  internal node identifiers.
  The field `internalNodes' is not the set of all sublists, finsets, or subsets
  of $V$ with cardinality at least $2$. It is the image of the actual
  root-to-descendant reachability relation in $\operatorname{callTree}(V)$.
  Trial-14 failure-specific refinement: the audited declaration fails this node
  if, after unfolding the fields of
  $\operatorname{MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage}$, the implementation has
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      =
      \{U:\operatorname{Finset}\operatorname{Row}(V):
        |U|\ge2\}
  \]
  or any variant filtering all finsets, sublists, subsets, masks, or node
  facades by the predicate ``cardinality at least two''.  The accepted
  `MinIPInternalNodes' field is instead the finite set generated by the
  inductive reachability constructors
  `root', `left' and `right', and the package must project the recursive
  leaf/internal equations below.  Similarly,
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
      =\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
  \]
  or any definition whose elements are node identifiers, subproblems, finsets,
  masks, or proofs of internality is rejected.  `MinIPAllCalls(V)' is a finite
  set of concrete dependent target-call records.  Each element $c$ must expose
  `callLeftSize', `callRightSize', `callDim' and
  `callInst(c):\operatorname{BMinIPInst}
  (\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),\operatorname{callRightSize}(c),
  \operatorname{callDim}(c))', and the membership theorem must recover a
  reachable internal node $U$ with
  \[
    c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U),\quad
    \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U),\quad
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R).
  \]
  A package that contains row-origin equations for some calls but omits
  path-carrying reachability, the recursive finite-set equations, parent
  uniqueness, unique cross-call coverage, cross-pair-to-original-pair
  transport, the score-set identity, the optimum identity, or the threshold
  identity is incomplete.  These are required projections of the audited
  declaration itself, not optional external lemmas.
  Trial-15 failure-specific refinement: the package must make the tree,
  concrete call set, and pair-coverage theorem mutually linked by projection
  equations.  The following normalized field shapes are mandatory:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{reachableInternalNodes\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)=
      \{\,U:\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\wedge |U|\ge2\,\},\\
    \operatorname{recursiveAllCalls\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)=
      \{\,\operatorname{nodeCall}(U):
          U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\,\},\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_inst\_eq}:&
      \operatorname{callInst}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))
      =\operatorname{crossInst}(U),\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_eq\_children}:&
      \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R),\\
    \operatorname{uniqueCrossCall\_iff}:&
      \forall W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
      \operatorname{MinIPCrossPair}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(W),p,q)
      \Longleftrightarrow W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{crossPairOrigTransport}:&
      \operatorname{MinIPCrossPair}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U),p,q)
      \to
      (p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)),(p,q))
      =
      \operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These theorem fields are rejected if any right-hand side is a cardinality
  filter over all subobjects, if `MinIPAllCalls' is definitionally the same
  finite set as `MinIPInternalNodes', if `nodeCall' stores only a node id, or
  if `MinIPCrossPair' is a predicate over original pairs that does not mention
  the concrete child-sized call record and its child-sized instance.  The
  score-set, optimum and threshold
  consequences below must be derived from `uniqueCrossCall_iff' and
  `crossPairOrigTransport'; they must not be reflexive statements and must not
  be proved by defining the recursive score/threshold objects to be copies of
  the root original-pair enumeration.
  The package must expose this by a reachability predicate
  \[
    \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)
  \]
  and theorem fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{internalNodes\_iff}:&
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\wedge |U|\ge2,\\
    \operatorname{reachableRoot}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(V),\\
    \operatorname{reachableLeft}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\wedge |U|\ge2
      \to \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U_L),\\
    \operatorname{reachableRight}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\wedge |U|\ge2
      \to \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U_R),\\
    \operatorname{reachableInduction}:&
      \text{the induction principle generated by root, left-child and
      right-child reachability.}
  \end{array}
  \]
  The reachability predicate is an inductive closure of the child relation,
  not a closed-form membership test.  A compliant implementation exposes
  constructors, or transparent theorem fields equivalent to constructors,
  with exactly the following content:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{ReachableNode.root}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(V),\\
    \operatorname{ReachableNode.left}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
      \to \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U_L),\\
    \operatorname{ReachableNode.right}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
      \to \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Its eliminator has the non-vacuous recursive type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{reachableInduction}(Q):\\
    \quad Q(V)\to
    \left(\forall U,\ \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
      \to Q(U)\to Q(U_L)\right)\to\\
    \quad
    \left(\forall U,\ \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
      \to Q(U)\to Q(U_R)\right)\to
    \forall U,\ \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to Q(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The induction field must consume the root case and the two child-step
  hypotheses.  It is explicitly rejected if its type is only
  \[
    (\forall U,\ Q(U))\to
    \forall U,\ \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to Q(U),
  \]
  or any equivalent principle that assumes the desired property for every node
  instead of proving it by recursion from the root.  Likewise,
  $\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)$ may not be defined as
  $U=V\vee |U|\ge2$, as $U\subseteq V$, as membership in all cardinality-filtered
  sublists of $V$, or as any closed-form predicate whose proof terms do not
  record the root-to-$U$ path through left/right child pointers.

  Trial-7 failure-specific refinement: the Lean declaration
  $\operatorname{MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage}$ must make
  $\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V$ an actual path-carrying inductive family, or
  a structure whose constructors and eliminator are definitionally equivalent
  to that inductive family.  The audited package must project the following
  proof-valued fields with these reserved names:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{reachableRoot}:&
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(V),\\
    \operatorname{reachableLeft}:&
      \forall U,\ \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
      \to \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U_L),\\
    \operatorname{reachableRight}:&
      \forall U,\ \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
      \to \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U_R),\\
    \operatorname{reachableInduction}:&
      \forall Q,\ Q(V)\to
      \left(\forall U,\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
        \to Q(U)\to Q(U_L)\right)\to\\
    &\quad
      \left(\forall U,\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to |U|\ge2
        \to Q(U)\to Q(U_R)\right)\to
      \forall U,\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\to Q(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The field `reachableInduction' is rejected if its first premise is
  $\forall U,\ Q(U)$, if it assumes the conclusion for all nodes, if it has no
  separate left-child and right-child step hypotheses, or if
  $\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)$ unfolds to a closed-form predicate such as
  `U is a subproblem of V', `U has cardinality at least two', `U \subseteq V',
  or `U \in MinIPInternalNodes(V)'.  A closed-form predicate plus a theorem
  saying all its members are reachable does not satisfy this node; the
  reachability proof itself must contain the finite sequence of child choices
  from the root to $U$ so that induction can be proved by cases on that path.

  Trial-7 arithmetic refinement: all finite-index witnesses created by this
  node must use the arithmetic package of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:split-tree-index-arithmetic}; they may not depend on
  `Mathlib.Tactic.Omega' or on any generated `by omega' proof. The call-record
  interface must expose proof-valued fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{callParentIndexLt}:&
      \operatorname{splitIndex}(c)<n,\\
    \operatorname{callParentIndexLtSucc}:&
      \operatorname{splitIndex}(c)<n+1,\\
    \operatorname{callRightChildIndexLtSucc}:&
      \operatorname{splitIndex}(c)+1<n+1,\\
    \operatorname{callRightSizeGeOne}:&
      1\le n-(\operatorname{splitIndex}(c)+1),\\
    \operatorname{callParentCardinalityGeTwo}:&
      2\le n-\operatorname{splitIndex}(c),\\
    \operatorname{rightOrigIndexLt}:&
      \forall j<n-(\operatorname{splitIndex}(c)+1),\
      \operatorname{splitIndex}(c)+1+j<n .
  \end{array}
  \]
  These fields are derived directly from
  $\operatorname{hasRightChild}(c):
  \operatorname{splitIndex}(c)+1<n$ and from the parameter proof
  $2\le n$. They are not optional helper lemmas: they are part of the audited
  split-tree package because they justify the `Fin' constructors for the
  parent suffix node, the right-child suffix node, the canonical right index,
  and the transported right-origin index. A generated definition such as
  \[
    \langle\langle0,\ \texttt{by omega}\rangle,\ \texttt{by omega}\rangle
  \]
  for a default call is rejected. If a default call is used at all, its two
  proof fields must be explicitly derived from the source parameter bound
  $2\le n$ by `zeroLtFromTwoLe' and the successor inequality fields above; but
  the preferred compliant construction has no default branch, because
  `nodeCall' is defined only for reachable internal nodes and therefore already
  has the split proof needed to construct the call.

  The statement audited at this label must also include a theorem field
  \[
    \operatorname{internalSuffixHasRightChild}:
      U=\operatorname{suffix}(k)\wedge
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      \Longrightarrow k+1<n .
  \]
  Thus `nodeCall(U)' for an internal suffix node is built from this displayed
  right-child proof. It is not built by case-splitting on an arbitrary node and
  falling back to a default `splitIndex = 0' call in impossible branches. The
  default-branch pattern caused the failed disposable implementation to create
  finite-index obligations with no visible constraints; the blueprint now
  requires the constraints to be fields of the construction itself.

  The same Trial-7 interface reserves the finite-set equations as projections
  of this package, not as external helper facts:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes\_leaf}:&
      \forall U,\ |U|<2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=\varnothing,\\
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes\_internal}:&
      \forall U,\ |U|\ge2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=
      \{U\}\cup\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_L)\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_R),\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls\_leaf}:&
      \forall U,\ |U|<2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U)=\varnothing,\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls\_internal}:&
      \forall U,\ |U|\ge2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U)=
      \{\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\}\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_L)\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These equations must be theorem fields whose right-hand sides syntactically
  mention the two children $U_L,U_R$ returned by $\operatorname{children}(U)$.
  The package fails this node if `MinIPInternalNodes' is defined by filtering
  all sublists/finsets/subsets by cardinality, if the internal-node equation is
  $\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=\{U\}$, if `MinIPAllCalls' is a
  singleton root call, or if `MinIPAllCalls' has elements that are node
  identifiers rather than concrete $\operatorname{nodeCall}$ records.

  Finally, the parent and child-membership interface is mandatory at this
  label.  The package must contain projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{leftInternalNode\_mem}:&
      \forall U,W,\ W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_L)\to
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U),\\
    \operatorname{rightInternalNode\_mem}:&
      \forall U,W,\ W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_R)\to
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U),\\
    \operatorname{leftCall\_mem}:&
      \forall U,c,\ c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_L)\to
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U),\\
    \operatorname{rightCall\_mem}:&
      \forall U,c,\ c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_R)\to
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U),\\
    \operatorname{parentOfNonRoot}:&
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\to U\ne V\to
      \exists W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
        U=W_L\vee U=W_R,\\
    \operatorname{parentUnique}:&
      U\ne V\to
      (U=W_L\vee U=W_R)\to (U=W'_L\vee U=W'_R)\to W=W'.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These fields must be obtained from the recursive equations and the
  path-carrying reachability induction.  A declaration where
  `parentOfNonRoot' is absent, where parent uniqueness is only $W=W$, or where
  child membership is proved by a broad cardinality-filter inclusion has not
  provided the global recursive split-tree invariant required for
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}.

  The same audited package must expose the recursive equations tying
  reachability to the finite node and call sets:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{internalNodes\_leaf}:&
      |U|<2\to \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=\varnothing,\\
    \operatorname{internalNodes\_internal}:&
      |U|\ge2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=
      \{U\}\cup\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_L)\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_R),\\
    \operatorname{allCalls\_leaf}:&
      |U|<2\to \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U)=\varnothing,\\
    \operatorname{allCalls\_internal}:&
      |U|\ge2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U)=
      \{\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\}\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_L)\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These four fields are required at this label, even if analogous facts are
  available for a helper tree type.  A declaration whose
  $\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}$ is closed-form and merely proves
  `internalNodes_iff' from that predicate, without the four recursive
  leaf/internal equations above, does not satisfy the node.  The recursive
  equations must mention the actual children returned by
  $\operatorname{children}(U)$ and, for `allCalls_internal', the concrete
  $\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)$ record.

  Parent information is also part of the interface, so that internal-node
  membership cannot be faked by a cardinality filter.  The package has
  proof-valued projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{parentOfNonRoot}:&
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\to U\ne V\to
      \exists W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
        (U=W_L\vee U=W_R),\\
    \operatorname{parentUnique}:&
      U\ne V\to
      (U=W_L\vee U=W_R)\to (U=W'_L\vee U=W'_R)\to
      W=W',\\
    \operatorname{leftInternalNode\_mem}:&
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_L)\to
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U),\\
    \operatorname{rightInternalNode\_mem}:&
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_R)\to
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U),\\
    \operatorname{leftCall\_mem}:&
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_L)\to
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U),\\
    \operatorname{rightCall\_mem}:&
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_R)\to
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are theorem fields, not stored propositions.  The
  `parentOfNonRoot' and `parentUnique' conclusions must mention the immediate
  children of the candidate parents; a proof that every non-root node has some
  ancestor, or a uniqueness theorem of the form $W=W$, is not enough.
  Here $U_L,U_R$ are the children returned by the package's own
  $\operatorname{children}(U)$ field. A definition such as
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      :=\{U\subseteq V: |U|\ge2\}
  \]
  or, in Lean, a finite set of all finsets of cardinality at least two, fails
  this node even if it satisfies a cardinality filter: it contains subsets that
  are not reachable by the recursive halving tree and omits the child-pointer
  structure needed for the unique-cross-call proof.
  The package must also expose nontrivial negative/uniqueness information
  ruling this out, for example
  \[
    U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
    \Longrightarrow
    U=V\ \vee\
    \exists W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
      U=W_L\ \vee\ U=W_R,
  \]
  and the parent in this last display is the unique immediate parent of $U$
  unless $U=V$. These fields force membership to arise by recursion from the
  root, not merely by satisfying $|U|\ge2$.
  The concrete call object associated to a reachable internal node is likewise
  fixed. The package must define
  \[
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)
      =
      (U_L,U_R)
      :\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell),
  \]
  with projection equations
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{crossInst\_leftRows}(U):&
      \operatorname{leftRows}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U))=U_L,\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_rightRows}(U):&
      \operatorname{rightRows}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U))=U_R,\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_leftSize}(U):&
      \operatorname{leftSize}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U))=|U_L|,\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_rightSize}(U):&
      \operatorname{rightSize}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U))=|U_R|,\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_score}(U,p,q):&
      \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U),p,q)
      =
      \inner{(U_L)_p}{(U_R)_q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Therefore `crossInst' must depend on the particular split node $U$ through
  its own children. A definition
  \[
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U):=(V,V)
  \]
  or any definition whose left and right rows are the full root instance
  independently of $U$ is explicitly rejected. For every non-root reachable
  internal node $U$, the package must prove at least one of
  $\operatorname{leftRows}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U))\ne V$ or
  $\operatorname{rightRows}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U))\ne V$ unless the
  corresponding child is genuinely the whole root by the child equations,
  which cannot occur in a strict recursive split.
  Finally, `allCalls' is the finite set of these dependent call records:
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
      =
      \left\{
        (|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U)):
        U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      \right\}.
  \]
  The package must expose both directions of membership:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{allCalls\_mem\_iff}:&
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
      c=(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U)),\\
    \operatorname{allCalls\_call\_mem}:&
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\to
      (|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U))
      \in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V).
  \end{array}
  \]
  A field whose type is only a set of node identifiers, or a set of pairs
  $(U,\operatorname{internalProof})$, is not `allCalls' for this node. Every
  element of `allCalls' must be directly callable by the bichromatic Min-IP
  algorithm through the concrete target family of
  Definition~\ref{def:bichromatic-minip}.
  The declaration audited at this label must therefore include the concrete
  call-record type used by `allCalls'.  A call record has projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{callNode}(c) &: \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callRightSize}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callDim}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callInst}(c) &: 
      \operatorname{BMinIPInst}
        (\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callDim}(c)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  For the call generated by a reachable internal node $U$, the package must
  expose the defining equations
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{callNode\_eq}(U):&
      \operatorname{callNode}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=U,\\
    \operatorname{callLeftSize\_eq}(U):&
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=|U_L|,\\
    \operatorname{callRightSize\_eq}(U):&
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=|U_R|,\\
    \operatorname{callDim\_eq}(U):&
      \operatorname{callDim}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=\ell,\\
    \operatorname{callInst\_eq}(U):&
      \operatorname{callInst}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))
      =\operatorname{crossInst}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The finite set `MinIPAllCalls(V)' is a set of these call records, not a set
  of nodes, and
  \[
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U).
  \]
  This makes the target oracle call recoverable from every member of
  `allCalls' without consulting an external helper. A Lean implementation whose
  `MinIPAllCalls' has element type `MinIPNode', `Finset MinIPNode',
  `Subtype MinIPInternalNodes', or any other node-identifier type does not
  satisfy the declaration, even if a later function maps such identifiers to
  target instances.
  The package must also prove that the call instance varies with the split
  node:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_leftRows}(U):&
      \operatorname{leftRows}(\operatorname{callInst}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)))
      =U_L,\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_rightRows}(U):&
      \operatorname{rightRows}(\operatorname{callInst}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)))
      =U_R.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These equations are required for arbitrary reachable internal $U$, not only
  for the root. If the generated `crossInst' or `nodeCall' ignores $U$, or if
  `crossInst U' is definitionally the root call $(V,V)$, then the equations for
  non-root internal nodes are false and the statement audit must reject the
  implementation.
  More explicitly, `internalNodes' and `allCalls' are global tree-level
  projections. They must be defined by recursion over the whole tree:
  \[
    \operatorname{internalNodes}(V)
      =
      \{V\}\cup\operatorname{internalNodes}(V_L)\cup
      \operatorname{internalNodes}(V_R)
      \quad\text{when }|V|\ge2,
  \]
  and
  \[
    \operatorname{allCalls}(V)
      =
      \{\operatorname{nodeCall}(V)\}\cup
      \operatorname{allCalls}(V_L)\cup
      \operatorname{allCalls}(V_R)
      \quad\text{when }|V|\ge2,
  \]
  with both sets empty at leaves. The package must expose these equations as
  theorem fields, for example `internalNodes_leaf',
  `internalNodes_internal', `allCalls_leaf', and `allCalls_internal'. A
  declaration such as
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)=
      \begin{cases}
        \{V\} & |V|\ge2,\\
        \varnothing & |V|<2
      \end{cases}
  \]
  is root-only and is rejected. Likewise,
  `allCalls V = \{\operatorname{nodeCall}(V)\}' for an internal root omits all
  recursive cross calls and is not the field required by this node. Every
  non-root internal node reached by recursively following left or right child
  pointers must occur in `internalNodes', and its concrete cross instance
  $(U_L,U_R)$ with child sizes must occur in `allCalls'.
  The reserved Lean names used for these projections have fixed types. The
  package must expose
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes\_leaf}(U):&
      |U|<2\to \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=\varnothing,\\
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes\_internal}(U):&
      |U|\ge2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U)=
      \{U\}\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_L)\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_R),\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls\_leaf}(U):&
      |U|<2\to \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U)=\varnothing,\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls\_internal}(U):&
      |U|\ge2\to
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U)=
      \{\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\}\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_L)\cup
      \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here $U_L,U_R$ are the actual children returned by
  $\operatorname{children}(U)$, and $\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)$ is the call
  record whose $\operatorname{callInst}$ is the concrete bichromatic instance
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R)$ with its child cardinalities and
  rows. A theorem named `MinIPInternalNodes_internal' whose right-hand side is
  just $\{U\}$, or a theorem named `MinIPAllCalls_internal' whose right-hand
  side is just $\{\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\}$, is not a weakened version of
  this node; it is a different root-only construction. The audited declaration
  must also contain membership introduction fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{leftInternalNode\_mem}:&
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_L)\to
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U),\\
    \operatorname{rightInternalNode\_mem}:&
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U_R)\to
      W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(U),\\
    \operatorname{leftCall\_mem}:&
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_L)\to
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U),\\
    \operatorname{rightCall\_mem}:&
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U_R)\to
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These fields rule out a singleton-root definition even when the recursive
  equations are hidden behind helper names.
  To rule out cardinality-filtered substitutes, the recursive equations are not
  optional documentation: they are the definitional interface for the finite
  sets. In particular, the theorem
  `MinIPInternalNodes_internal(U)' must name the two children returned by
  `children(U)' on its right-hand side, and the theorem
  `MinIPAllCalls_internal(U)' must name
  `nodeCall(U)', `MinIPAllCalls(U_L)', and `MinIPAllCalls(U_R)' on its
  right-hand side. A proof that every member merely has cardinality at least
  $2$, or a definition by filtering all finsets of rows of $V$ by cardinality,
  cannot be coerced into this interface. The package also has exclusion fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{internalNodes\_reachableOnly}:&
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\to
      \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U),\\
    \operatorname{allCalls\_concreteOnly}:&
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)\to
      \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
        c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\wedge
        \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The first field rules out the set of all cardinality-$\ge2$ finsets; the
  second rules out call collections made only of node identifiers.

  Trial-8 failure-specific refinement: the audited declaration must reject the
  exact weakened package shape in which `internalNodes' is just a
  leaf/cardinality filter and `allCalls' is a universe of predeclared calls.
  The following normalized definitions are not acceptable, even if they are
  wrapped in a structure named `MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage':
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      :=\{U:\ |U|\ge2\}
      \quad\text{or}\quad
      \{U:\operatorname{Leaf}(U)=\mathrm{false}\wedge |U|\ge2\},\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V):=\mathrm{Finset.univ}
      \text{ over a type such as }\operatorname{MinIPSplitAllCalls}(V),\\
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
      \Longleftrightarrow c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\\
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
      \Longleftrightarrow c\in\mathrm{Finset.univ}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  In particular, a membership theorem named `allCalls_mem_iff' or
  `MinIPSplitAllCalls_mem_iff' must not be a tautology and must not reduce to
  membership in `Finset.univ'. Its required type is the concrete
  reconstruction theorem
  \[
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U,\ 
      U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\ \wedge\
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callDim}(c)=\ell .
  \]
  The existential witness $U$ must be a reachable internal node of the actual
  recursive tree, and the call instance must be the child-sized bichromatic
  instance $(U_L,U_R)$. A finite call type whose inhabitants are generated
  independently of the tree, such as a global inductive or enum named
  `MinIPSplitAllCalls', is permitted only if every inhabitant carries these
  projections and the displayed iff recovers a reachable internal node and its
  concrete child-sized call. Otherwise `Finset.univ' supplies all calls by type
  inhabitance rather than by recursive reachability, which is exactly the
  skipped argument this node is meant to prevent.

  For each original distinct pair $(p,q)$ in $V$, the package contains its
  lowest split node:
  \[
    \operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)\in\operatorname{internalNodes}
  \]
  The value of `splitNode' is not allowed to be constantly the root. It is the
  lowest common ancestor of the two singleton leaves containing $p$ and $q$ in
  the recursive tree, equivalently the unique internal node $U$ such that $p$
  and $q$ both lie in $U$, but they lie in different children $U_L$ and $U_R$.
  The witness therefore contains path and lowest-split projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{leafOfIndex}(p):&
      \text{the unique leaf containing the original row }p,\\
    \operatorname{pathToLeaf}(p):&
      \text{the root-to-}\operatorname{leafOfIndex}(p)\text{ path},\\
    \operatorname{splitNode\_contains}(p,q):&
      p,q\in\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{splitNode\_cross}(p,q):&
      (p\in U_L\wedge q\in U_R)\vee
      (p\in U_R\wedge q\in U_L)
      \quad\text{for }U=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{splitNode\_lowest}(p,q):&
      \text{every strict descendant of }U
      \text{ contains at most one of }p,q.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are proof-valued fields about the recursively defined tree. A
  definition `splitNode p q := root' fails this node unless it also proves that
  the root is the lowest split node for the particular pair, which is false for
  pairs separated only in a lower recursive subproblem.
  It also contains a proof-valued field
  \[
    \operatorname{pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall}(p,q):
    p\ne q\Longrightarrow
    \begin{cases}
      p\in U_L,\ q\in U_R\ \text{or}\ p\in U_R,\ q\in U_L,\\
      U=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),\\
      \text{no other internal node has }(p,q)\text{ as a cross pair.}
    \end{cases}
  \]
  This field has a non-tautological dependent type. After unfolding, its
  conclusion must mention the concrete node
  $U=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$, the concrete children $U_L,U_R$, the
  membership of $p$ and $q$ in opposite children, and a uniqueness statement
  over all $W\in\operatorname{internalNodes}(V)$:
  \[
    \operatorname{CrossPair}_W(p,q)
    \Longleftrightarrow W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q).
  \]
  A field that stores only the original-pair fact $p\ne q$, or proves only a
  uniqueness condition of the form $W=W$, does not assert that the pair appears
  in a cross oracle call and is rejected.
  More concretely, the field named `pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall' has a
  dependent conclusion whose projections are proof fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{pairSplitNodeMem}:&
      \operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)\in
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{pairOppositeChildren}:&
      \operatorname{CrossPair}_{\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)}(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{pairCrossIff}:&
      \forall W\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
      \operatorname{CrossPair}_{W}(p,q)
      \Longleftrightarrow W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{pairCallMem}:&
      \operatorname{crossInst}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))
      \in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The implication direction
  $\operatorname{CrossPair}_{W}(p,q)\Rightarrow
  W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$ must be proved from the tree paths and the
  lowest-split theorem, not assumed as a hypothesis of the same shape. A proof
  package whose uniqueness component has type
  $W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)\to
  W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$, or whose only nontrivial content is
  `pairSplitNodeMem', fails this node. The constant definition
  `splitNode p q := root' can satisfy `pairCrossIff' only for pairs separated
  at the root; since the field is required for every original distinct pair, it
  is rejected unless it proves the displayed lowest-split facts for that pair.
  Conversely every cross pair in every call is an original distinct pair:
  \[
    \operatorname{crossPair\_to\_origPair}(U,p,q):
    p\in U_L\wedge q\in U_R
    \Longrightarrow (p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V).
  \]
  This theorem must return the concrete original-pair data:
  both endpoints are original indices of the root instance $V$, the two root
  rows are distinct, and the transported score is the same root score:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    p,q\in\operatorname{Rows}(V),\qquad p\ne q,\\
    \operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q)
      =
      \inner{\operatorname{row}_U(p)}{\operatorname{row}_U(q)}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Returning only the fact that $U$ is internal, or only that the cross instance
  is well-formed, is not enough; it does not connect a cross oracle pair to the
  original Min-IP search space.
  The reserved field `crossPair_to_origPair' must return a structure, or an
  equivalent dependent tuple, with projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{origLeftIndex}:&
      p\in\operatorname{Rows}(V),\\
    \operatorname{origRightIndex}:&
      q\in\operatorname{Rows}(V),\\
    \operatorname{origDistinct}:&
      p\ne q,\\
    \operatorname{origPairMem}:&
      (p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V),\\
    \operatorname{origScoreTransport}:&
      \operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q)=
      \inner{\operatorname{row}_{U}(p)}
             {\operatorname{row}_{U}(q)}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The hypothesis must identify $U$ as a member of
  $\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)$ and $(p,q)$ as a concrete cross pair
  of the split $U_L,U_R$. A field returning only
  $U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)$, or only a proof that $U$ is
  internal, has none of the original-pair data needed for the reduction.
  These two fields give the disjoint-union equation
  \[
    \operatorname{OrigPair}(V)
    =
    \bigsqcup_{U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}}
      \operatorname{CrossPair}(U).
  \]
  A statement that only says every node can be split, or only defines
  `CrossPair' locally, does not satisfy this node.

  The package then derives the score-set identity for the original root:
  \[
    \{\inner{v_p}{v_q}:p\ne q\}
    =
    \bigcup_{U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}}
      \{\inner{x}{y}:x\in U_L,\ y\in U_R\},
  \]
  as a theorem field named, or transparently equivalent to, `scoreSetIdentity'.
  Its left-hand side must be the set of scores of original distinct pairs at the
  root; its right-hand side must be the union over
  `internalNodes (callTree V)' of scores of the concrete cross instances in
  `allCalls'. It is rejected if both sides unfold to the same helper expression,
  if the right-hand side ranges only over the root call, or if the theorem is
  proved by reflexivity after defining the left-hand side to be the right-hand
  side. The proof must use `pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall' for the forward
  inclusion and `crossPair_to_origPair' for the reverse inclusion.
  To make this syntactic, the package must define two separate expressions
  \[
    \operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)
      :=
      \{\operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q):(p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)\}
  \]
  and
  \[
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V)
      :=
      \bigcup_{U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)}
      \{\operatorname{crossScore}_{U}(p,q):
        \operatorname{CrossPair}_{U}(p,q)\}.
  \]
  The theorem field has the exact shape
  \[
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity}(V):
      \operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)=
      \operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V).
  \]
  The two definitions above are not allowed to be aliases for each other.
  `RootScoreSet' must unfold to the original distinct-pair scores of
  Definition~\ref{def:minip}; `RecursiveCrossScoreSet' must unfold to the
  finite union over all recursive cross calls. If either side is defined by
  copying the other side, then a reflexive proof of `scoreSetIdentity' is
  rejected. The witness should instead expose proof fields
  `scoreSetIdentity_forward' and `scoreSetIdentity_reverse' using respectively
  `pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall' and `crossPair_to_origPair'.
  The package also exposes the corresponding minimum and threshold consequences:
  \[
    \operatorname{origOpt}(V)
    =
    \min_{U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}}m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),
  \]
  \[
    \operatorname{origThresholdYes}(V,t)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U\in\operatorname{internalNodes},\
      \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U).
  \]
  The fields for these consequences, for example `optimumIdentity' and
  `thresholdIdentity', must be derived from `scoreSetIdentity' and the
  disjoint-union coverage. `thresholdIdentity' has the displayed type with
  `origThresholdYes(V,t)' on the left and a real existential over recursive
  cross calls on the right. It is explicitly rejected if its type normalizes to
  `origThresholdYes(V,t) \Longleftrightarrow origThresholdYes(V,t)', to
  `CrossYes_t(root) \Longleftrightarrow CrossYes_t(root)', or to an iff between
  two names that were both defined as the same disjunction over cross calls.
  Similarly, `scoreSetIdentity' may not be
  `scoreSetIdentity : S = S', and the optimum consequence may not be
  `origOpt(V)=origOpt(V)'. The left-hand objects must unfold to the original
  Min-IP semantics from Definition~\ref{def:minip}, while the right-hand
  objects unfold to the finite union/minimum/existential over the recursive
  cross-call family.
  These are theorem fields about the original Min-IP semantics of
  Definition~\ref{def:minip}. They may not be proved by defining
  $\operatorname{origOpt}$ or $\operatorname{origThresholdYes}$ to be the right
  hand side. This is the argument that the recursive oracle calls cover all and
  only the pairs of the original instance.
  The threshold field has a similarly fixed non-reflexive form. The package
  defines
  \[
    \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)
      :=
      \exists (p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V),\
        \operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q)\le t
  \]
  and
  \[
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t)
      :=
      \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
        \exists (p,q),\
          \operatorname{CrossPair}_{U}(p,q)\wedge
          \operatorname{crossScore}_{U}(p,q)\le t.
  \]
  The theorem field is
  \[
    \operatorname{thresholdIdentity}(V,t):
      \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t).
  \]
  `RootThresholdYes' must unfold to the original existential over distinct
  root pairs, while `RecursiveCrossThresholdYes' must unfold to the existential
  over $\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)$ and concrete cross pairs. They
  may not both be abbreviations for the same disjunction. The accepted proof of
  `thresholdIdentity' maps an original witness $(p,q)$ to the cross call at
  $\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$ using
  `pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall', and maps a recursive cross witness back to an
  original pair using `crossPair_to_origPair'. A theorem of type
  $P\Longleftrightarrow P$, even when $P$ is a helper predicate whose name
  mentions thresholds, does not satisfy this field.

  Trial-7/13 failure-specific refinement: the following Lean names, used by the
  disposable implementations, have reserved meanings at this label. If present,
  `MinIPInternalNodes' must be the complete recursive finite set described by
  `internalNodes_leaf', `internalNodes_internal', and
  `internalNodes_iff', not a root-only set and not the cardinality-filtered set
  of all finsets or sublists of $V$ with size at least two.
  `allCalls' must be the complete recursive finite set of concrete
  $\operatorname{BMinIP}$ calls described by `allCalls_leaf' and
  `allCalls_internal' and by the membership equivalence
  `allCalls_mem_iff'; it is not a singleton root call and not a set of node
  identifiers. `crossInst' must unfold to the child instance $(U_L,U_R)$ of the
  particular split node $U$, with the left/right row, size and score equations
  `crossInst_leftRows', `crossInst_rightRows',
  `crossInst_leftSize', `crossInst_rightSize', and `crossInst_score'. A
  `crossInst' that ignores $U$ and uses the full root instance $V$ on both
  sides fails the statement audit. `splitNode' must be the
  lowest split node of the pair and must satisfy `splitNode_cross' and
  `splitNode_lowest'. `pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall' must have a conclusion
  containing opposite-child membership and
  $\operatorname{CrossPair}_W(p,q)\Longleftrightarrow
  W=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$. `crossPair_to_origPair' must output a
  concrete member of $\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)$, including $p\ne q$, not
  merely an internal-node proof. `scoreSetIdentity' and `thresholdIdentity'
  must be the non-reflexive root-versus-recursive-call statements displayed
  above. Any implementation in which these names unfold to root-only
  definitions, constant root `splitNode', tautological uniqueness, an
  internal-node-only conclusion, or reflexive equalities/iff statements fails
  this blueprint node even if other abstract reduction fields are present.
  Trial-2 failure-specific refinement: a Lean declaration satisfying only a
  weakened interface named `MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage' is not enough. The
  audited structure must have projections with the exact mathematical roles
  listed in this node:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{ReachableNode}:&
      \text{inductive root/left/right reachability in }\operatorname{callTree}(V),\\
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}:&
      \{U:\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\wedge |U|\ge2\},\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall}:&
      U\mapsto (|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U)),\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}:&
      \{\operatorname{nodeCall}(U):U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\},\\
    \operatorname{crossInst}:&
      U\mapsto(U_L,U_R)
        :\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{splitNode}:&
      (p,q)\mapsto\text{the lowest reachable internal node whose children
      separate }p\text{ and }q,\\
    \operatorname{pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall}:&
      \text{opposite-child membership at }\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)
      \text{ and uniqueness among all reachable internal nodes},\\
    \operatorname{crossPair\_to\_origPair}:&
      \text{a concrete original distinct pair with score transport},\\
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity}:&
      \operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)=
      \operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V),\\
    \operatorname{optimumIdentity}:&
      \operatorname{origOpt}(V)=
      \min_{U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)}m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\\
    \operatorname{thresholdIdentity}:&
      \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)\Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Each line is a projection or theorem field of the audited declaration itself.
  It is not acceptable to provide a structure with unrelated fields whose names
  suggest these concepts while their normalized types are cardinality filters,
  node-id sets, root calls, or tautologies. The following normalized shapes are
  specifically rejected:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      =\{U:\operatorname{Rows}(U)\subseteq\operatorname{Rows}(V)
          \wedge |U|\ge2\},\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
      =\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)
      =(\operatorname{Rows}(V),\operatorname{Rows}(V)),\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_score}(U,p,q)
      =\inner{v_p}{v_q}
      \text{ with }p,q\text{ indexing the root rows rather than }U_L,U_R,\\
    \operatorname{pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall}(p,q)
      \text{ lacking }\operatorname{pairOppositeChildren}
      \text{ or }\operatorname{pairCallMem},\\
    \operatorname{crossPair\_to\_origPair}(U,p,q)
      \text{ lacking }\operatorname{origDistinct}
      \text{ or }\operatorname{origScoreTransport},\\
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity}:S=S,\quad
    \operatorname{optimumIdentity}:m=m,\quad
    \operatorname{thresholdIdentity}:P\Longleftrightarrow P .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The generator must therefore construct the reachable recursive tree first,
  then derive calls and pair coverage from that tree. It cannot satisfy this
  node by selecting all sufficiently large finsets of rows, by using the full
  root instance as every cross call, or by replacing the score/optimum/threshold
  consequences with reflexive statements.
  In particular, the rejected trial shapes are:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)=\{V\}
      \text{ for every internal root }V,\\
    \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)=
      \{U\subseteq V: |U|\ge2\}
      \text{ or any cardinality-only filter over all finsets/sublists},\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCallsRoot}(V)=
      \{\operatorname{crossInst}(V)\}
      \text{ with no recursive child calls},\\
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)=
      \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)
      \text{ or any set whose elements are node identifiers rather than }
      (|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U))
      \text{ target calls},\\
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(V,V)
      \text{ or any target instance independent of }U
      \text{ and its children }U_L,U_R,\\
    \operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)=\operatorname{MinIPRootSplitNode}(V)
      \text{ for every }p\ne q,\\
    \operatorname{pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall}
      \text{ proving only }
      N=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)\to
      N=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{crossPair\_to\_origPair}
      \text{ returning only }N.\operatorname{internal},\\
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity}:
      \operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)=\operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V),\\
    \operatorname{thresholdIdentity}:
      \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)\Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Any future implementation with these normalized types fails the statement
  audit, regardless of surrounding comments or separately asserted abstract
  reduction fields.

  Trial-3 failure-specific refinement: the declaration named
  $\operatorname{MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage}$ must not satisfy this node by
  presenting a split tree facade while encoding the oracle calls at the root
  size with masks. The target call associated to an internal node $U$ is the
  actual child-sized bichromatic instance
  \[
    \operatorname{nodeCall}(U)
      =
      (|U_L|,\ |U_R|,\ \ell,\ \operatorname{crossInst}(U)),
    \qquad
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R).
  \]
  Its instance type is
  $\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell)$, or the equivalent dependent
  target-call type used by Definition~\ref{def:bichromatic-minip}. It is not
  an instance of $\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n,n,\ell)$ whose rows are the root
  rows together with Boolean masks, inactive dummy rows, sentinel values, or
  predicates selecting the active children. If a formalization uses padding to
  fit an equal-size target family, the padding must be an explicit separate
  construction with row equations, dummy-row score bounds, and a theorem that
  the padded optimum/threshold is identical to the child-sized cross problem.
  Without that padding theorem, a root-sized masked call is rejected.

  Consequently, `allCalls' has element type a concrete target-call record, not
  a subtype of internal nodes and not a record whose only payload is a node id.
  Trial-3 failure-specific refinement, sharpened: if the Lean implementation
  uses a structure named `MinIPCallRecord', then that structure itself must
  carry the target-call payload. Its non-proof projections must include
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{callNode}(c) &: \operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\\
    \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callRightSize}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callDim}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callInst}(c) &: 
      \operatorname{BMinIPInst}
        (\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callDim}(c)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The declaration is rejected if `MinIPCallRecord' stores only `callNode',
  even if later external functions can compute sizes or an instance from that
  node. Pattern matching on a call record, or unfolding its transparent Sigma
  representation, must expose the child-sized target parameter and the
  concrete target instance as data of that same element. The canonical element
  has the definitional tuple shape
  \[
    \operatorname{nodeCall}(U)
      =
      \left\langle
        U,\ |U_L|,\ |U_R|,\ \ell,\ \operatorname{crossInst}(U),
        \operatorname{nodeCall\_inst}(U)
      \right\rangle,
  \]
  where $\operatorname{crossInst}(U):\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell)$
  is the concrete instance $(U_L,U_R)$. A record whose only data field is
  `callNode' and whose remaining fields are propositions, theorem fields, or
  opaque computed projections is not a concrete oracle-call record for this
  node.
  Projecting an element $c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)$ must immediately
  recover
  \[
    \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callDim}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callInst}(c),
  \]
  with a proof
  \[
    \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\quad
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)
      \wedge
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U)
      \wedge
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|
      \wedge
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|.
  \]
  A later map from a node record to a call is insufficient: the finite oracle
  call set itself must be directly consumable by the bichromatic Min-IP
  algorithm. In particular, implementations where `allCalls' is a subtype such
  as
  \[
    \{U // U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\}
  \]
  or a structure containing only `callNode' plus proof fields fail this node
  unless the same element also stores the child-sized target parameter and
  target instance as projections satisfying the equations above.
  The membership theorem must also recover those projections:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\\
    \qquad
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callDim}(c)=\ell\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  A theorem of the weaker form
  $c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)\Longleftrightarrow
  \exists U,\ c.\operatorname{callNode}=U$ is rejected, because it proves only
  that calls are node wrappers and does not expose a target oracle instance.

  The uniqueness theorem is likewise about cross-pair membership across all
  recursive calls, not about uniqueness of a synthetically chosen call value.
  For every original pair $o=(p,q)$ with $p\ne q$, the required field
  `unique\_cross\_call' or `pairAppearsInUniqueCrossCall' has the non-tautological
  form
  \[
    \exists! c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
      \operatorname{CrossPair}_{\operatorname{callInst}(c)}(p,q),
  \]
  together with the equation identifying this unique call with
  $\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$. The predicate
  $\operatorname{CrossPair}_{\operatorname{callInst}(c)}(p,q)$ must unfold to
  the assertion that the original endpoints $p,q$ occur in opposite child lists
  of the concrete call instance $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$, after transporting
  them along the row-origin maps of that call. The rejected type
  \[
    \exists! c,\ c=\operatorname{lowestSplitCall}(o)
  \]
  proves only uniqueness of equality to a chosen value and says nothing about
  whether $o$ appears as a cross pair in any oracle call. Such a theorem fails
  even if the chosen value is later called `lowestSplitCall'.
  If the implementation uses a predicate named `MinIPCrossPair', its definition
  must be independent of $\operatorname{splitNode}$. For a concrete call record
  $c$ and original endpoints $p,q$, the accepted definition is
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{MinIPCrossPair}(c,p,q)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists i:\operatorname{Fin}(\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)),\
    \exists j:\operatorname{Fin}(\operatorname{callRightSize}(c)),\\
    \qquad
      \Bigl(
        \operatorname{callLeftOrig}(c,i)=p\ \wedge\
        \operatorname{callRightOrig}(c,j)=q
      \Bigr)
      \vee
      \Bigl(
        \operatorname{callLeftOrig}(c,i)=q\ \wedge\
        \operatorname{callRightOrig}(c,j)=p
      \Bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Equivalently, it may use row-origin maps for
  $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$, but it must mention the concrete call record
  $c$, the left and right call indices, and the two origin equations. It must
  not unfold to
  $c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$, to
  $U=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$, to
  $\operatorname{canonicalCall}(p,q)=c$, or to any predicate over the original
  pair alone. The theorem `uniqueCrossCall_iff' must then have the audited
  shape
  \[
    \forall c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\quad
      \operatorname{MinIPCrossPair}(c,p,q)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)),
  \]
  where the left-hand side is the concrete cross-pair membership predicate just
  described. A theorem whose left-hand side is already
  $c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$, or whose proof is
  an iff between two equalities to the chosen call, is tautological and fails
  this node.

  The score and threshold objects must be built from the recursive call set,
  not from a second copy of the original pair enumeration. The package must
  expose the definitions
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V)
      &=
      \displaystyle
      \bigcup_{c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)}
      \{\operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o):
        \operatorname{CrossOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)\},\\[2mm]
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t)
      &\Longleftrightarrow
      \displaystyle
      \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
      \exists o:\operatorname{CrossOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
        \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)\le t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  These right-hand sides must mention `MinIPAllCalls', `callInst', and the
  concrete bichromatic score of the call. They may not be aliases for canonical
  original-pair sets such as
  $\{\operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q):(p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)\}$, and
  they may not be defined by transporting every original pair through a
  canonical map before the pair-coverage theorem is proved. The theorem
  `scoreSetIdentity' is exactly the proof that this recursive-call score set
  equals the root score set; `thresholdIdentity' is exactly the proof that the
  recursive-call threshold existential equals the original threshold
  existential. If either side of those theorems unfolds to the same canonical
  original-pair expression, the implementation has assumed the desired pair
  coverage instead of proving it and fails this node.
  The normalized definitions are required to have membership/iff theorems
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    s\in\operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
    \exists o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
      s=\operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o),\\[1mm]
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
    \exists o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
      \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)\le t .
  \end{array}
  \]
  These statements are rejected if the right-hand side contains
  $\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)$, $\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)$,
  $\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)$,
  $\operatorname{MinIPSplitCanonicalCall}$, or
  $\operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(V,o)$ in place of a quantified concrete call
  $c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)$ and a concrete bichromatic output
  $o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c))$. The canonical
  split-call transport from Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-canonical-cross-score-transport}
  is allowed only inside the proof of the forward inclusion of
  `scoreSetIdentity'; it is not allowed in the definition of
  $\operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}$ or
  $\operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}$.
  In particular, the following normalized shapes fail this node:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V)
      =
      \{\operatorname{BMinIPScore}
        (\operatorname{crossInst}(V,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
         (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o))):
        o\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)\},\\
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists o\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V),\
        \operatorname{BMinIPScore}
          (\operatorname{crossInst}(V,\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)),
           (0,\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)))\le t .
  \end{array}
  \]
  These formulas enumerate original pairs with a canonical call per pair; they
  do not range over the finite recursive oracle-call set and therefore assume
  the coverage theorem that this node is supposed to prove.

  In short, the accepted implementation order is:
  build reachable nodes; build child-sized concrete calls from reachable
  internal nodes; prove every original pair appears in the unique concrete
  cross call determined by its lowest split node; prove every concrete cross
  call output transports back to an original distinct pair; only then derive
  `scoreSetIdentity', `optimumIdentity', and `thresholdIdentity'. Any
  implementation that replaces this order by root-size masks, node-subtype
  call sets, tautological uniqueness, or canonical original-pair definitions of
  the recursive score/threshold objects does not satisfy
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}.

  Trial-4 failure-specific refinement: the audited Lean declaration must make
  the recursive call interface itself impossible to satisfy with root-sized
  masked calls or node-only records. The package
  $\operatorname{MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage}$ has a dependent call-record
  projection, or an equivalent Sigma type, with exactly the semantic shape
  \[
    \operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V :=
    \sum_{U:\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)}
    \sum_{n_L,n_R:\N}
    \sum_{\ell':\N}
      \operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n_L,n_R,\ell').
  \]
  For the canonical call generated by an internal node $U$, the projection
  equations are theorem fields of this same package:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_node}(U) &: \operatorname{callNode}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=U,\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_leftSize}(U) &: \operatorname{callLeftSize}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=|U_L|,\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_rightSize}(U) &: \operatorname{callRightSize}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=|U_R|,\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_dim}(U) &: \operatorname{callDim}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))=\ell,\\
    \operatorname{nodeCall\_inst}(U) &: \operatorname{callInst}(\operatorname{nodeCall}(U))
      =\operatorname{crossInst}(U),\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_type}(U) &: \operatorname{crossInst}(U):
      \operatorname{BMinIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell),\\
    \operatorname{crossInst\_rows}(U) &: \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Thus the type of $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$ must depend on
  $\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)$ and $\operatorname{callRightSize}(c)$.
  A structure whose call instance always has type
  $\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n,n,\ell)$, even if it stores masks, active-row
  predicates, row-origin functions, or dummy-row promises, is a different
  construction. It may appear only after an additional padding node proves that
  the padded root-sized instance has the same cross optimum and threshold
  predicate as the child-sized instance; absent that proof, it fails this node.
  In particular, the normalized field type
  \[
    \operatorname{allCalls} :
      \operatorname{Finset}\{U // U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)\}
  \]
  or any node-subtype variant is rejected. The accepted field is
  \[
    \operatorname{allCalls} :
      \operatorname{Finset}(\operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V)
  \]
  with membership theorem
  \[
    c\in\operatorname{allCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V),\
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U).
  \]

  The field named `unique\_cross\_call' is reserved for uniqueness among
  concrete recursive oracle calls. Its accepted dependent type is
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{unique\_cross\_call}(p,q,h_{pq}):\\
    \qquad
    \exists! c:\operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V,\
      c\in\operatorname{allCalls}(V)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q),
  \end{array}
  \]
  together with projection fields
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{uniqueCrossCall\_eq}:&
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)),\\
    \operatorname{uniqueCrossCall\_cross}:&
      \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}
        (\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)),p,q),\\
    \operatorname{uniqueCrossCall\_unique}:&
      \forall c\in\operatorname{allCalls}(V),\
      \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here $\operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q)$ unfolds to the assertion that
  the original endpoints $p$ and $q$ are transported by the row-origin maps of
  $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$ to one row of its left child list and one row of
  its right child list, in either order. The rejected theorem
  \[
    \exists! c,\ c=\operatorname{lowestSplitCall}(p,q)
  \]
  or $\exists! c,\ c=\operatorname{lowestSplitCall}(o)$ has no cross-pair
  predicate and is not a weakening of the desired statement; it says only that
  equality to a chosen term is unique.

  Finally, the score and threshold fields must be definitionally recursive-call
  objects. The accepted definitions are
  \[
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V)
    =
