    \bigcup_{c\in\operatorname{allCalls}(V)}
      \{\operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o):
        o\in\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c))\},
  \]
  and
  \[
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists c\in\operatorname{allCalls}(V),\
    \exists o\in\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
      \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)\le t .
  \]
  The names `scoreSet', `scoreSetIdentity', `thresholdYes', and
  `thresholdIdentity', if used, must point to these recursive-call definitions
  and to the non-reflexive theorems comparing them with the original root
  semantics. They may not define `scoreSet' by enumerating canonical original
  pairs, may not define `thresholdYes' by the original existential over
  $\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)$, and may not prove
  `scoreSetIdentity' or `thresholdIdentity' by reflexivity after both sides
  unfold to canonical original-pair expressions. The original-pair enumeration
  belongs only on the left-hand side
  $\operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)$ or
  $\operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)$; the right-hand side must traverse
  $\operatorname{allCalls}(V)$, $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$, and concrete
  bichromatic oracle outputs.

  Trial-4 audit repair: the accepted call-record interface is now part of the
  mathematical statement of this node, not an implementation hint.  The
  declaration audited as $\operatorname{MinIPSplitTreePairCoverage}$ must expose
  a type family
  \[
    \operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V
      =
      \sum_{U:\operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V)}
      \sum_{n_L,n_R,\ell':\N}
        \operatorname{BMinIPInst}(n_L,n_R,\ell')
  \]
  or an isomorphic transparent record.  Every value
  $c:\operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V$ has data projections
  \[
    \operatorname{callNode}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callDim}(c),\quad
    \operatorname{callInst}(c),
  \]
  where
  \[
    \operatorname{callInst}(c):
      \operatorname{BMinIPInst}
        (\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callDim}(c)).
  \]
  These five projections must be stored data or transparent Sigma projections of
  the call value.  It is not sufficient for `MinIPCallRecord' to store only
  `callNode' and define the sizes and target instance later by functions of that
  node; such a record is a node wrapper, not an oracle call.  If a helper name
  `MinIPCallRecord' is used, then after unfolding that helper the normalized
  record type must still contain the four size/dimension/instance projections
  above as fields of the same call element.

  The finite oracle-call set has the exact element type
  $\operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V$:
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V):
      \operatorname{Finset}(\operatorname{ConcreteBMinIPCall}_V).
  \]
  Its membership theorem is the non-tautological reconstruction statement
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U:\operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V),\\
    \qquad
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callDim}(c)=\ell\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  For the canonical call generated by $U$,
  \[
    \operatorname{nodeCall}(U)
      =
      \langle U,|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U)\rangle,
    \qquad
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R).
  \]
  Thus the call set is rejected if its element type is a subtype of
  $\operatorname{MinIPInternalNodes}(V)$, a set of node identifiers, a set of
  masks, a set of canonical original pairs, or a set of records whose only
  non-proof payload is `callNode'.  The membership theorem is also rejected if
  it normalizes to membership in `Finset.univ', to
  $c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)\Longleftrightarrow
  c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)$, or to
  $\exists U,\operatorname{callNode}(c)=U$ without the displayed
  child-sized target-instance equations.

  Trial-5 failure-specific refinement: the accepted call set is the recursive
  image of reachable internal split nodes, not a universe of canonical suffix
  calls.  In particular, the declaration audited at this label is rejected if
  the concrete call type normalizes to
  \[
    \{\,i:\operatorname{Fin}(n): i.\operatorname{val}+1<n\,\},
  \]
  to any lower-index/suffix-call type, or to any type whose inhabitants are
  original row indices rather than child-sized bichromatic oracle-call records.
  The generated name `MinIPConcreteAllCalls', if present, must satisfy the
  non-tautological membership theorem
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U:\operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V),\\
    \qquad
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callDim}(c)=\ell\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Therefore
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V)=\operatorname{Finset.univ}
  \]
  is acceptable only in the degenerate implementation style where the ambient
  finite type itself is definitionally the subtype of records
  $\{\operatorname{nodeCall}(U):U\in\operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V),
  |U|\ge2\}$ and every inhabitant stores
  `callLeftSize', `callRightSize', `callDim' and `callInst' as data.  It is
  explicitly rejected when the ambient type is
  $\{i:\operatorname{Fin}(n):i.\operatorname{val}+1<n\}$, a suffix-call index,
  a canonical-pair index, a row-index subtype, a mask id, or any record from
  which the child-sized target instance is computed only by external functions.
  A suffix call such as the one determined by a lower index $i$ and the right
  suffix $\{i+1,\ldots,n-1\}$ is not a node of the recursive halving tree unless
  the package proves a reachable internal node $U$ whose actual children are
  exactly the singleton row $i$ and that suffix.  Since the halving tree's
  children are fixed by recursive bisection, such a proof is generally false;
  the blueprint requires the recursive tree call set, not the collection of all
  lower-index suffix comparisons.

  Trial-6 rejection-specific refinement: the exact failed normalized interface
  is forbidden.  A declaration does \emph{not} satisfy this node if the concrete
  call type, `MinIPConcreteCall', `MinIPConcreteAllCalls', or any transparently
  equivalent field unfolds to
  \[
    \{\,i:\operatorname{Fin}(p.n)\ //\ i.\operatorname{val}+1<p.n\,\},
  \]
  with
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(X)=\operatorname{Finset.univ}.
  \]
  This remains rejected even if each such index $i$ is later interpreted by a
  helper as the call comparing row $i$ against the suffix
  $\{i+1,\ldots,p.n-1\}$, and even if separate theorems prove that the suffix
  score equals the score of a canonical original pair.  The type above is a
  lower-index suffix-call universe; it is not the recursive split-tree call
  family of Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}.

  The accepted replacement is a positive dependent record type, projected from
  this node, whose inhabitants are already oracle calls:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{MinIPRecursiveCall}(V) &: \mathrm{Type},\\
    \operatorname{callNode}(c) &: \operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V),\\
    \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callRightSize}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callDim}(c) &: \N,\\
    \operatorname{callInst}(c) &:
      \operatorname{BMinIPInst}
        (\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),
         \operatorname{callDim}(c)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The concrete all-call set has type
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V):
      \operatorname{Finset}(\operatorname{MinIPRecursiveCall}(V)),
  \]
  and its membership theorem must be exactly an image-of-reachable-nodes theorem:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U:\operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V),\\
    \qquad
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callNode}(c)=U\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callDim}(c)=\ell\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Thus `Finset.univ' is acceptable only if the ambient type is definitionally
  this dependent image type of reachable internal nodes with the five call
  projections above.  It is not acceptable when the ambient type is any subtype
  of `Fin p.n', any subtype of original row indices, any suffix descriptor, any
  canonical-pair descriptor, or any type whose only non-proof data is an index
  and whose target instance is recovered by an external function.

  The exported unique-call and score/threshold fields must also quantify over
  this positive call-record type.  Their statements must contain the subterms
  \[
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V),\qquad
    \operatorname{callInst}(c),\qquad
    \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)
  \]
  before any row-origin or score transport is applied.  A theorem that ranges
  over a suffix index $i$, constructs the suffix call for
  $\min(p,q)$, or proves uniqueness of the canonical lower-index call is not
  the required `unique\_cross\_call'.  The canonical transport lemma
  \ref{lem:minip-canonical-cross-score-transport} may only be used as a proof
  tool after a prior field has identified the relevant concrete call as
  $\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$; it may not define
  the call set, recursive score set, recursive threshold predicate, optimum
  identity, or unique-call predicate.

  The score, optimum and threshold objects must quantify over
  $\operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V)$ only through this membership
  theorem.  They are rejected if their definitions enumerate original pairs
  $o=(i,j)$, construct the lower-index suffix call associated to
  $\min(i,j)$, and then use the canonical right-suffix index of $\max(i,j)$.
  That canonical suffix construction is exactly the auxiliary transport of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-canonical-cross-score-transport}; it may appear inside a
  proof after showing the same pair occurs in the unique recursive call
  $\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(i,j))$, but it may not be
  the definition of `MinIPConcreteAllCalls',
  `RecursiveCrossScoreSet', `RecursiveCrossThresholdYes', `unique_cross_call',
  `scoreSetIdentity', `optimumIdentity', or `thresholdIdentity'.  The exported
  uniqueness theorem must range over concrete call records
  $c\in\operatorname{MinIPConcreteAllCalls}(V)$ and prove
  \[
    \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)),
  \]
  with the left-hand side unfolding through `callInst(c)' and local left/right
  indices.  A proof that every pair has exactly one lower-index suffix call, or
  a proof that a canonical suffix-call score equals
  $\operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(V,o)$, does not establish pair coverage for the
  recursive split tree and fails this node.

  Cross-pair membership is a relation between an original pair and a concrete
  oracle call.  If the implementation uses the name `MinIPCrossPair' or
  `CrossPairInCall', its unfolded definition must have the form
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists i:\operatorname{Fin}(\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)),\
    \exists j:\operatorname{Fin}(\operatorname{callRightSize}(c)),\\
    \qquad
    \bigl(\operatorname{callLeftOrig}(c,i)=p\wedge
          \operatorname{callRightOrig}(c,j)=q\bigr)
    \vee
    \bigl(\operatorname{callLeftOrig}(c,i)=q\wedge
          \operatorname{callRightOrig}(c,j)=p\bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here `callLeftOrig' and `callRightOrig' are the row-origin maps attached to
  $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$, so the predicate mentions the concrete call
  instance, its local left and right indices, and the transport of those local
  indices back to original row indices.  It must not unfold to
  $c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$,
  $U=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)$, a predicate over the canonical original
  pair alone, or an equality to `canonicalCall'.  The uniqueness field is
  therefore
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{uniqueCrossCall\_iff}(p,q,h_{pq}):\\
    \qquad
    \forall c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
      \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  This theorem is rejected if the left-hand side is already the equality on the
  right, if its proof is only uniqueness of equality to a chosen
  `lowestSplitCall', or if it never mentions the local indices of
  $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$.

  The recursive score and threshold objects are likewise required to range over
  the concrete call set and concrete target outputs.  The package must expose
  the two definitional membership theorems
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    s\in\operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
    \exists o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
      s=\operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o),\\[1mm]
    \operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}(V,t)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V),\
    \exists o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
      \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)\le t .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The right-hand sides of these theorem fields must contain the quantified call
  $c$, the hypothesis $c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)$, the target output
  $o$ for $\operatorname{callInst}(c)$, and the score
  $\operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)$.  They are rejected
  if they contain $\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)$,
  $\operatorname{canonicalCall}(o)$,
  $\operatorname{canonicalRightIndex}(o)$, or
  $\operatorname{MinIPPairScore}(V,o)$ in place of the quantified concrete
  call and its target output.  Canonical-call transport may appear only in the
  proof of the forward direction of `scoreSetIdentity', where an original pair
  is first sent to the unique concrete call supplied by
  `uniqueCrossCall_iff'.  It may not appear in the definitions of
  $\operatorname{RecursiveCrossScoreSet}$ or
  $\operatorname{RecursiveCrossThresholdYes}$.

  Finally, the derived fields must make the direction of reasoning explicit:
  `scoreSetIdentity_forward' maps a root pair
  $(p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)$ to the call
  $\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$, proves this call is
  in $\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)$, constructs the corresponding local
  bichromatic output $o$, and rewrites its
  $\operatorname{BMinIPScore}$ to $\operatorname{origScore}_V(p,q)$ by row-origin
  transport.  `scoreSetIdentity_reverse' starts from a quantified
  $c\in\operatorname{MinIPAllCalls}(V)$ and
  $o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c))$, uses the membership
  theorem to recover the reachable internal node and child-sized
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)$, then uses `crossPair_to_origPair' to produce
  the original distinct pair and score equality.  The threshold and optimum
  identities must be derived from these two directions.  A proof by reflexivity
  after defining both sides from canonical original pairs, or any definition in
  which the recursive side is already a copy of the root original-pair
  enumeration, is not this node.

  Trial-8 rejection-specific refinement: the audited Lean declaration must rule
  out the suffix-index facade identified by the statement audit. The names
  `MinIPTreeInternalNodes', `MinIPTreeAllCalls',
  `MinIPTreeRecursiveScoreSet', `unique_cross_call',
  `scoreSetIdentity_forward', `scoreSetIdentity_reverse',
  `optimumIdentity', and `thresholdIdentity', if present, have the fixed
  meanings below. They are rejected if they are implemented only for a type of
  suffix indices, lower indices, or nodes of the form
  \[
    \{\,i:\operatorname{Fin}(n)\ //\ i.\operatorname{val}+1<n\,\},
  \]
  with
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPTreeInternalNodes}(V)=\operatorname{Finset.univ}
  \]
  or with `allCalls' equal to the image of this universe. Such a type records
  possible suffix comparisons, not the reachable nodes of the recursively
  halved call tree. It is not enough for a suffix-index node to carry a proof
  that the corresponding suffix call is well formed; every internal node must
  instead carry a root-to-node path built from the root, left-child and
  right-child constructors of $\operatorname{ReachableNode}_V$.

  A compliant package therefore contains a positive path-carrying internal-node
  type, or an isomorphic transparent Sigma type,
  \[
    \operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V)
      :=
      \{U:\operatorname{Node}(V) //
        \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U)\wedge |U|\ge2\},
  \]
  and the field
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPTreeInternalNodes}(V):
      \operatorname{Finset}(\operatorname{ReachableInternalNode}(V)).
  \]
  Its membership theorem must recover the path proof:
  \[
    U\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeInternalNodes}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{ReachableNode}_V(U.\operatorname{node})\wedge
    |U.\operatorname{node}|\ge2.
  \]
  The right-hand side may not be merely
  $U.\operatorname{index}+1<n$, $|U|\ge2$, `True', or membership in
  `Finset.univ'. The same package must project `reachableRoot',
  `reachableLeft', `reachableRight' and the non-vacuous
  `reachableInduction' eliminator displayed earlier in this node. If
  `ReachableNode' is absent, if it unfolds to suffix-index well-formedness, or
  if its eliminator assumes $\forall U,Q(U)$ instead of using the root and two
  child steps, then the package does not satisfy this lemma.

  The call set must be a finite set of child-sized oracle-call records obtained
  from these reachable internal nodes:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeInternalNodes}(V),\\
    \qquad
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callNode}(c)=U\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callLeftSize}(c)=|U_L|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callRightSize}(c)=|U_R|\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callDim}(c)=\ell\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{callInst}(c)=\operatorname{crossInst}(U)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  This is the required normalized type of `MinIPTreeAllCalls_mem_iff' or
  `allCalls_mem_iff'. A theorem whose right-hand side is
  $c\in\operatorname{Finset.univ}$, $c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V)$,
  $c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(i)$ for a suffix index $i$, or
  $\exists i,\ c=\operatorname{suffixCall}(i)$ is rejected. The element $c$
  itself must expose `callInst(c)' as data with type
  $\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(\operatorname{callLeftSize}(c),
  \operatorname{callRightSize}(c),\operatorname{callDim}(c))$; a call record
  whose payload is only a suffix index or node index is not a target oracle
  call.

  The uniqueness field is also about these concrete calls. The field named
  `unique_cross_call' must have, after unfolding aliases, the form
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{unique\_cross\_call}(p,q,h_{pq}):\\
    \qquad
    \exists! c,\ 
      c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V)\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q),
  \end{array}
  \]
  together with the theorem
  \[
    \forall c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V),\
      \operatorname{CrossPairInCall}(c,p,q)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q)).
  \]
  Here `CrossPairInCall(c,p,q)' must mention `callInst(c)', local left and
  right output indices for that instance, and the origin maps carrying those
  local indices back to the original endpoints $p$ and $q$. A uniqueness theorem
  over internal-node indices,
  \[
    \exists! U,\ U=\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q),
  \]
  or over suffix indices, or a theorem whose cross-pair predicate is already
  the equality $c=\operatorname{nodeCall}(\operatorname{splitNode}(p,q))$, is
  tautological and is not this field.

  The recursive score set must be the scores of all concrete target outputs of
  the concrete call set:
  \[
    s\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeRecursiveScoreSet}(V)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V),\
    \exists o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
      s=\operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o).
  \]
  This definition may not be replaced by the set of original pair scores, by a
  set of canonical suffix-call scores, or by a set whose membership theorem
  proves only that every original pair score is a member. The package must
  expose both directions as theorem fields:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity\_forward}:&
      s\in\operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)\to
      s\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeRecursiveScoreSet}(V),\\
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity\_reverse}:&
      s\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeRecursiveScoreSet}(V)\to
      s\in\operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V),\\
    \operatorname{scoreSetIdentity}:&
      \operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)=
      \operatorname{MinIPTreeRecursiveScoreSet}(V).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The reverse field is mandatory: it must start from a concrete call
  $c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V)$ and a concrete target output
  $o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c))$, recover the
  reachable internal node through `allCalls_mem_iff', use
  `crossPair_to_origPair' to produce an original distinct pair, and transport
  the score back to $\operatorname{RootScoreSet}(V)$. A package proving only
  the forward membership of original pair scores in a recursive score set, or
  whose `scoreSetIdentity' is not exported as equality of the two sets above,
  formalizes a weaker invariant and is rejected.

  The optimum and threshold consequences are not optional corollaries outside
  the audited declaration. The same package must project
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{optimumIdentity}:&
      \operatorname{RootMinIPOpt}(V)=
      \min\{\,m_{\mathrm{cross}}(c):
        c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V)\,\},\\
    \operatorname{thresholdIdentity}:&
      \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists c\in\operatorname{MinIPTreeAllCalls}(V),\
      \exists o:\operatorname{BMinIPOut}(\operatorname{callInst}(c)),\
        \operatorname{BMinIPScore}(\operatorname{callInst}(c),o)\le t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The left-hand objects must unfold to the original Min-IP optimum and original
  threshold existential over distinct root pairs from Definition~\ref{def:minip};
  the right-hand objects must unfold to minima and existential quantification
  over the concrete recursive call set above. These fields are rejected if
  their types normalize to membership implications only, to `True', to
  $\operatorname{RootMinIPOpt}(V)=\operatorname{RootMinIPOpt}(V)$, to
  $\operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)\Longleftrightarrow
  \operatorname{RootThresholdYes}(V,t)$, or to statements over suffix indices
  that never mention `callInst(c)'.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:minip, def:bichromatic-minip}
  For two distinct leaves of the recursion tree containing original indices
  $p$ and $q$, follow their root-to-leaf paths. Since the root contains both
  indices and singleton leaves separate them, there is a unique first node at
  which the two paths go to different children. That node is internal and its
  cross bichromatic call contains exactly this pair. Uniqueness follows because
  below this node the two indices lie in different subtrees and are never again
  in the same recursive subproblem, while above it they lie in the same child
  of every split.

  The converse is immediate: every cross pair of a split node consists of two
  original rows from disjoint children of one node, so the two original indices
  are distinct. Thus original distinct pairs are in bijection with the disjoint
  union of cross pairs over all internal nodes. Taking inner-product scores
  across this bijection gives the score-set identity; taking minima gives the
  global-optimum equation, and existentially testing whether some score is at
  most $t$ gives the threshold equivalence.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Bichromatic Min-IP reduction, Lemma A.8]
  \label{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}
  \uses{def:minip, def:gamma-minip, def:minip-dec, def:bichromatic-minip, def:tsq-alg-exists, lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}
  If $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }\MinIP_{n,\ell}}$ exists with polynomial factors
  in $\ell$, then $\TSQAlg{\MinIP_{n,\ell}}$ exists with polynomial factors in
  $\ell$ (possibly with a different positive exponent). The same implication
  holds for $\gamma\text{-}\MinIP_{n,\ell}$ and for the decision version
  $\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}$.

  The audited declaration at this label must expose the recursive halving
  algorithm-transfer package
  $\operatorname{MinIPBichromaticRecursiveWitness}$. This package is the
  declaration audited at the label; the theorem statement is not merely the
  three implications between $\TSQAlg$ propositions. Its fields are:
  \[
    \operatorname{split}(V)=(V_L,V_R),\qquad
    |V_L|=\lceil |V|/2\rceil,\quad |V_R|=\lfloor |V|/2\rfloor,
  \]
  a call tree whose nodes are subsets $U\subseteq V$ and whose non-leaf node
  with split $(U_L,U_R)$ makes exactly the bichromatic oracle call
  $(U_L,U_R)$, and a reconstruction procedure taking all oracle answers and
  returning the best among the cross-split answers and the two recursively
  reconstructed within-half answers. The exact-search correctness field states
  \[
    \min_{\substack{p,q\in U\\p\ne q}}\inner{p}{q}
    =
    \min\!\left(
      \min_{\substack{p\in U_L\\q\in U_R}}\inner{p}{q},
      \min_{\substack{p,q\in U_L\\p\ne q}}\inner{p}{q},
      \min_{\substack{p,q\in U_R\\p\ne q}}\inner{p}{q}
    \right)
  \]
  at every recursive node, together with the theorem that the reconstructed
  pair realizes the global minimum of the original instance. The
  $\gamma$-approximate field states that if every oracle call returns a
  $\gamma$-approximate minimum for its cross part, then the best reconstructed
  candidate is a $\gamma$-approximate minimum for $V$. The threshold-decision
  field states that
  \[
    \exists p\ne q\in U,\ \inner{p}{q}\le t
  \]
  is equivalent to the disjunction of the corresponding cross, left-recursive,
  and right-recursive predicates.
  The cross problem at a non-leaf node is a real target instance, not an index
  or placeholder:
  \[
    \operatorname{crossInst}(U)
      :=(U_L,U_R):\operatorname{BMinIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell),
  \]
  with score
  \[
    s_{\mathrm{cross},U}(p,q)=\inner{(U_L)_p}{(U_R)_q}.
  \]
  The required oracle-call equation is
  \[
    \operatorname{callsAtNode}(U)
      =
      \{\,(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossInst}(U))\,\}
  \]
  for every non-leaf node. A call field that stores only the node $U$, only the
  pair of cardinalities, or an arbitrary index into the recursion tree is not a
  bichromatic Min-IP oracle call.
  This equation is a named projection of the audited package, for example
  \[
    \operatorname{callsAtNode\_eq\_singleton}(U):
    \operatorname{callsAtNode}(U)
      =
      \{\,(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,
          \operatorname{crossInst}(U))\,\}.
  \]
  The right-hand side must contain the actual split lists $U_L,U_R$ through
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)$ and the child cardinalities $|U_L|,|U_R|$. A
  statement such as
  $\operatorname{callsAtNode\_eq\_singleton}(U):\mathrm{True}$,
  $\mathrm{True}\wedge\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{callsAtNode}(U))$,
  or an equality to a singleton whose element is only a node identifier is not
  this projection.
  The parameters of this call are the child cardinalities $|U_L|$ and $|U_R|$,
  or a single balanced-size parameter together with explicit padding/truncation
  equations if the formal bichromatic family is restricted to equal-size color
  classes. They are not the original top-level parameters $(n,\ell)$ unless
  $U$ is the root and the two halves have the required size. Thus a definition
  such as
  \[
    \operatorname{callsAtNode}(U)
      =\{(n,\ell,\operatorname{someGenericBMinIPInst}(n,\ell))\}
  \]
  is rejected: it is not the split subinstance at node $U$.

  Write
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)&=
      \min_{p\in U_L,\ q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    m_L(U)&=\min_{p\ne q\in U_L}\inner{p}{q},\\
    m_R(U)&=\min_{p\ne q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    m_U&=\min_{p\ne q\in U}\inner{p}{q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The exact-node correctness field is the equation
  \[
    m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U))).
  \]
  This equation must mention the three separately defined optima above. It is
  rejected if it reduces to
  $m_U=\min(m_U,\min(m_U,m_U))$, or to the same expression with
  `MinIPOpt U' repeated on both sides. The reconstruction fields must define
  named left and right subinstances
  $\operatorname{leftInst}(U)=U_L$ and
  $\operatorname{rightInst}(U)=U_R$, with optima
  $m_L(U)$ and $m_R(U)$ computed on those subinstances, and the cross optimum
  $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$ computed on $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)$. A formal
  proof that obtains the displayed equation by rewriting all three optima to
  the same expression is not an instance of this node.
  The field has the named type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactNodeCorrectness}(U):\\
    \qquad
    m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U))),
  \end{array}
  \]
  where $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $m_L(U)$ and $m_R(U)$ are separate projections
  with the displayed definitions. The field is rejected if its type is
  $\mathrm{True}$, $\mathrm{Unit}$, an existential statement with no equality,
  an implication from a validity relation to itself, or any proposition in
  which $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $m_L(U)$ and $m_R(U)$ do not all occur.
  The reconstruction fields must define
  \[
    \operatorname{candidateSet}(U)
      =\{o_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),o_L(U),o_R(U)\}
  \]
  with the cross candidate obtained from the valid oracle output for
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)$ and the left/right candidates obtained from
  recursive reconstruction, and
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstructExact}(U,\operatorname{answers})
      \in \arg\min_{o\in\operatorname{candidateSet}(U)} s_U(o).
  \]
  The global-correctness field must then prove
  $s_V(\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers}))=m_V$.
  It is not enough to prove an implication whose premise and conclusion are the
  same `ValidOut' proposition.

  For the decision version, define the three predicates separately:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)&\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p\in U_L,\exists q\in U_R,\ \inner{p}{q}\le t,\\
    \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)&\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p\ne q\in U_L,\ \inner{p}{q}\le t,\\
    \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U)&\Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p\ne q\in U_R,\ \inner{p}{q}\le t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The field `thresholdNodeCorrectness' must state
  \[
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\MinIP_t}(U)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U).
  \]
  It is rejected if the same predicate is repeated in all three disjuncts.
  The approximate and threshold fields are likewise concrete:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{gammaNodeCorrectness}(U,\operatorname{answers}):\\
    \qquad
    m_U\le
    s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
    \le \gamma m_U,\\[1mm]
    \operatorname{thresholdNodeCorrectness}(U):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{Yes}_{\MinIP_t}(U)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  $\operatorname{gammaNodeCorrectness}$ must mention the reconstructed
  candidate, the score $s_U$ and both approximation inequalities. It is not an
  identity implication such as
  $\operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma\MinIP}\to
  \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\gamma\MinIP}$. The threshold field is not a tautology
  $P\leftrightarrow P$, and its three right-hand disjuncts must be the distinct
  cross, left and right predicates displayed above.

  More explicitly, the package has named projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{callTree}:&
      \text{the finite binary recursion tree of subsets }U\subseteq V,\\
    \operatorname{callsAtNode}:&
      U\mapsto\{(U_L,U_R)\}\text{ for every non-leaf node},\\
    \operatorname{reconstructExact}:&
      \text{selects the candidate with smallest inner product from the
      cross, left and right answers},\\
    \operatorname{exactNodeCorrectness}:&
      \text{the displayed minimum-decomposition equality for every node }U,\\
    \operatorname{exactGlobalCorrectness}:&
      \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\MinIP}(V,
        \operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers})),\\
    \operatorname{reconstructGamma}:&
      \text{the same smallest-score selection among approximate candidates},\\
    \operatorname{gammaNodeCorrectness}:&
      m_U\le s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGamma})\le\gamma m_U,\\
    \operatorname{thresholdNodeCorrectness}:&
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\MinIP_t}(U)\Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\mathrm{cross},t}(U_L,U_R)\vee
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\MinIP_t}(U_L)\vee
      \operatorname{Yes}_{\MinIP_t}(U_R).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The last three fields are propositions containing the displayed mathematical
  relations. They may not have type `True', `Unit', `True -> True',
  `Nonempty True', or any other placeholder, and they may not be proved only
  from an abstract transfer implication.

  The runtime field is tied to the call tree:
  \[
    T_{\mathrm{mono}}(n,\ell)
      \le C n\ell+
      C\sum_{r=0}^{\lceil\log_2 n\rceil-1}
        2^r\,T_{\mathrm{bi}}\!\left(\left\lceil n/2^{r+1}\right\rceil,\ell\right),
  \]
  and the witness proves that if
  $T_{\mathrm{bi}}(m,\ell)\le C' m^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell)$, then the
  right-hand side is at most
  $C'' n^{2-\eps'}\operatorname{poly}(\ell)$ for some $\eps'>0$. A declaration
  whose fields are only implications between
  $\operatorname{Nonempty}(\operatorname{TSQAlgorithm})$ propositions, or which
  does not contain the split tree, optimum-in-some-call correctness, and the
  displayed runtime sum, is not this lemma.
  To prevent vacuous implementations, the audited package must also contain
  named runtime projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V) &: \R_{\ge0},\\
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntimeDef}:&
      \operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{split}}\,n\ell+
      c_{\mathrm{calls}}
      \sum_{U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V))}
        T_{\mathrm{bi}}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell)
      +c_{\mathrm{recon}}\,|\operatorname{callTree}(V)|\,\ell,\\
    \operatorname{runtimeRecurrence}:&
      \operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V)
      \le
      C n\ell+
      C\sum_{r=0}^{\lceil\log_2 n\rceil-1}
        2^r\,T_{\mathrm{bi}}\!\left(
          \left\lceil n/2^{r+1}\right\rceil,
          \left\lfloor n/2^{r+1}\right\rfloor,
          \ell\right).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Here the target runtime is evaluated on the actual child color-class sizes of
  each cross instance. If the formal bichromatic family is equal-size only, the
  runtime definition must instead include the explicit padding/truncation cost
  and the padded target sizes; it may not silently call a root-size oracle. A
  field named `runtimeRecurrence' whose conclusion is a self-bound such as
  $T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)+n\ell\le C(T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)+n\ell)$, or whose
  left-hand side is not the named $\operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}$ above, is
  rejected. Likewise, `exactNodeCorrectness',
  `exactGlobalCorrectness', `gammaNodeCorrectness', and
  `thresholdNodeCorrectness' are rejected if they reduce respectively to
  $m_U=m_U$, $\operatorname{ValidOut}=\operatorname{ValidOut}$,
  $\operatorname{ValidOut}_\gamma\to\operatorname{ValidOut}_\gamma$, or
  $\operatorname{Yes}_t(U)\leftrightarrow\operatorname{Yes}_t(U)$ after
  unfolding the declarations audited at this label. Their types must contain
  the separate cross, left and right objects named above.

  To make the rejection criterion syntactic, the following exact placeholder
  shapes are explicitly forbidden at this label:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactNodeCorrectness}(X):
      \operatorname{MinIPOpt}(X)=\operatorname{MinIPOpt}(X),\\
    \operatorname{exactGlobalCorrectness}(X):
      \operatorname{MinIPValidOut}(X)=\operatorname{MinIPValidOut}(X),\\
    \operatorname{thresholdNodeCorrectness}(X):
      \operatorname{MinIPDecYes}(p,X)\Longleftrightarrow
      \operatorname{MinIPDecYes}(p,X),\\
    \operatorname{runtimeRecurrence}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},n,\ell):
      T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)+n\ell
      \le C\bigl(T_{\mathrm{bi}}(n,\ell)+n\ell\bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The corresponding accepted statements must mention
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)$, $\operatorname{leftInst}(U)$,
  $\operatorname{rightInst}(U)$, $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $m_L(U)$,
  $m_R(U)$, the reconstructed candidate, and the named
  $\operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}$. The target runtime may occur only through
  the call-tree sum over the child-sized bichromatic calls, not as a single
  root-sized oracle call.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: the audited Lean declaration must make the
  split-node quantities projections of the witness, not local names that can be
  unfolded away. In particular it must contain equations
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{crossOpt\_eq}(U):&
      m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)=
      \min_{p\in U_L,q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{leftOpt\_eq}(U):&
      m_L(U)=\min_{p\ne q\in U_L}\inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{rightOpt\_eq}(U):&
      m_R(U)=\min_{p\ne q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{nodeOpt\_eq}(U):&
      m_U=\min_{p\ne q\in U}\inner{p}{q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The exact global field has the dependent type
  \[
    \operatorname{exactGlobalCorrectness}:
    \left(\forall U,\ \operatorname{oracleAnswersValid}(U)\right)
    \to
    \operatorname{MinIPValidOut}
      (V,\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers})),
  \]
  where the conclusion is the concrete search validity relation for the
  reconstructed pair. It is not an equality between two propositions named
  `MinIPValidOut'. The gamma field must first define
  $s^*_U=s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers}))$ and
  then prove the two inequalities
  $m_U\le s^*_U$ and $s^*_U\le\gamma m_U$ from the three candidate bounds. The
  threshold field must define `CrossYes_t', `LeftYes_t' and `RightYes_t' as
  separate predicates and its right-hand side must syntactically contain those
  three names. Any field whose normalized type is
  `MinIPOpt X = MinIPOpt X',
  `MinIPValidOut X = MinIPValidOut X',
  `GammaMinIPValidOut X -> GammaMinIPValidOut X', or
  `MinIPDecYes p X ↔ MinIPDecYes p X' fails this node, even if other abstract
  transfer fields are present.

  Trial-9 alignment requirement: the names used by the generated Lean attempt
  are reserved with the following concrete types. If the witness contains fields
  named `exactSearchCorrectness', `gammaApproxCorrectness', or
  `thresholdDecisionCorrectness', those fields must be theorem fields with the
  meanings below; they may not be alternative weaker summaries.

  First, the recursion may not assign the numeric value $0$ to leaves merely to
  make minima easy. A leaf $U$ with $|U|<2$ has no distinct-pair output, no
  exact candidate, and no finite optimum used in the reconstructed candidate
  set. Formally the witness must expose one of the following equivalent
  encodings:
  \[
    \operatorname{leafCandidate}(U)=\operatorname{none}
    \quad\text{for } |U|<2,
  \]
  or an extended-real neutral value
  $m_U=+\infty$ for leaves with no distinct pair. It must also contain
  \[
    \operatorname{leafNoCandidate}(U):
      |U|<2\Rightarrow
      \neg\exists o,\ \operatorname{MinIPOut}(U,o).
  \]
  The declaration is rejected if it defines a projection such as
  `MinIPNodeLeafValue := 0' and then uses that value as $m_L(U)$ or $m_R(U)$
  in an internal-node minimum. For an internal node, the left and right values
  are the true recursive optima of the concrete subinstances $U_L$ and $U_R$
  when those subinstances contain a distinct pair, and are the explicit
  no-candidate neutral values otherwise.

  The field `exactSearchCorrectness' has the dependent type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactSearchCorrectness}(V,\operatorname{answers}):\\
    \qquad
    \left(\forall U\in
      \operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V)),\
      \operatorname{BMinIPValidOut}
        (\operatorname{crossInst}(U),
         o_{\mathrm{cross}}(U))\right)
    \to\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{MinIPValidOut}
      (V,\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers}))
    \ \wedge\
    s_V(\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers}))=m_V .
  \end{array}
  \]
  Its proof must proceed through the internal-node theorem
  \[
    m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U)))
  \]
  with $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $m_L(U)$ and $m_R(U)$ defined by the projection
  equations `crossOpt_eq', `leftOpt_eq' and `rightOpt_eq' above. The selected
  candidate is
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstructExact}(U,\operatorname{answers})
    \in
    \arg\min\{s_U(o_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)),
              s_U(o_L(U)),
              s_U(o_R(U))\},
  \]
  after omitting child candidates that are absent at leaves. A field proving
  only
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeReconstructedValue}(U)
      =
      \min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),
           \min(\operatorname{MinIPNodeLeafValue},
                \operatorname{MinIPNodeLeafValue}))
  \]
  is explicitly rejected, even if the field is named
  `exactSearchCorrectness'. That statement contains neither the true global
  minimum over pairs in $U$ nor a proof that the reconstructed root output is a
  valid $\MinIP$ output.

  The field `gammaApproxCorrectness' has the dependent type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{gammaApproxCorrectness}
      (U,\operatorname{answers}):\\
    \qquad
    \left(\forall W\text{ below }U,\
      \operatorname{cross/recursive candidates at }W
      \text{ satisfy their concrete }
      \gamma\text{-approximate validity relations}\right)
    \to\\
    \qquad
    m_U\le
      s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
    \ \wedge\
    s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
      \le \gamma m_U .
  \end{array}
  \]
  The conclusion must mention the reconstructed candidate and the true optimum
  $m_U$ of the concrete node $U$. Its proof must use the three inequalities for
  the cross candidate, the left recursive candidate and the right recursive
  candidate, together with the equality
  $m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U)))$. It is rejected if its
  normalized type is an identity implication
  \[
    \operatorname{GammaMinIPValidOut}(\cdots)
      \to \operatorname{GammaMinIPValidOut}(\cdots),
  \]
  or any implication whose conclusion is exactly one of its assumptions.

  The field `thresholdDecisionCorrectness' has the dependent type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{thresholdDecisionCorrectness}(U,t):\\
    \qquad
    \bigl(\exists p,q\in U,\ p\ne q\ \wedge\ \inner{p}{q}\le t\bigr)
    \Longleftrightarrow\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The left-hand side is the concrete yes predicate of
  $\MinIP_{|U|,\ell,t}$ on the node $U$; it is not a newly defined predicate
  whose body is the right-hand disjunction. The proof must split an arbitrary
  distinct pair in $U$ into the three cases ``one endpoint in $U_L$ and one in
  $U_R$'', ``both endpoints in $U_L$'', and ``both endpoints in $U_R$'', and
  conversely inject any witness from a right-hand disjunct into $U$. A field
  proving only
  \[
    (\operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)\vee
     \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)\vee
     \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U))
    \Longleftrightarrow
    (\operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)\vee
     \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)\vee
     \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U))
  \]
  is explicitly rejected, even if it is named
  `thresholdDecisionCorrectness'.

  Trial-10 failure-specific refinement: the audited declaration must not use a
  recursively defined helper predicate or helper value as a substitute for the
  original Min-IP semantics. The witness therefore exposes the original
  node-level objects as separate projections:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{OrigPair}(U) &:=
      \{(p,q):p,q\in U,\ p\ne q\},\\
    \operatorname{origScore}_U(p,q) &:=
      \inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{origOpt}(U) &:=
      \min_{(p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)}
        \operatorname{origScore}_U(p,q),\\
    \operatorname{origThresholdYes}(U,t) &:=
      \exists (p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(U),\
        \operatorname{origScore}_U(p,q)\le t .
  \end{array}
  \]
  For $|U|<2$, $\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)$ is empty and the exact/gamma
  reconstruction returns no candidate from $U$; the witness must not assign a
  real optimum $0$ to this empty search space. For $|U|\ge2$, the projection
  \[
    \operatorname{origOpt\_eq\_MinIPOpt}(U):
      \operatorname{origOpt}(U)=\operatorname{MinIPOpt}(U)
  \]
  ties the node optimum to the concrete family from Definition~\ref{def:minip}.
  The accepted exact correctness theorem is rooted at the original root
  instance:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactSearchCorrectness}(V,\operatorname{answers}):\\
    \qquad
    \left(\forall U\in
      \operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V)),\
      \operatorname{BMinIPValidOut}
        (\operatorname{crossInst}(U),o_{\mathrm{cross}}(U))\right)
    \to\\
    \qquad
    \exists i,j,\ i\ne j\ \wedge\
      \operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers})=(i,j)
      \ \wedge\
      \inner{v_i}{v_j}
        = \min_{p\ne q}\inner{v_p}{v_q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Equivalently it may conclude
  $\operatorname{MinIPValidOut}
  (V,\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers}))$, but only
  together with the score equality above or the projection
  $\operatorname{origOpt\_eq\_MinIPOpt}(V)$ used in the proof. A theorem about
  `MinIPNodeReconstructedValue', `MinIPNodeLeafValue', or any recursively
  defined value is not accepted unless it also has this root-level existential
  pair conclusion.

  The witness must also expose the trichotomy that makes the split recurrence
  non-tautological:
  \[
    \operatorname{pairSplitTrichotomy}(U,p,q):
    (p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{CrossPair}_U(p,q)\vee
    \operatorname{LeftPair}_U(p,q)\vee
    \operatorname{RightPair}_U(p,q).
  \]
  Here `CrossPair', `LeftPair' and `RightPair' are defined by membership of the
  two endpoints in $U_L\times U_R$, $U_L\times U_L$, and
  $U_R\times U_R$, respectively, with distinctness retained in the same-side
  cases. The proof of `exactNodeCorrectness',
  `gammaApproxCorrectness' and `thresholdDecisionCorrectness' must use this
  trichotomy. A recurrence obtained by defining the left-hand predicate or value
  to be the right-hand disjunction/minimum is rejected.

  The exact decomposition theorem must be a theorem about the original optimum,
  not the definition of a helper value. If the generated Lean introduces names
  such as `MinIPNodeGlobalValue', `MinIPNodeExactDecomposition',
  `MinIPNodeExactDecomposition_correct', or
  `reconstructedPairRealizesGlobalMinimum', those names have the reserved
  meanings below. The helper `MinIPNodeGlobalValue U', if present, must unfold
  to the original finite minimum over $\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)$:
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeGlobalValue}(U)
    =
    \min_{(p,q)\in\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)}
      \operatorname{origScore}_U(p,q).
  \]
  It is explicitly not allowed to define
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeGlobalValue}(U)
      :=
      \min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U))).
  \]
  The witness must expose this by a projection
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeGlobalValue\_eq\_origOpt}(U):
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeGlobalValue}(U)=\operatorname{origOpt}(U),
  \]
  or by making `MinIPNodeGlobalValue' definitionally equal to
  $\operatorname{origOpt}(U)$.

  Consequently the decomposition field has the non-definitional type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeExactDecomposition\_correct}(U):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{origOpt}(U)
    =
    \min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U))),
  \end{array}
  \]
  for internal nodes $U$ with the no-candidate leaf convention applied to
  absent children. The proof of this field must use
  $\operatorname{pairSplitTrichotomy}$ to show both inequalities between the
  original minimum over $\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)$ and the three branch
  optima. A proof by `rfl' is accepted only if the left-hand side still unfolds
  to the original finite minimum over $\operatorname{OrigPair}(U)$ and the
  right-hand side is definitionally that same finite minimum for reasons
  independent of the branch definitions. In particular, the trial failure shape
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeExactDecomposition\_correct}(U) := rfl
  \]
  after defining `MinIPNodeGlobalValue' to be
  $\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U)))$ is rejected. Such a theorem
  proves only consistency of a renamed split value and never proves the paper's
  recurrence for the concrete Min-IP optimum.

  The field `reconstructedPairRealizesGlobalMinimum' must then target the
  original optimum:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{reconstructedPairRealizesGlobalMinimum}
      (V,\operatorname{answers}):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{origScore}_V
      (\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers}))
    =
    \operatorname{origOpt}(V),
  \end{array}
  \]
  together with the proof that
  $\operatorname{reconstructExact}(V,\operatorname{answers})
  \in\operatorname{OrigPair}(V)$. It is not enough to prove equality to
  `MinIPNodeGlobalValue V' unless the same witness also exposes
  `MinIPNodeGlobalValue_eq_origOpt V'. The gamma approximation theorem is
  subject to the same restriction: its lower and upper bounds are with respect
  to $\operatorname{origOpt}(U)$, not with respect to a recursively defined
  `MinIPNodeGlobalValue' unless that value is proved equal to
  $\operatorname{origOpt}(U)$ as above.

  The approximate theorem has the same original-semantics requirement. It must
  define
  \[
    s^*_U =
      \operatorname{origScore}_U
        (\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
  \]
  for the actual returned pair, and its conclusion is exactly
  \[
    \operatorname{origOpt}(U)\le s^*_U
    \ \wedge\ 
    s^*_U\le \gamma\,\operatorname{origOpt}(U).
  \]
  The assumptions are validity proofs for the concrete cross oracle answers and
  the recursively reconstructed child candidates; the conclusion may not be one
  of those assumptions repeated verbatim. If the generated field named
  `gammaApproxCorrectness' has type
  $\operatorname{CandidateValid}(U,o)\to
  \operatorname{CandidateValid}(U,o)$, or any normalized form in which the
  consequent is syntactically one premise, it fails this node even if helper
  definitions named `origOpt' exist elsewhere.

  The threshold theorem also must use the original threshold predicate:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{thresholdDecisionCorrectness}(U,t):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{origThresholdYes}(U,t)
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)\vee
    \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U),
  \end{array}
  \]
  together with projection equations
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{origThresholdYes\_eq}(U,t):&
      \operatorname{origThresholdYes}(U,t)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p,q\in U,\ p\ne q\ \wedge\ \inner{p}{q}\le t,\\
    \operatorname{crossThresholdYes\_eq}(U,t):&
      \operatorname{CrossYes}_t(U)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p\in U_L,\exists q\in U_R,\ \inner{p}{q}\le t,\\
    \operatorname{leftThresholdYes\_eq}(U,t):&
      \operatorname{LeftYes}_t(U)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p,q\in U_L,\ p\ne q\ \wedge\ \inner{p}{q}\le t,\\
    \operatorname{rightThresholdYes\_eq}(U,t):&
      \operatorname{RightYes}_t(U)
      \Longleftrightarrow
      \exists p,q\in U_R,\ p\ne q\ \wedge\ \inner{p}{q}\le t.
  \end{array}
  \]
  Thus a field whose left-hand side is itself defined to be
  `CrossYes_t U or LeftYes_t U or RightYes_t U' is explicitly not the threshold
  correctness theorem. The left-hand side must unfold to the original
  existential over distinct pairs in $U$, and the proof must map witnesses
  through `pairSplitTrichotomy' in both directions.

  Trial-11 failure-specific refinement: the audited declaration must expose the
  recursive algorithm transfer itself, not only local decomposition lemmas. The
  witness therefore has three algorithm-construction projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{mkExactMinIPFromBichromatic}:&
      \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}
        (\operatorname{BMinIPExact})
      \to
      \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}(\MinIP),\\
    \operatorname{mkGammaMinIPFromBichromatic}:&
      \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}
        (\operatorname{BMinIPApprox})
      \to
      \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}(\gamma\text{-}\MinIP),\\
    \operatorname{mkThresholdMinIPFromBichromatic}:&
      \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}
        (\operatorname{BMinIPThreshold})
      \to
      \operatorname{def\_tsq\_alg\_exists}(\MinIP_t).
  \end{array}
  \]
  These are transparent constructors whose `run', `correct', `T' and
  truly-subquadratic proof projections reduce to the split-tree reconstruction
  and runtime objects specified in this node. In particular, for each target
  runtime $T_{\mathrm{bi}}$ the source runtime projection is exactly the named
  value
  \[
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V),
  \]
  with defining equation
  \[
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntimeDef}:
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V)
    =
    c_{\mathrm{split}}n\ell+
    c_{\mathrm{calls}}
    \sum_{U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V))}
      T_{\mathrm{bi}}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell)
    +c_{\mathrm{recon}}|\operatorname{callTree}(V)|\ell,
  \]
  and the projection
  \[
    \operatorname{runtimeRecurrence}
  \]
  is a theorem whose left-hand side is this same
  $\operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V)$ and whose right-hand side
  is the level-by-level recursive runtime sum over the child-sized
  bichromatic calls. The witness also contains an exponent-transfer projection
  \[
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntimeTSQ}:
    \forall \eps>0,\ \exists \eps'>0,\quad
    T_{\mathrm{bi}}(a,b,\ell)=
      O((a+b)^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))
    \Rightarrow
    \operatorname{splitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{bi}},V)
      =O(n^{2-\eps'}\operatorname{poly}(\ell)).
  \]
  A generated `MinIPBichromaticRecursiveWitness' with no projections literally
  named, or transparently equivalent to, `splitTreeRuntime',
  `splitTreeRuntimeDef', `runtimeRecurrence', and
  `splitTreeRuntimeTSQ' fails this lemma, even if it proves some local
  correctness statement. Likewise, proving only
  $\TSQAlg{\mathrm{BMinIP}}\to\TSQAlg{\MinIP}$ as an opaque implication is
  insufficient; the constructed algorithm's run, correctness and runtime must
  be obtained from these projections.

  The exact correctness package must derive an optimum equation, not only a
  score-set identity. If a helper theorem named
  `MinIPNodeScoreSetDecomposition' is present, it is allowed only as an
  intermediate lemma with the explicit derived projection
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{scoreSetDecomposition\_to\_exactNodeCorrectness}(U):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{MinIPNodeScoreSetDecomposition}(U)
    \to
    m_U=\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\min(m_L(U),m_R(U))).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The audited field `exactNodeCorrectness' itself must have the displayed
  minimum equation as its type and must mention the separately projected optima
  $m_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $m_L(U)$ and $m_R(U)$. A field whose only exact-search
  theorem is `MinIPNodeScoreSetDecomposition U hU' is rejected because a union
  equality of score sets does not by itself construct the recursive output,
  prove it is valid, or provide the optimum equation required by the reduction.

  The reconstruction functions are constrained by the oracle answers. The exact
  run at a node has projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{crossExactAnswer}(U,\operatorname{answers}) &:=
      \operatorname{answers}(\operatorname{crossInst}(U)),\\
    \operatorname{leftExactAnswer}(U,\operatorname{answers}) &:=
      \operatorname{reconstructExact}(U_L,\operatorname{answers}),\\
    \operatorname{rightExactAnswer}(U,\operatorname{answers}) &:=
      \operatorname{reconstructExact}(U_R,\operatorname{answers}),\\
    \operatorname{exactCandidateSet}(U,\operatorname{answers}) &:=
      \{\,\operatorname{crossExactAnswer},
          \operatorname{leftExactAnswer},
          \operatorname{rightExactAnswer}\,\}
      \text{ after omitting absent leaf candidates},\\
    \operatorname{reconstructExact\_eq\_argmin}:&
      \operatorname{reconstructExact}(U,\operatorname{answers})
      \in\arg\min_{o\in
        \operatorname{exactCandidateSet}(U,\operatorname{answers})}
        \operatorname{origScore}_U(o).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Thus `reconstructExact' is a function of the oracle-answer assignment and the
  recursive child reconstructions. A helper named `MinIPReconstructPair' may be
  used only if the audited witness proves
  \[
    \operatorname{MinIPReconstructPair}(U,\operatorname{answers})
    =
    \operatorname{reconstructExact}(U,\operatorname{answers})
  \]
  and the right-hand side satisfies `reconstructExact_eq_argmin' above. A
  definition that chooses `MinIPNodeGlobalPair U' by classical choice from the
  original instance, independent of the cross oracle answer and independent of
  the recursive left and right answers, bypasses the reduction and is rejected.

  The $\gamma$-approximation package has the same dependency requirement. The
  oracle-answer assumptions are only:
  a concrete $\gamma$-valid cross answer for each
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)$ and recursively produced $\gamma$-valid
  candidates for $U_L$ and $U_R$. They do not include the final reconstructed
  candidate or its approximation guarantee. In particular, a structure named
  `MinIPNodeGammaOracleAnswers' must have fields for
  `crossGammaAnswer', `crossGammaValid', `leftGammaAnswer',
  `leftGammaValid', `rightGammaAnswer', and `rightGammaValid' (with absent
  leaves handled by the no-candidate convention), but it must not contain a
  field named `reconstructedApprox', `reconstructedApproxValid',
  `bestApprox', or any proposition equivalent to
  \[
    \operatorname{origOpt}(U)\le
    \operatorname{origScore}_U
      (\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
    \le \gamma\,\operatorname{origOpt}(U).
  \]
  The projection `gammaApproxCorrectness' must prove that displayed
  two-sided inequality from the three candidate-validity fields, the candidate
  selection equation for `reconstructGamma', and
  `MinIPNodeExactDecomposition_correct'. A theorem such as
  `MinIPNodeGammaApprox_best' is accepted only if its hypotheses are exactly
  these oracle and recursive candidate-validity fields and its conclusion is
  the two-sided bound for
  $\operatorname{reconstructGamma}(U,\operatorname{answers})$. If it merely
  returns a stored field `reconstructedApprox' from
  `MinIPNodeGammaOracleAnswers', it assumes the conclusion and fails this node.

  Trial-12 failure-specific refinement: a witness with only per-node split and
  cross-call functions is incomplete. The audited
  $\operatorname{MinIPBichromaticRecursiveWitness}$ must contain a whole-tree
  algorithm layer whose projections are visible at this label:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{wholeCallTree}(V)&=\operatorname{callTree}(V),\\
    \operatorname{wholeCallSet}(V)&=
      \{\,\operatorname{crossInst}(U):
        U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V))\,\},\\
    \operatorname{wholeAnswerAssignment}_{\mathcal A}(V)&:
      \prod_{c\in\operatorname{wholeCallSet}(V)}
        \operatorname{AlgOut}_{\operatorname{BMinIP}}(c),\\
    \operatorname{wholeAnswersCorrect}_{\mathcal A}(V)&:
      \forall c\in\operatorname{wholeCallSet}(V),\
        \operatorname{AlgCorrect}_{\operatorname{BMinIP}}
          (c,\operatorname{wholeAnswerAssignment}_{\mathcal A}(V,c)).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The root exact run is not an arbitrary pair and is not a locally chosen
  `MinIPNodeGlobalPair'. It is definitionally
  \[
    \operatorname{exactRun}_{\mathcal A}(V)
    =
    \operatorname{reconstructExact}
      (V,\operatorname{wholeAnswerAssignment}_{\mathcal A}(V)),
  \]
  and the root correctness field has the concrete type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactRunCorrect}_{\mathcal A}(V):\\
    \qquad
    \operatorname{MinIPValidOut}
      \left(V,\operatorname{exactRun}_{\mathcal A}(V)\right)
    \ \wedge\
    \operatorname{origScore}_V
      \left(\operatorname{exactRun}_{\mathcal A}(V)\right)
      =
      \operatorname{origOpt}(V).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Its proof must invoke Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}, the
  validity of every answer in `wholeAnswerAssignment', and the
  `reconstructExact_eq_argmin' projection. A field whose proof only unfolds
  `MinIPNodeExactDecomposition' to the definition of
  `MinIPNodeReconstructedValue' as
  $\min(m_{\mathrm{cross}},\min(m_L,m_R))$ is rejected, because it never
  connects the reconstructed root pair to the minimum over original distinct
  pairs.

  The gamma algorithm layer is likewise whole-tree. Its run is
  \[
    \operatorname{gammaRun}_{\mathcal A}(V)
    =
    \operatorname{reconstructGamma}
      (V,\operatorname{wholeGammaAnswerAssignment}_{\mathcal A}(V)),
  \]
  where the answer assignment contains only concrete $\gamma$-valid oracle
  answers for all cross calls and recursive child candidates obtained by the
  same reconstruction. The required correctness theorem is
  \[
    \operatorname{origOpt}(V)\le
    \operatorname{origScore}_V(\operatorname{gammaRun}_{\mathcal A}(V))
    \ \wedge\
    \operatorname{origScore}_V(\operatorname{gammaRun}_{\mathcal A}(V))
      \le \gamma\,\operatorname{origOpt}(V).
  \]
  This theorem may not have type
  `MinIPNodeGammaApproxPredicate ... -> MinIPNodeGammaApproxPredicate ...',
  may not assume validity of the final reconstructed candidate, and may not
  conclude one of its hypotheses verbatim. It must derive the displayed
  root-level inequalities from all cross-call oracle validities, recursive
  child validities, candidate selection, and
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}.

  The threshold algorithm layer must also use the original root predicate. It
  defines
  \[
    \operatorname{thresholdRun}_{\mathcal A}(V,t)=\mathrm{true}
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \exists U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V)),\
      \operatorname{crossThresholdOracleRun}_{\mathcal A}(U,t)=\mathrm{true},
  \]
  where the oracle run is on the concrete call
  $\operatorname{crossInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R)$. Its correctness field is
  \[
    \operatorname{thresholdRun}_{\mathcal A}(V,t)=\mathrm{true}
    \Longleftrightarrow
    \operatorname{origThresholdYes}(V,t),
  \]
  using the threshold consequence of
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}. A field proving
  `MinIPNodeThresholdRecursivePredicate U hU t' iff the same disjunction used
  to define that predicate is rejected, even if the field is named
  `thresholdDecisionCorrectness'; the accepted statement must mention
  $\operatorname{origThresholdYes}(V,t)$ at the root or
  $\operatorname{origThresholdYes}(U,t)$ at a specified node and must prove
  equivalence by classifying original pairs through the split tree.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{def:minip, def:bichromatic-minip, lem:minip-split-tree-pair-coverage}
  Given a $\MinIP_{n,\ell}$ instance $V = \{v_1, \ldots, v_n\}$, partition $V$
  into two halves $V_1, V_2$ of equal size and run $\mathcal A$ on the
  bichromatic instance $(V_1, V_2)$; this returns the minimal pair with one
  element in each half. Then recurse: split $V_1$ into two equal halves and find
  the minimal pair inside $V_1 \times V_1$, and likewise for $V_2$. The minimal
  pair of the whole instance lies either across the top-level split or inside one
  half, so it is found by some recursive call. The running time satisfies
  \[
    \operatorname{poly}(\ell)\cdot \sum_{i=1}^{\log n}
      \bigO\!\left(\left(\tfrac{n}{2^{i}}\right)^{2-\eps}\right)
    = \bigO\!\left(n^{2-\eps}\operatorname{poly}(\ell)\log n\right)
    \le \bigO\!\left(n^{2-\eps'}\operatorname{poly}(\ell)\right)
  \]
  for some $\eps'>0$ (the geometric sum is dominated by its first term). The same
  argument applies to $\gamma\text{-}\MinIP$ (the optimal pair still appears in
  some recursive call) and to $\MinIP_{n,\ell,t}$ (we examine all pairs across
  some call).
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Bichromatic Max-IP reduction, Lemma A.12]
  \label{lem:maxip-bichromatic-reduction}
  \uses{def:maxip, def:gamma-maxip, def:bichromatic-maxip, def:tsq-alg-exists}
  If $\TSQAlg{\text{bichromatic }(\gamma\text{-})\MaxIP_{n,\ell}}$ exists with
  polynomial factors in $\ell$, then
  $\TSQAlg{(\gamma\text{-})\MaxIP_{n,\ell}}$ exists with polynomial factors in
  $\ell$ (possibly with a different positive exponent).

  The declaration audited at this label must expose its own recursive
  halving witness package
  $\operatorname{MaxIPBichromaticRecursiveWitness}$. It may reuse the same
  split-tree combinator as Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}, but it
  must instantiate it with maxima through its own concrete fields, not by
  pointing to the Min-IP recurrence as an abstract field. At every node
  $U=U_L\cup U_R$ its correctness theorem is
  \[
    \max_{\substack{p,q\in U\\p\ne q}}\inner{p}{q}
    =
    \max\!\left(
      \max_{\substack{p\in U_L\\q\in U_R}}\inner{p}{q},
      \max_{\substack{p,q\in U_L\\p\ne q}}\inner{p}{q},
      \max_{\substack{p,q\in U_R\\p\ne q}}\inner{p}{q}
    \right),
  \]
  and the reconstruction procedure returns the candidate with largest inner
  product among the cross-call and recursive candidates. For approximate
  Max-IP, if every bichromatic call returns a score in
  $[\gamma^{-1}M_{\mathrm{cross}},M_{\mathrm{cross}}]$, the reconstructed
  candidate must be proved to have score at least $\gamma^{-1}$ times the
  global maximum. The runtime field is the same call-tree sum as in
  Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}, with
  $T_{\mathrm{biMax}}$ in place of $T_{\mathrm{biMin}}$, and it must prove
  preservation of a positive truly-subquadratic exponent.
  At each non-leaf node the witness must explicitly construct the target
  bichromatic Max-IP instance
  \[
    \operatorname{crossMaxInst}(U)
      :=(U_L,U_R):\operatorname{BMaxIPInst}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell)
  \]
  and its score
  $s_{\mathrm{cross},U}(p,q)=\inner{(U_L)_p}{(U_R)_q}$. Its call field is the
  singleton containing this concrete instance:
  \[
    \operatorname{callsAtNode}(U)
      =
      \{\,(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,\operatorname{crossMaxInst}(U))\,\}.
  \]
  This `callsAtNode' field is mandatory for Max-IP even if the implementation
  reuses a generic split-tree library. A witness with no concrete
  `crossMaxInst' projection and no singleton call containing that instance is
  rejected. A call list containing only a node identifier, only the original
  parameter $(n,\ell)$, or only an abstract `BMaxIP' family value is not this
  oracle call.
  The package must contain the named projection
  \[
    \operatorname{maxCallsAtNode\_eq\_singleton}(U):
    \operatorname{callsAtNode}(U)
      =
      \{\,(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell,
          \operatorname{crossMaxInst}(U))\,\}.
  \]
  Its conclusion must be this equality. It may not have type
  $\mathrm{True}$, $\mathrm{True}\wedge\operatorname{Nonempty}$, or a statement
  that merely says some call exists. The element of the singleton must be the
  concrete target instance
  $\operatorname{crossMaxInst}(U)=(U_L,U_R)$ with child sizes $|U_L|$ and
  $|U_R|$; an equality to a singleton containing the root instance $(V,V)$, the
  original parameter $(n,\ell)$, or an index into the call tree is rejected.
  The node also defines
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)&=
      \max_{p\in U_L,\ q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    M_L(U)&=\max_{p\ne q\in U_L}\inner{p}{q},\\
    M_R(U)&=\max_{p\ne q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    M_U&=\max_{p\ne q\in U}\inner{p}{q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The exact maximum-decomposition field is exactly
  \[
    M_U=\max(M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\max(M_L(U),M_R(U))).
  \]
  It is rejected if it reduces to
  $M_U=\max(M_U,\max(M_U,M_U))$, or to the same expression with
  `MaxIPOpt U' repeated. Here $M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$ must be the optimum of the concrete
  $\operatorname{crossMaxInst}(U)$, while $M_L(U)$ and $M_R(U)$ are the optima
  of the left and right recursive subinstances. The three names may not be
  implemented as aliases for a single expression `MaxIPOpt U'. The audited
  package must expose the equations
  \[
    M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)=
      \max_{p\in U_L,q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\quad
    M_L(U)=\max_{p\ne q\in U_L}\inner{p}{q},\quad
    M_R(U)=\max_{p\ne q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q}.
  \]
  The named correctness projection has the type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactMaxNodeCorrectness}(U):\\
    \qquad
    M_U=\max(M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),\max(M_L(U),M_R(U))).
  \end{array}
  \]
  This type must contain all four quantities $M_U$,
  $M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $M_L(U)$ and $M_R(U)$. It is not an existential
  proposition, not a proof that an optimum exists, not $\mathrm{True}$, and not
  an implication whose conclusion repeats its premise. In particular, a field
  named `exactMaxNodeCorrectness' with type
  $\exists o,\operatorname{ValidOut}_{\MaxIP}(U,o)$ does not prove the
  recurrence needed for the reduction.
  The exact reconstruction field forms the candidate set
  from the valid cross oracle answer and the two recursive answers,
  \[
    \operatorname{candidateSetMax}(U)
      =\{o_{\mathrm{cross}}(U),o_L(U),o_R(U)\},
  \]
  and selects an element attaining the largest score in that set:
  \[
    \operatorname{reconstructExactMax}(U,\operatorname{answers})
      \in \arg\max_{o\in\operatorname{candidateSetMax}(U)}s_U(o).
  \]
  The global correctness field must prove
  $s_V(\operatorname{reconstructExactMax}(V,\operatorname{answers}))=M_V$.
  A field of the form
  `ValidOut -> ValidOut', an identity implication, or a correctness theorem
  using only one repeated optimum is not accepted.

  For approximate Max-IP the witness must define the selected score
  $s^*_U=s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGammaMax}(U,\operatorname{answers}))$ and
  prove
  \[
    \gamma^{-1}M_U\le s^*_U\le M_U
  \]
  from the three separate bounds for the cross, left and right candidates. It
  may not reuse the exact reconstruction theorem as a placeholder for this
  interval proof.
  The approximate correctness projection therefore has the type
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{gammaMaxNodeCorrectness}(U,\operatorname{answers}):\\
    \qquad
    \gamma^{-1}M_U\le
      s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGammaMax}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
      \le M_U.
  \end{array}
  \]
  A field of type $\mathrm{True}$, an identity implication, or a theorem that
  exact maximizers are valid approximate outputs without mentioning
  $\operatorname{reconstructGammaMax}$ and the selected score is not this field.

  The witness must have named projections
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{callTree}:&
      \text{the finite split tree of subsets }U\subseteq V,\\
    \operatorname{reconstructExactMax}:&
      \text{selects the candidate with largest inner product},\\
    \operatorname{exactMaxNodeCorrectness}:&
      \text{the displayed maximum-decomposition equality for every node},\\
    \operatorname{exactMaxGlobalCorrectness}:&
      \operatorname{ValidOut}_{\MaxIP}(V,
        \operatorname{reconstructExactMax}(V,\operatorname{answers})),\\
    \operatorname{reconstructGammaMax}:&
      \text{selects the largest-score approximate candidate},\\
    \operatorname{gammaMaxNodeCorrectness}:&
      \gamma^{-1}M_U\le
      s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGammaMax})\le M_U,\\
    \operatorname{maxRuntimeSum}:&
      T_{\mathrm{monoMax}}(n,\ell)
      \le C n\ell+
      C\sum_{r=0}^{\lceil\log_2 n\rceil-1}
        2^r\,T_{\mathrm{biMax}}\!\left(
          \left\lceil n/2^{r+1}\right\rceil,\ell\right).
  \end{array}
  \]
  Fields named `exactNodeCorrectness', `gammaNodeCorrectness', or similar are
  acceptable only if their types are the maximum identities above. They may not
  be `True -> True' placeholders, and a proof object that only reuses a Min-IP
  recurrence without exposing the maximum reconstruction is not this lemma.
  Transfer implications alone do not satisfy this node.
  The package must also expose Max-IP-specific runtime projections, not merely
  reuse a generic implication:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{maxSplitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{biMax}},V) &: \R_{\ge0},\\
    \operatorname{maxSplitTreeRuntimeDef}:&
      \operatorname{maxSplitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{biMax}},V)
      =
      c_{\mathrm{split}}\,n\ell+
      c_{\mathrm{calls}}
      \sum_{U\in\operatorname{internalNodes}(\operatorname{callTree}(V))}
        T_{\mathrm{biMax}}(|U_L|,|U_R|,\ell)
      +c_{\mathrm{recon}}\,|\operatorname{callTree}(V)|\,\ell,\\
    \operatorname{maxRuntimeRecurrence}:&
      \operatorname{maxSplitTreeRuntime}(T_{\mathrm{biMax}},V)
      \le C n\ell+
      C\sum_{r=0}^{\lceil\log_2 n\rceil-1}
        2^r\,T_{\mathrm{biMax}}\!\left(
          \left\lceil n/2^{r+1}\right\rceil,
          \left\lfloor n/2^{r+1}\right\rfloor,
          \ell\right).
  \end{array}
  \]
  A field called `runtime' or `maxRuntimeSum' with the tautological conclusion
  $T_{\mathrm{biMax}}(n,\ell)+n\ell\le
  C(T_{\mathrm{biMax}}(n,\ell)+n\ell)$ is not this runtime recurrence. The
  correctness fields are similarly rejected if, after unfolding, they become
  $M_U=M_U$, $\operatorname{MaxIPOpt}(U)=\operatorname{MaxIPOpt}(U)$,
  $\operatorname{GammaMaxIPOpt}(U)=\operatorname{GammaMaxIPOpt}(U)$, or an
  implication whose premise and conclusion are the same validity predicate.
  The cross optimum of $\operatorname{crossMaxInst}(U)$ and the two recursive
  optima must all occur in the statement being audited.

  The following placeholder shapes are also explicitly rejected:
  \[
  \begin{array}{l}
    \operatorname{exactMaxNodeCorrectness}(X):
      \operatorname{MaxIPOpt}(X)=\operatorname{MaxIPOpt}(X),\\
    \operatorname{exactMaxGlobalCorrectness}(X):
      \operatorname{MaxIPValidOut}(X)=\operatorname{MaxIPValidOut}(X),\\
    \operatorname{gammaMaxNodeCorrectness}(X):
      \operatorname{GammaMaxIPOpt}(X)=\operatorname{GammaMaxIPOpt}(X),\\
    \operatorname{maxRuntimeRecurrence}(T_{\mathrm{biMax}},n,\ell):
      T_{\mathrm{biMax}}(n,\ell)+n\ell
      \le C\bigl(T_{\mathrm{biMax}}(n,\ell)+n\ell\bigr).
  \end{array}
  \]
  The accepted maximum-node correctness statements must contain the four
  separately projected quantities $M_U$, $M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)$, $M_L(U)$ and
  $M_R(U)$, and the accepted approximate statement must contain the selected
  score
  $s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGammaMax}(U,\operatorname{answers}))$ with the
  two inequalities $\gamma^{-1}M_U\le s^*_U\le M_U$. Runtime preservation must
  be a theorem about $\operatorname{maxSplitTreeRuntime}$ and the split-tree
  oracle-call sum, followed by an explicit exponent-preservation field producing
  some $\eps'>0$ from a target exponent $\eps>0$.

  Trial-8 alignment requirement: the Max-IP witness must expose the maximum
  decomposition as data with named projection equations, parallel to the Min-IP
  witness but with maxima:
  \[
  \begin{array}{ll}
    \operatorname{crossMaxOpt\_eq}(U):&
      M_{\mathrm{cross}}(U)=
      \max_{p\in U_L,q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{leftMaxOpt\_eq}(U):&
      M_L(U)=\max_{p\ne q\in U_L}\inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{rightMaxOpt\_eq}(U):&
      M_R(U)=\max_{p\ne q\in U_R}\inner{p}{q},\\
    \operatorname{nodeMaxOpt\_eq}(U):&
      M_U=\max_{p\ne q\in U}\inner{p}{q}.
  \end{array}
  \]
  The field `exactMaxGlobalCorrectness' has target
  \[
    \operatorname{MaxIPValidOut}
      (V,\operatorname{reconstructExactMax}(V,\operatorname{answers})),
  \]
  derived from the fact that the selected candidate's score equals $M_V$; it is
  not a proposition equality involving `MaxIPValidOut'. The field
  `gammaMaxNodeCorrectness' must mention the selected score
  \[
    s^*_U=s_U(\operatorname{reconstructGammaMax}(U,\operatorname{answers}))
  \]
  and have the exact conclusion
  $\gamma^{-1}M_U\le s^*_U\wedge s^*_U\le M_U$. It is rejected if the field
  type normalizes to `GammaMaxIPOpt X = GammaMaxIPOpt X', if it proves only
  that an exact maximizer would be a valid approximate output, or if the
  reconstructed approximate candidate does not occur in the type. The runtime
  theorem must use the named
  $\operatorname{maxSplitTreeRuntime}$ from `maxSplitTreeRuntimeDef' on the
  left-hand side; a self-bound on
  $T_{\mathrm{biMax}}(n,\ell)+n\ell$ is not runtime accounting for the
  constructed monochromatic algorithm.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
  \uses{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction, def:maxip, def:bichromatic-maxip}
  Identical to the proof of Lemma~\ref{lem:minip-bichromatic-reduction}: split
  the input recursively into halves and run the bichromatic Max-IP algorithm
  $\mathcal A$ on each pair of halves; the maximal pair appears in some recursive
  call, and the geometric sum of running times is dominated by the top term,
  giving $\bigO(n^{2-\eps'}\operatorname{poly}(\ell))$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Complement inner product identity]
  \label{lem:complement-inner}
  \uses{def:inner-prod, def:l2norm}
  For binary vectors $v,u\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$, write $\bar u\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}$ for
  the coordinatewise complement defined by $\bar u[h]=1-u[h]$. If
  $\norm{v}_1=r$, then
  \[
    \inner{v}{\bar u}=r-\inner{v}{u}.
  \]
  This is a concrete arithmetic identity, not an existence claim or a
  placeholder. The declaration audited at this label must state exactly this
  equality, with the complement given by $\bar u[h]=1-u[h]$ and the constant $r$
  fixed as the Hamming weight $\norm{v}_1$. A statement that merely introduces
